2001 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Montoya


No. 28017-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 299



February 25, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Montoya, 115 Wn. App. 1050, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 872 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Mason County. Docket No: 00-1-00426-5. Date filed: 10/25/2001.



DISPOSITION: Superior court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of six counts of communication with a minor for immoral purposes, contrary to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090, in the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington). Defendant appealed, asserting the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions.


OVERVIEW: The jury heard consistent testimony that defendant suggested the following dares: (1) for a 12-year-old boy to walk next door and sexually proposition a neighbor; (2) for a boy to touch a girl's breasts; and (3) for 12-year-old girls to go outside and expose themselves. Moreover, the jury contemplated the children's testimony that defendant wrote sexually explicit language on the children's bodies and on the girls' bras. Defendant's contention that insufficient evidence existed to convict her of violating Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090, because the State did not prove she received commercial gain or personal sexual gratification from her actions, was not persuasive. "Personal gratification" was not included as an element of § 9.68A.090. Although defendant may not have specifically asked or forced the children to engage in the conduct, sufficient evidence existed in the record for any reasonable jury to be able to conclude that defendant participated in the sexually explicit activity. Thus, sufficient evidence existed in the record for the jury to reasonably conclude that defendant's participation was communication with children for immoral purposes, by words or conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

2002 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Eugster v. City of Spokane


No. 21473-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


115 Wn. App. 740; 63 P.3d 841; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 258



February 20, 2003, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city council member petitioned for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent city to appoint his law firm to represent him in a lawsuit filed against the council member and his wife by developers. The Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, denied the writ petition. The city council member petitioned for direct review by the Washington Supreme Court, which denied the petition and transferred the case to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: The city council member argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.041, because it did not say otherwise, required the city to hire him to defend himself and his wife. He contended that § 4.96.041 operated to: (1) guarantee him the right to retain counsel of his choice; and (2) require that the city either contract directly with his chosen counsel to conduct his defense or reimburse him for expenses he incurred by contracting with counsel himself. The city argued that § 4.96.041 did not give the council member the absolute right to represent himself. The instant court disagreed with the council member's contention that the city was required to hire him so that he could defend himself. The city charter prohibited any city officer from benefiting from a city contract. The council member was precluded from accepting an appointment, even if one were offered. The city charter did not conflict with § 4.96.041. The instant court rejected the council member's equal protection argument. The city had a legitimate interest in distinguishing between elected city officers and outside entities, in determining who could benefit from transactions with the city. The appeal was not technically moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the city council member's petition for writ of mandamus was affirmed.

 

2003 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jaspers


No. 47555-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 226



February 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Jaspers, 115 Wn. App. 1038, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 822 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 001027431. Judge signing: Hon. Richard A. Jones.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which ordered restitution after his conviction for driving under the influence of liquor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck a disabled vehicle in the rear. The disabled vehicle was partially blocking one lane of travel. Defendant struck the vehicle from behind, causing injuries to several persons on the scene. Defendant was charged with vehicular assault and driving under the influence of liquor. Defendant was found guilty on the driving under the influence charge, but the jury failed to reach a verdict on the other charge. At sentencing, defendant was ordered to pay restitution. Defendant then sought review. In affirming, the court determined that an award of restitution for misdemeanor offenses was permitted if there was a causal connection between the crime and the victim's damages. Substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding of causal connection. Moreover, the State was not collaterally estopped from litigating the "causal connection" issue at the restitution hearing because there was no verdict on the vehicular assault charge. Additionally, there were different burdens of proof required in the criminal case and the civil remedial proceeding. Finally, the court declined to hear defendant's issue concerning his right to a jury trial on the issue of restitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2004 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Mullin-Coston


No. 49713-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


115 Wn. App. 679; 64 P.3d 40; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 245



February 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by State v. Mullin-Coston, 150 Wn.2d 1001, 77 P.3d 650, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 674 (2003)
Affirmed by State v. Mullin-Coston, 152 Wn.2d 107, 95 P.3d 321, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 534 (Wash., July 15, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a jury verdict convicting him of premeditated first degree murder for his role in the strangling and stabbing death of a 15-year-old, contending, inter alia, that the doctrine of non-mutual collateral estoppel precluded the state from relitigating the codefendant's premeditation, in light of a different jury's conviction of his codefendant of the lesser degree offense of second degree intentional murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that by convicting his co-defendant of second degree intentional murder rather than premeditated first degree murder, the jury necessarily found that the co-defendant did not act with premeditated intent. Accordingly, appellant asserted that the State was barred in his trial from relitigating the issue of his co-defendant's premeditation. Appellant further argued that in failing to so instruct the jury, the trial court omitted an essential element of the offense, and that his attorney provided ineffective assistance by failing to argue this issue at trial. The court of appeals rejected these arguments and held that issues decided by the co-defendant's jury were not binding on the later trial of appellant. The court of appeals added that the trial court was not required to reference appellant's charged crime in its accomplice liability instruction and that it was sufficient to instruct the jury with language from the accomplice liability statute under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.08.020.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction on charges of premeditated first degree murder was affirmed.

 

2005 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Durrah v. Wright


No. 28410-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


115 Wn. App. 634; 63 P.3d 184; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 213



February 14, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Durrah v. Wright, 150 Wn.2d 1004, 77 P.3d 650, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 702 (Wash., Sept. 30, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, land possessors, appealed the judgment of the Wahkiakum County Superior Court (Washington) that entered judgment awarding them some, but not all, land that was the subject of an adverse possession suit.


OVERVIEW: The possessors argued that the trial court erred by denying them a jury trial because they were guaranteed a jury trial for their adverse possession claim under Wash. Const. art. I, § 21. The court of appeals disagreed. Section 21 guaranteed the right to a jury trial in an action for ejectment but not in an action to quiet title, and that right had not been expanded by statute. If the case was only an equitable action to quiet title, there was no right to a jury trial. The possessors titled their complaint, "complaint to quiet title." They alleged that they had been in possession for more than 10 years. They prayed that fee-simple title be established and quieted in them. Because they were in possession, they did not allege or seek ejectment. Necessarily then, their action was to quiet title, it was wholly equitable in nature, and art. I, § 21 did not guarantee the right to a jury trial. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2006 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Pinecrest Homeowners Ass'n v. Glen A. Cloninger & Assocs.


No. 20916-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


115 Wn. App. 611; 62 P.3d 938; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 203



February 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by Pinecrest Homeowners Ass'n v. Glen A. Cloninger & Assocs., 150 Wn.2d 1001, 77 P.3d 650, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 680 (2003)
Reversed by Pinecrest Homeowners Ass'n v. Glen A. Cloninger & Assocs., 151 Wn.2d 279, 87 P.3d 1176, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 282 (Wash., Apr. 15, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, homeowners, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, affirming appellee city council's reversal of the hearings examiner's denial of appellee landowner's application to rezone. On remand from the superior court, the hearing examiner approved the rezone in accordance with the city council's direction, and the homeowners elected not to supersede or enjoin the superior court judgment.


OVERVIEW: The landowner wanted to rezone the property to develop what was called mixed use, which included a close mix of retail, office, and residential uses. The city comprehensive plan would accommodate the mixed-use zoning, but the city had not yet enacted a zoning ordinance implementing the mixed-use designation. The superior court concluded, based on Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70B.040(1), that the city council had authority to authorize the rezone based upon the comprehensive plan. The appellate court ruled that the homeowners were not required to either enjoin or supersede an adverse zoning decision to proceed with the appeal. It was not necessary for the homeowners to appeal the hearing examiner's second decision, which complied with the city council's direction by order of the superior court. Furthermore, the appellate court ruled that the city council could not authorize a zone change based on the comprehensive plan, absent specific zoning regulations that were anticipated by the plan but never promulgated. A comprehensive plan, even when specifically addressing the concepts for the particular area, did not provide the necessary specific criteria for land use decisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

2007 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parent


No. 49748-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 188



February 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Kerry, 115 Wn. App. 1030, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 791 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 011028932. Date filed: 12/03/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Phillip Hubbard.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to trial court for entry of findings and conclusions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of taking a motor vehicle without permission. Specifically, defendant challenged the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A driver had just left the house of several persons with long criminal histories. After the driver made several turns, the officer pulled the vehicle over. The officer alleged that the driver failed to signal properly before the turns were made. Defendant was charged with taking a motor vehicle without permission. Defendant was convicted after his motion to suppress was denied. He then sought review. On review, the court determined that the driver did not testify that she signaled less than 100 feet before making the turns. However, because there was evidence to support a finding that the driver signaled less than 100 feet from the turns, the court remanded the case for additional findings of fact on the disputed issue. The trial court did not err in determining that the stop was not pretextual. There was no evidence that the officer witnessed any criminal activity before the stop was made. The fact that the officer knew of the criminal history of the driver's acquaintances was irrelevant, as the officer did not see the driver leave the residence. Therefore, under the totality of the circumstances, the officer had an objectively reasonable basis for the stop.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for the entry of proper findings and conclusions regarding its order denying suppression of the evidence.

 

2008 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Swagerty


No. 27361-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 175



February 7, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Swagerty, 115 Wn. App. 1026, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 587 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No: 96-1-00102-2. Date filed: 05/16/2001.
State v. Swagerty, 98 Wn. App. 452, 989 P.2d 1222, 1999 Wash. App. LEXIS 2105 (1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Clallam County, Washington, convicting him of first degree child rape, classifying him as a persistent offender, and sentencing him to life in prison without possibility of parole under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(4) (1996) (recodified Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505) of the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the information charging him with first degree child rape was constitutionally defective for failure to set forth the alleged victim's name. The appellate ruled that the information was sufficient, as under the plain terms of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073, the alleged victim's name was not a statutory element of first degree child rape. Defendant cited no common law authority for the proposition that the rape victim's name was an essential element. The appellate court also ruled that the lack of formal notice that defendant could be sentenced as a persistent offender if convicted did not deprive defendant of a fair trial or violate his due process rights because he received adequate notice of what was at stake, as the present appeal followed defendant's third trial. Furthermore, the POAA did not violate the Due Process Clause of the U.S. Constitution or the Washington Constitution, and the POAA did not violate the separation of powers doctrine of Wash. Const. art. IV, § 1 or Wash. Const. art. IV, § 6.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2009 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Parmelee


No. 47231-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


115 Wn. App. 273; 63 P.3d 800; 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 131



February 3, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion denied by In re Pers. Restraint of Parmelee, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 355 (Wash., Feb. 20, 2004)
Review denied by In re Pers. Restraint of Parmelee, 151 Wn.2d 1017, 92 P.3d 779, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 443 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: King.
State v. Parmelee, 108 Wn. App. 702, 32 P.3d 1029, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2270 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was twice sanctioned for insolence while he was incarcerated for stalking. In his personal restraint petition, he argued that the sanctions were based solely on the language he used in two written grievances that he filed and that such language in written grievances was protected from infringement by the First Amendment. The Superior Court for King County (Washington) denied the petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because the rule prohibiting insolence passed the Turner tests, jail authorities had not unreasonably sanctioned petitioner when he violated the rule by including scandalous, insolent, and abusive language in his written grievances. The appellate court held that it followed that neither the rule itself nor the imposition of the sanctions represented an "exaggerated response" to the legitimate penological concerns that the rule was intended to foster. As both hearing officers painstakingly explained to petitioner in their written decisions, he needed to understand that the grievance procedure was for the purpose of bringing issues to the attention of the jail authorities, not a forum to make disparaging, degrading, abusive comments about correctional staff. As both administrative appeal officers explained, petitioner was not being punished or sanctioned for using the grievance process. Rather, he was being held accountable for the degrading, abusive language he chose to use in the exercise of his right, despite his knowledge of the applicable rule prohibiting insolence. In addition to its insolence, his language constituted a true threat and was unprotected by the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

2010 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carlson


No. 27307-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 39



January 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 00-1-04306-8. Date filed: 03/30/2001.
State v. Carlson, 115 Wn. App. 1001, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 725 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with unlawful manufacturing of a controlled substance, unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, unlawful possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine, and driving while in suspended or revoked status in the third degree. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicted defendant as charged, and defendant appealed the three drug crime convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion by failing to reopen the suppression hearing to allow him to testify that his briefcase was locked. The appellate court ruled that there was no abuse of discretion by denying defendant's motion to reopen. Defendant offered no proof or argument establishing that, if he testified at the suppression hearing, it was likely that the trial court would have believed his testimony over the officer's. Also, defendant failed to make a showing of deficient performance sufficient to overcome the strong presumption of effective assistance. Although defense counsel claimed that her performance was deficient, there was no basis in the record to conclude that the decision to not call defendant was some sort of oversight, as opposed to a strategic or tactical move. Furthermore, defendant failed to show that the trial court abused its discretion by denying his motion for a continuance to allow private counsel to represent him, or that the statute under which he was convicted for possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine was unconstitutionally ambiguous or that he was entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2011 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Crisman v. Fire Prot. Dist. No. 21


No. 27830-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


115 Wn. App. 16; 60 P.3d 652; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3195



December 31, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, candidate and spouse, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, county fire protection district (district) and director, in the candidate's action alleging claims under Washington's Public Disclosure Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 42.17 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 of the federal Civil Rights Act.


OVERVIEW: The candidate ran for the county fire district commissioner against the incumbent. After he lost, the candidate sued respondents, claiming that the director coerced district employees to campaign for the incumbent. He alleged claims under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 42.17, the Washington Public Disclosure Act, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. He also alleged that the district was negligent in hiring the director. The trial court granted summary judgment for respondents and the candidate appealed. The court affirmed, stating that the incumbent had no private claim for damages under the Public Disclosure Act. Further, he failed to show that he was harmed by the district's hiring of the director. The director also did not violate the candidate's constitutional right to associate with his supporters and campaign for the office. Based on those foregoing reasons, the grant of summary judgment was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

In re Det. of W.R.G.


No. 27911-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3201



December 31, 2002, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re W.R.G., 114 Wn. App. 1079, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3526 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 98-6-00937-3. Date filed: 09/20/2001.
State v. W.R.G. (In re W.R.G.), 110 Wn. App. 318, 40 P.3d 1177, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 262 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Appeal was dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant detainee challenged the involuntary commitment order of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) which authorized his detainment by appellee hospital for an additional 180 days.


OVERVIEW: Two hospital doctors petitioned for the detainee's additional 180-day involuntary treatment, stating he presented a danger of serious injury to himself and others. In a supporting affidavit they stated he was convicted of first degree statutory rape and taking indecent liberties of his daughters. After his incarceration, he was detained under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.05. He asserted the evidence was speculative and insufficient to submit to the jury. The jury found he suffered from a mental disorder, presented a likelihood of serious harm to others, was gravely disabled, and his detention for 180 days was in his best interest and the interest of others. His appeal involved the fact-specific issue of whether the evidence in his commitment hearing supported giving a particular jury instruction, private in nature, as it depended on testimony elicited at trial. Thus, it did not involve matters of continuing and substantial public interest to overcome its mootness. Because the 180-day commitment order had expired, the appellate court could not afford detainee relief; his appeal was moot.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed as moot.

 

2013 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


No. 44463-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3160



December 23, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Parker, 114 Wn. App. 1070, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3490 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 96-1-07511-2. Date filed: 03/16/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Sharon Armstrong.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the King County Superior Court (Washington) of aggravated murder in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by admitting statements he made while in police custody because questioning continued after he requested counsel. The court of appeals disagreed. Assuming a violation occurred, any error was harmless. At trial, a detective testified that during the second conversation with defendant from 12:25 p.m. to 2:38 p.m., he said that his girlfriend got the television from her brother. He also said that he was with his girlfriend at the time of the second fire. When asked about one of the murders, defendant said that he did not do it. Those statements were primarily exculpatory. Moreover, the evidence of defendant's guilt was substantial and included DNA from both murder scenes, the property recovered from defendant, the testimony from a fellow jail inmate, and defendant's earlier statements. In light of all the evidence, there was no reasonable probability that the outcome of the trial would have been different but for the admission of those statements. Therefore, the trial court did not err by admitting the statements.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2014 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


No. 47115-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3162



December 23, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-05897-6. Date filed: 07/05/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Jay White.
State v. Jackson, 114 Wn. App. 1070, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3491 (2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Superior Court of King County (Washington), defendant was convicted of one count of third degree rape. Defendant had prior convictions for statutory second degree rape and first degree robbery. At sentencing on remand after appeal, the trial court imposed a life sentence under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030(32). Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that imposition of a life sentence under the POAA constituted cruel and unusual punishment under the U.S. Const. amend. VIII and was a disproportionate sentence under Wash. Const. art. I, § 14. The appellate court noted that all his crimes were against persons. He contended that his current crime of third degree rape, a Class C felony, was not the type of crime that the POAA intended to punish. The POAA defined the term "most serious offense" to include Class A felonies such as second degree statutory rape and first degree robbery as well as third degree rape, the crimes defendant committed. The POAA reflected the intent of the voters, as stated in the law itself. The appellate court held defendant's sentence was not disproportionate. He contended that the POAA was an ex post facto law and a bill of attainder, and that his due process rights were violated when the persistent offender allegation was not charged in the information, tried to the jury, nor proved beyond a reasonable doubt. These arguments had been previously rejected by the State Supreme Court. Contrary to his argument, the appellate court found defendant received all the process due him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's life sentence.

 

2015 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Rhoades v. City of Battle Ground


No. 27889-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


115 Wn. App. 752; 63 P.3d 142; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3031



December 13, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish February 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rhoades v. City of Battle Ground, 114 Wn. App. 1062, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3460 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pet owners owned one African serval, one caiman, and two cougars when appellee city passed Battle Ground, Wash., Municipal Code, 6.10.020 making exotic animal ownership unlawful. The city issued the owners a notice of violation, which the owners challenged. The municipal court found that the owners violated the ordinance, and the Clark County Superior Court (Washington) upheld the finding. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the pet owners argued, inter alia, that the ordinance violated equal protection, substantive due process, and was a taking without compensation. On the claim that the ordinance treated residents who kept exotic pets differently from those who kept dangerous dogs, the appellate court found that there was a legitimate interest in treating exotic animals and dangerous dogs differently. The city determined that exotic animals were more of a threat to the health and safety of its citizens, and that determination was sufficient on rational basis review to justify the disparate treatment between the classes of pet owners. On the substantive due process claim, the city had a legitimate interest in protecting its citizens from exotic animals, the ban on possession within the city limits served that purpose, and the city's purpose in preserving the safety of both residents and the animals themselves would likely not have been served by a less drastic ordinance. Finally, the owners could not establish that their animals would be taken at all, and that, if taken, they would be taken for public use, as opposed to under the city's police powers, the owners' takings claim failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2016 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sick


No. 26584-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3006



December 9, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 00-1-01222-9. Date filed: 10/24/2000.
State v. Sick, 114 Wn. App. 1053, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3423 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Thurston County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted him of residential burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged seven trial court errors: (1) improper admission of gun-related and poverty evidence; (2) prosecutorial misconduct during closing argument suggesting that he was more likely to have committed the burglary because he was homeless and living in the jail; (3) an unconstitutional inference-of-intent instruction; (4) insufficient evidence of specific intent; (5) ineffective assistance of counsel; (6) cumulative error; and (7) unjustified controlled substance sentencing conditions. The instant court found prejudicial, cumulative error. The State conceded that admission of a receipt and a manual for an automatic handgun was error. The prejudicial effect of this evidence outweighed any relevance it might have had to the burglary. The permissive inference instruction, taken together with other errors, could have erroneously relieved the State of its burden of proving the requisite intent for burglary. Although the evidence was sufficient to support a guilty verdict, because of the other cumulative errors, the instant court could not say with certainty that the jury would have convicted defendant if the errors had not been committed or if the trial court had cured them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

2017 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Everett Rec. Vehicle Park v. City of Everett


No. 49335-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3010



December 9, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 99-2-09101-7. Date filed: 08/06/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald L. Castleberry.
Everett Rec. Vehicle Park v. City of Everett, 114 Wn. App. 1058, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3444 (2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners filed a Land Use Petition Act petition and complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief in the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, against appellee city and alleged several constitutional violations by virtue of a land use regulation. The trial court granted the city summary judgment. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners purchased property intending to use the site as a recreational vehicle park. The city approved a special use permit with several conditions, including that stays on the property be limited to 48 hours. Thereafter, the landowners applied for a permit to expand their park and requesting to extend the 48-hour requirement to six to 12 months. The city refused to consider the application because the landowners had not complied with several conditions of the special use permit. The landowners unsuccessfully sought declaratory relief, arguing the land use regulation violated substantive due process, equal protection, and was a regulatory taking. The appellate court initially noted the landowners' lawsuit was an as-applied challenge to which declaratory relief was not appropriate. The appellate court held the regulation did not constitute a taking because it did not deprive the landowners of all reasonable economic use of the property. The appellate court further held the regulation was neither a violation of the landowners' substantive due process rights nor equal protection because legal nonconforming uses had a rational relationship to the ordinance's purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2018 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Biggs


No. 26980-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2996



December 6, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 00-1-00826-8. Date filed: 01/25/2001.
State v. Biggs, 114 Wn. App. 1053, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3425 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington), as charged by the State, of residential burglary. Defendant challenged his conviction and the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: A police officer approached defendant in a store because he was wearing a jacket that was reported to be stolen. Defendant accompanied the officer outside, where she asked if he had any weapons. Defendant said no and told the officer she could check if she wanted. During a pat-down, the officer felt what she thought was a marijuana pipe. Defendant told her that it was, and the officer arrested him for possession of drug paraphernalia. After his arrest, defendant admitted to the burglary. Later, he moved to suppress his statements and the items seized after his arrest, but the trial court denied the motion. Defendant was convicted, but the court reversed on appeal. The court first found that the officer had reasonable suspicion for an investigative stop, and defendant had consented to the pat-down search. However, defendant's possession of the pipe was not sufficient probable cause because the mere possession of drug paraphernalia was not a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.412(1). There was no evidence that defendant had used the drug paraphernalia in a proscribed manner. Thus, defendant's arrest was unlawful, and defendant's suppression motion should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision.

 

2019 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hampton


No. 26357-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


114 Wn. App. 486; 60 P.3d 95; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2964



November 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended December 23, 2002. Order Amending Opinion December 20, 2002.
Review denied by State v. Hampton, 149 Wn.2d 1023, 72 P.3d 762, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 517 (Wash., July 8, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which denied defendant's motion to suppress cocaine after he was charged with unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant reported that defendant was seen dealing cocaine and that he had numerous rocks of crack cocaine on his person. The police department then applied for and received a warrant to search defendant for controlled substances. Fifteen rocks were found between defendant's penis and scrotum, and defendant filed a motion to suppress the cocaine. The trial court denied the motion, and the court affirmed. The court stated that the warrant properly authorized a search of defendant's person, because the affidavit showed that, on 10 prior occasions, the confidential informant had seen defendant in possession of cocaine and that defendant had been seen dealing cocaine "out in the open." The court held that the warrant properly authorized a search of the area between defendant's penis and scrotum, stating that special safeguards were not needed when officers conducted a strip search pursuant to a warrant based on probable cause to search defendant's person for drugs. The warrant was properly executed, because the van had tinted windows, the officers did not engage in unnecessary or abusive touching, and the officers and defendant were all males.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress cocaine found on his person.

 

2020 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Citoli v. City of Seattle


No. 49188-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


115 Wn. App. 459; 61 P.3d 1165; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2958



November 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Reported in Table Case Format at: 114 Wn. App. 1047, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3341.Review denied at 149 Wn.2d 1033, 75 P.3d 968 (2003).
The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published January 21, 2003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owner sued defendants, the city, the mayor, the police chief, the electric company, and the gas company, seeking damages for his economic losses and emotional injuries arising from the termination of utilities to his business while protestors were in the building. The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted summary judgment in defendants' favor and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The underlying action arose as a result of a large, week-long protest where protestors barricaded themselves in the top two vacant floors of the three-story building where the owner's place of business was. The mayor proclaimed a state of emergency in the city and the police ordered the building's gas and electricity disconnected. The owner unsuccessfully attempted to conduct his business while the protestors were still in the building; the owner lost business, which was eventually shut down. On review, the owner contended summary judgment on all his claims was improper. The appellate court found that the takeover of the building by protestors was an emergency and that police had valid safety concerns and reasonably ordered that power to the building be shut down; thus, Seattle, Wash., Municipal Code § 21.49.110(U), absolved the electric company from both contractual and tort liability for interruptions of electrical service due to circumstances beyond its control. The gas company's failure to give notice to the owner as required by it own tariff rules did not make it liable for losses or damages arising from the force majeure, and did not entitle the owner to damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

TRAPP v. JACKELS


No. 49490-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2905



November 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 114 Wn. App. 1040, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3314.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 002064126. Date filed: 10/01/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Larry E. McKeeman.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) that quieted title in a piece of property to defendant in which plaintiff claimed an interest.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was given an interest in the property by his grandmother which was not recorded. Later, plaintiff's father was given full title to the property by plaintiff's grandmother. Defendant became interested in buying the property and asked various members of plaintiff's family (plaintiff was in prison) about who owned the property. Defendant was given conflicting information by different people. Plaintiff argued that the trial court erred by granting defendant's motion for summary judgment because defendant was not a bona fide purchaser of the property. The court of appeals agreed. There was clear evidence in the record that defendant received actual notice of plaintiff's unrecorded claim to the property, and sufficient constructive notice to indicate that there might have been some truth to the claim, despite the denials of plaintiff's father. Defendant was placed on inquiry notice and upon inquiry, learned that plaintiff's family could not agree among themselves whether plaintiff had an unrecorded ownership interest or not. Therefore, the trial court erred by granting defendant's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

State v. Stinebaugh


No. 20477-4-III CONSOLIDATED WITH 20478-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2869



November 14, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 114 Wn. App. 1037, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3304.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 00-1-00641-5, 00-1-00636-9. Judge signing: CAROLYN BROWN. Date filed: August 24, 2001.
State v. Stinebaugh, 114 Wn. App. 1037, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3304 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the judgment of the Superior County Court, Washington, convicting each of them of possession of controlled substances, Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(a) and (d), and possession of ephedrine or pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine, former Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.440 (2000).


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendants stemmed from an executed search warrant on their residence. Defendants challenged the sufficiency of the evidence supporting the possession with intent to manufacture charges. Female defendant argued the trial court impermissibly commented on the evidence, and male defendant argued the charging document for possession of methamphetamine contained an incorrect date for the alleged offense. The appellate court ruled that, considering the totality of the evidence, any rational juror could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendants possessed the pseudoephedrine tablets in the Mason jar, which was found in a drawer of their bed, with the intent to manufacture or to assist the manufacture of methamphetamine. Also, a propane tank found in the shed held ammonia, and the officers found other components of the anhydrous ammonia method of producing methamphetamine. Furthermore, nothing in the trial court's statement revealed its attitude toward the merits of the case or the witness's testimony, and, by changing the charging date, the trial court did not alter the essential elements of the charge against the male defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

State v. Lewis


No. 49369-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2854



November 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 001096743. Date filed: 10/15/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Helen Halpert.
State v. Lewis, 114 Wn. App. 1033, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3388 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the King County Superior Court (Washington) of residential burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was denied a fair trial, because the trial judge improperly commented on the evidence when, during jury selection, she mistakenly read the charging information from defendant's prior residential burglary case. The court of appeals disagreed. Immediately after the mistaken reading, there was an off the record bench conference between counsel and the trial court. Thereafter, the judge immediately acknowledged the mistake and so informed the jury. There was no record of any request by defendant's counsel for a mistrial or a special corrective instruction to the jury. In addition, there was substantial evidence against defendant. Defendant was observed by the victim's landlord attempting to push or pull something out of the victim's front door. When the police arrived, defendant fled. At the point where defendant jumped a fence and fled, a police officer found stacks of electronics and other boxes on the ground. Therefore, defendant was not denied a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2024 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gray


No. 27359-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2657



November 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 96-1-00791-6. Date filed: 04/17/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Stephen M. Warning.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to burglary and bail jumping. Defendant had several previous convictions and an offender score of 16 without counting his current convictions. Defendant moved for a drug offender sentencing alternative (DOSA) sentence. The Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington) found that his motion was untimely under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8 and Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the trial court's denial of his motion to modify his 1998 sentence. The appellate court held that the change in the law upon which defendant relied was the legislature's 1999 amendment to the DOSA statute, former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(6)(a) (1996), re-codified as Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505(2)(a)(viii)). All three divisions of the court of appeals had held that that amendment was not retroactive. Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100(6) did not apply, and defendant's motion to reopen his sentence was not timely as it had been filed over one year from the date of his conviction and sentencing. Even if defendant's motion had been timely, his right to equal protection had not been violated. A statute violated the equal protection clause only if the legislature had no rational basis for creating the classifications it used. Defendant had to have shown beyond a reasonable doubt that the legislature had no rational basis for applying the 1999 DOSA amendment prospectively but not retroactively, so as to distinguish between: (1) a class of pre-amendment offenders; and (2) a class of post-amendment offenders, which defendant failed to do.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2025 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Berst v. Snohomish County


No. 49545-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


114 Wn. App. 245; 57 P.3d 273; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2633



November 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

As corrected by 119 Wn. App. errata.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by, On reconsideration by Berst v. Snohomish County, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 471 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 19, 2003)
Review denied by Berst v. Snohomish County, 150 Wn.2d 1015, 79 P.3d 445, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 798 (Wash., Nov. 4, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiff property owners against defendant county in which the owners challenged the imposition of a building moratorium, the Snohomish County Superior Court, Washington, denied the owners' motion for summary judgment and granted the county's motion to dismiss. The owners appealed the orders.


OVERVIEW: The owners applied for a permit for a larger mobile home to replace the single home they had on their property. The county administratively waived the moratorium for the limited purpose of replacing the mobile home with another mobile home of the same size and in the same location. The dispositive issue in this case was whether the imposition of the moratorium was a "land use decision" triggering the Washington Land Use Petition Act (LUPA). The owners argued that the trial court erred in dismissing their claims for failure to bring timely claims under LUPA. According to the owners, the county's decision to impose the moratorium under the Washington Forest Practices Act was not a land use decision. The instant court agreed with the owners. Because the imposition of the moratorium was not a land use decision, LUPA was not a bar to the owners' declaratory judgment action. Regarding the owners' contention that the moratorium violated their right to procedural due process, there was a risk of erroneous deprivation of the owners' property interest because of the procedures used. The trial court also erred in dismissing the owners' claim of inverse condemnation.


OUTCOME: The instant court reversed the trial court's orders and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the instant court's opinion.

State v. Flores


No. 27169-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


114 Wn. App. 218; 56 P.3d 622; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2616



November 1, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by, Motion granted by State v. Flores, 148 Wn.2d 1025, 67 P.3d 1096, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 261 (Wash., Apr. 1, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, convicting him a second time of first degree child molestation, and sentencing him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole as required by former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(4) (2000) (recodified in Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505) of Washington's Persistent Offender Accountability Act.


OVERVIEW: Sometime after Christmas, the victim's mother learned that her live-in boyfriend, defendant, had earlier been convicted of a sex crime against children. After questioning her eight-year-old daughter, the victim, the mother suspected that defendant had abused her. At trial, the victim testified that defendant had inappropriately touched her. Defendant argued that this sentence was cruel and unusual punishment, and violated his equal protection rights. Defendant also claimed that his counsel was ineffective for failing to interview important witnesses and failing to discredit the victim's story. The appellate court ruled that it found no reversible error. Defendant's sentence was not grossly disproportionate to his crime, as he was a convicted child molester who had molested a child on at least two separate occasions. The legislature was justified in punishing repeat child sex offenders more severely than other repeat offenders, and defendant's sentence fulfilled the legislature's intended purpose and did not violate Washington's prohibition of cruel punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Reed (In re Personal Restraint of Reed)


No. 26346-7-II, No. 27834-1-II (consolidated) Respondent,

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, convicting him of three counts of second degree assault.


OVERVIEW: The jury convicted defendant of three counts of second degree assault and acquitted him of the domestic violence assault. The jury also found that he was armed with a firearm. The trial court imposed concurrent 15-month sentences for each assault count and 36-month consecutive sentences for the three firearm enhancements. The appellate court granted his appeal. He also filed a consolidated personal restraint petition. On review, the appellate court found no reversible error. While defendant claimed the trial court should not have admitted his blood alcohol report without an adequate foundation, defense counsel made only a general objection and failed to preserve this issue for review. Upon testimony of State's witness commenting on defendant's exercise of his Fifth Amendment right not to give evidence against himself, counsel was not ineffective for failure to call for a curative instruction; this was a reasonable decision based on legitimate trial strategy to avoid confusing the jury.

Hunt v. Horne (In re J.M.)


No. 48319-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2588



October 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 96-3-08290-6. Date filed: 03/16/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Kathleen J. Learned. Case Also Reported at: 114 Wn. App. 1013, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3259.
Hunt v. Horne (In re J.M.), 114 Wn. App. 1013, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3259 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed several motions to vacate a default child custody decree awarding custody to respondents, the mother's mother and stepfather. The King County Superior Court, Washington, denied the mother's motions to vacate and awarded attorney fees to respondents. The mother appealed the orders. Respondents cross-appealed the denial of attorney fees when the mother initially filed her motions to vacate.


OVERVIEW: The mother claimed that respondents' relief petition envisioned that the child would be returned to her under certain circumstances. However, the mother argued that the custody decree made no provision for the child to return to her and severely limited her visitation rights. The instant court determined that the default order and decree and all subsequent orders were not void. The relief provided did not exceed the request in respondents' petition. Regarding the mother's contention that the third party child custody statute, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.10, violated her due process because it did not require the appointment of counsel at the State's expense for the mother, the instant court concluded that the statute provided due process to all parents, even though it did not require appointment of counsel for indigent parents. The statute also did not violate equal protection. Because the trial court ruled on the issue of paternity without notice to the child or the opportunity for the child's best interests to be represented by a guardian ad litem, it violated the child's due process rights. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying, then granting, attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and vacated in part. The portion of the decree dealing with paternity was void.

State v. Simmons


No. 19977-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2552



October 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: LINCOLN. Judge signing: PHILIP BORST. Date filed: January 23, 2001. Case Also Reported at: 114 Wn. App. 1009, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3245.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lincoln County Superior Court (Washington) denied defendant's motion to dismiss and entered a final judgment of conviction, after it found defendant guilty of telephone harassment in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230(1)(a) in a case involving telephone calls defendant made to his ex-wife. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's ex-wife received several phone calls from defendant. The calls were loud, and defendant was ranting and raving. He used offensive and obscene language. He was charged with violating the telephone harassment statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230(1)(a). He contended the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad. The trial court denied his motion to dismiss the charge. The State submitted evidence that he previously pled guilty to a harassment crime. The trial court then found that he made the calls using indecent or obscene words or language, that he made those calls with the intent to harass, intimidate, torment, or embarrass her, and that he had previously been convicted of a harassment crime. After defendant was convicted, the appellate court found that the evidence sufficiently supported the conviction. It also found the statute regulated conduct implicating speech, not speech itself, and was not overbroad, as its intent requirement prevented speech protected under the First Amendment from being chilled. Finally, it found the language in the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, as the definitions of the inappropriate conduct were clear.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. M. K.


No. 49084-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2540



October 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 018014384. Date filed: 08/22/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Nicole Mac Innes. Case Also Reported at: 114 Wn. App. 1006, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3234.
State v. M.K., 114 Wn. App. 1006, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3234 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Juvenile defendant was found guilty in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) of felony harassment, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020(1). He told a classmate he was going to bring a gun to school and shoot everyone. Defendant claimed he was only joking. The principle argument on appeal was that the evidence and findings were insufficient to support the trial court's conclusion that his statement amounted to a "true threat."


OVERVIEW: Defendant also challenged the felony harassment statute as unconstitutionally overbroad. The appellate court held that the evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that the threat was a "true threat." Given the circumstances in which the threat was made, it was reasonable to conclude that defendant's threat would be interpreted by his classmate as a serious threat to kill. The appellate court also held that, because the harassment statute prohibited only "true threats," which were constitutionally unprotected speech, the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad. The trial court found defendant knew that he communicated a threat and knew that the communication he imparted was a threat of intent to cause bodily injury. The trial court also found that his threat placed his classmate in reasonable fear that the threat would be carried out. Defendant's threat was made at school in an atmosphere of fear and concern following several highly publicized school shootings. In discussing the objective reasonableness of that fear, the trial court properly focused on the context of the statement and how a reasonable person foresaw that the statement would have been interpreted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Webb


No. 26816-7-II, Consolidated with 27856-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2520



October 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Mason County. Docket No: 97-1-00244-3. Date filed: 11/30/2000. Judge signing: Hon. James B. Sawyer II. Case Also Reported at: 114 Wn. App. 1002, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3218.
State v. Webb, 114 Wn. App. 1002, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3218 (2002)
State v. Webb, 102 Wn. App. 1045, 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2703 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of first degree rape and second degree assault. On appeal, the convictions were affirmed, but the case was remanded for resentencing. After resentencing, the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington) denied appellant's post-trial motion for a new trial. Appellant sought review of the resentencing proceeding and denial of his post-trial motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: After appellant's trial, the police department fired an investigative officer for dishonesty. Appellant claimed that his conviction resulted from an inherently unfair trial, because he never had the opportunity to challenge the officer for possible dishonesty, an issue he was not aware of at the time of trial. Appellant also claimed that the department of corrections (DOC) was improperly denying him earned early release time. The appellate court found that: (1) the DOC was not applying the former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(4), which had been declared unconstitutional, to deny appellant earned early release time, it was properly applying the reenacted Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(4), which had been transferred to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.505; and (2) the post-trial motion for a new trial was properly denied, because the evidence of the officer's dishonesty would not have materially affected the testimony of the witnesses' that the officer interviewed or the trial outcome.


OUTCOME: The district court's amended judgment and sentence were affirmed, and the district court's order was affirmed.

Pers. Restraint of Forbis


No. 48625-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


113 Wn. App. 822; 57 P.3d 630; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2465



October 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Denying Motion for Reconsideration November 15, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2877.
Reconsideration denied by In re Pers. Restraint of Forbis, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2877 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 18, 2002)
Reversed by, Petition dismissed by In re Forbis, 150 Wn.2d 91, 74 P.3d 1189, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 560 (Wash., Aug. 21, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a personal restraint petition, challenging the application of a policy of the Washington Department of Corrections requiring inmates to participate in stress/anger management classes if they wanted to continue earning early release and other credits.


OVERVIEW: When petitioner was sentenced to prison in 1988, he was eligible to earn early release time, good conduct time, and dayroom privileges without having to participate in stress/anger management classes. The department later adopted a policy requiring inmates to participate in these classes if they wanted to continue earning early release and other credits. After petitioner refused to participate in the classes, the department imposed sanctions, including a loss of earned early release credits. The instant court held that the department's application of the policy to petitioner violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws. When the department applied the policy to petitioner, it increased the punishment for petitioner's offense by imposing retrospective punitive sanctions. The policy affected petitioner's substantive right to earn early release credits. The regulation was adopted after petitioner's conviction and required him to satisfy additional conditions to receive the same sentence for that offense. Petitioner's opportunity to earn early release credits changed because he had to satisfy an extra condition to earn the same credits.


OUTCOME: The instant court granted petitioner's personal restraint petition, prohibited the department from applying the policy requiring inmates to participate in stress/anger management classes to petitioner, reversed the sanctions imposed for petitioner's refusal to participate in the classes, and directed the department to reinstate petitioner's earned early release time.

 

2033 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Shaffer


No. 48372-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


113 Wn. App. 812; 55 P.3d 668; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2472



October 14, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted defendant's motion to vacate a 24 month sentence enhancement after defendant was charged with vehicular homicide. The State appealed and defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued the trial court improperly vacated on due process grounds defendant's two year sentence enhancement. The appellate court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(v) prescribed that the enhancement did not apply to all reckless driving convictions, only those that resulted from a charge that was originally filed as a violation of DUI. The effect of the statute was to elevate a prior reckless driving conviction to a DUI conviction without any proof. Because the statute did not require any proof of the charge of DUI, it failed to set the minimum constitutional standard required for criminal conviction. Because an unproven charge of DUI triggered, in part, a mandatory two years of incarceration as an enhancement violated due process, the statute was unconstitutional. Defendant's reckless driving conviction alone would not trigger the two year sentence enhancement. A sentencing enhancement could not be based on a mere charge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. E.J.Y.


No. 48674-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


113 Wn. App. 940; 55 P.3d 673; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2473



October 14, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The King County Superior Court, Washington, adjudicated defendant, a juvenile, guilty of felony harassment, based on threatening statements he made to school officials. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) the criminal harassment statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020, violated both the First Amendment and Wash. Const. art. I, § 5, because it proscribed protected speech; (2) he was denied a fair trial when he was held in restraints throughout his fact finding hearing; (3) the trial court did not address the issue of defendant's subjective intent; and (4) the State failed to prove that defendant's words or conduct placed school officials in reasonable fear. The instant court evaluated defendant's claims of overbreadth by applying federal constitutional law. It concluded that the criminal harassment statute was not overbroad under the First Amendment because the statute proscribed only true threats, which were constitutionally unprotected. The statute also was not void for vagueness. Because defendant had a bench trial, there was no risk of juror prejudice from viewing the restraints. Even though the record did not contain the required factual showing to support the use of restraints, the error was harmless. The evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to conclude that the school officials were subjectively afraid.


OUTCOME: The adjudication of guilt was affirmed.

State v. Roth


No. 27522-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2458



October 10, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Jefferson County. Docket No: 001000923. Date filed: 07/02/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Thomas J. Majhan.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Jefferson County, Washington, convicting her of multiple drug-related offenses, claiming error in denying her motion to suppress evidence seized from her person incident to her arrest for obstructing justice.


OVERVIEW: The arresting officer testified that he and several other officers responded to a domestic violence call and observed defendant walking away from the house where the fight was reported to have occurred. The officer stopped defendant and told her "she was not free to leave," and asked for identification. When defendant opened her purse to retrieve her identification, the officer observed a ceramic pipe. According to the officer, when he asked defendant about the pipe, she "turned and tried to turn from me," at which time the officer arrested defendant for obstructing justice, searched her incident to the arrest, and discovered the challenged drug evidence. The appellate court ruled that the officer conducted a proper Terry stop and did not exceed the scope of the stop by asking defendant for identification, however, the evidence did not support defendant's arrest for obstructing justice. The appellate court could not say that the evidence was sufficient to persuade a rational, fair-minded person that defendant was attempting to flee, and, without evidence of an attempt to flee, the officer lacked probable cause to arrest defendant for obstructing justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and dismissed.

Cascade Ambulance Serv. v. City of Bellingham


No. 47985-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2444



October 7, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 98-2-01139-1. Date filed: 01/05/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Michael F. Moynihan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ambulance service company sued defendant city, challenging an ordinance prohibiting private ambulance companies from responding to medical emergencies within the city limits. The Whatcom County Superior Court, Washington, dismissed on summary judgment all the company's claims, except its claim that the city violated its constitutional right of freedom to contract. The city appealed, and the company cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company asserted three causes of action against the city: (1) violation of the company's constitutionally protected right to freedom of contract, (2) violation of the company's right to equal protection of the laws, and (3) tortious interference with the company's business expectancy. The instant court concluded that the trial court erred in refusing to dismiss the company's claim that the city violated the company's constitutional right of freedom to contract. The company's existing contracts were not impaired by the enactment of the ordinance because the company was not incorporated until two years after the ordinance was enacted. The company's objective was the removal of impediments to new contracts. However, this was not an objective protected by the Contract Clauses of the United States and Washington Constitutions. Although the company contended that the city's refusal to train the company's paramedic amounted to an interference for a wrongful purpose, because the company apparently refused to agree to comply with the ordinance, the city's refusal to train the paramedic was essential to realizing the purpose of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the dismissal of the company's tortious interference claim, reversed the denial of summary judgment dismissing the company's right to contract claim, and remanded with directions to dismiss.

Marriage of Robertson


No. 27686-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


113 Wn. App. 711; 54 P.3d 708; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2402



September 27, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee former wife petitioned for modification of child support and a superior court commissioner granted modification. The wife moved under Wash. Rev. Code § 2.24.050 to revise the order's income provisions and transfer payment amount. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, denied appellant husband's motion to strike the revision motion as untimely and entered a revised child support order. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: Twelve days after the commissioner entered the modification of child support order, the wife moved under Wash. Rev. Code § 2.24.050 to revise the order. In denying the husband's motion to strike, the superior court found that the wife had an additional 10-days to seek reconsideration under Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 59(b) after the commissioner's order became a superior court order at the end of the 10-day revision period. The husband argued that under the plain language of Wash. Rev. Code § 2.24.050, when the deadline passed for moving for revision, an aggrieved party's only recourse was to seek appellate review. The appellate court ruled that Wash. Rev. Code § 2.24.050 clearly and unambiguously provided the wife 10-days from the date of the commissioner's order to move for revision. Once the 10-days passed, the wife's only recourse for review was with the court of appeals. Consequently, the superior court lacked statutory authority to consider the wife's revision motion as a motion for reconsideration.


OUTCOME: The superior court's order was reversed and the superior court commissioner's order was reinstated.

State v. Hepton


No. 20127-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


113 Wn. App. 673; 54 P.3d 233; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2399



September 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by State v. Hepton, 149 Wn.2d 1018, 72 P.3d 762, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 521 (Wash., July 8, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of methamphetamine manufacture in the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington). Defendant appealed, contending; (1) evidence obtained after a warrantless search of a garbage can area should have been excluded, (2) the evidence was insufficient, (3) a unanimity instruction was not given, (4) his statements to police were involuntary, and (5) statements regarding prior criminal acts were improperly admitted.


OVERVIEW: After a fire, investigators found evidence of what appeared to be methamphetamine manufacture. An investigator returned without a warrant, and discovered in a garbage can by an abandoned house next door, further evidence of methamphetamine manufacture. That evidence was used to obtain a search warrant for defendant's residence. The appellate court held: (1) defendant had no privacy interest in the neighbor's garbage can, the investigation did not constitute a search that violated Wash. Const. art. I, § 7; (2) although the substance found in defendant's residence was fully processed, a reasonable juror could conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of processing methamphetamine or its immediate precursor; (3) in light of the State's clear direction to the jury to rely only on the acts that took place on a single date, a unanimity instruction was not necessary; (4) substantial evidence supported the trial court's determination that defendant's statements to police were voluntary; and (5) the prejudicial effect of another tenant's testimony that she saw defendant cooking methamphetamine a few days before the fire did not outweigh its probative value.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

2039 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Wellington River v. King County


No. 47976-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


121 Wn. App. 224; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3545; 16 A.L.R.6th 875



September 23, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1] [Reporter's Note: The following opinion incorporates the Court of Appeals order amending opinion dated February 9, 2004 and supersedes the report of the opinion at 113 Wn. App. 574.]

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals February 9, 2004.]


PRIOR HISTORY: Wellington River Hollow, L.L.C. v. King County, 113 Wn. App. 574, 54 P.3d 213, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2396 (2002).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate developer (developer) sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondents, King County (county) and Northshore School District (school district), and held that impact fees assessed against the developer were proper.


OVERVIEW: The developer appealed $ 1,398 per unit school impact fees assessed by the County for the benefit of the school district, which was partially located in the County. The court affirmed the assessments, stating that jurisdictions within a school district were given the discretion to impose school impact fees on new developments. That discretion meant that the amount of fees for comparable units might be different from one jurisdiction to another. The developer failed to show that the discretionary treatment was unconstitutional. The developer also failed to demonstrate that its school impact fees were incorrectly calculated or that unusual circumstances rendered the fees unjust. The County's decision to impose school impact fees of $ 1,398 per unit on the developer complied with Wash. Rev. Code §§ 82.02.050(3), 82.02.060(1), and 82.02.090(8), and the County's ordinances. The fact that other jurisdictions within the school district used that discretion differently did not render the County's fees invalid. Further, because the developer acknowledged that Wash. Rev. Code ch. 82.02 taxes were not property taxes, its constitutional uniformity argument failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
