Wellington River v. King County


No. 47976-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


113 Wn. App. 574; 54 P.3d 213; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2396



September 23, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Reprinted as amended at Wellington River Hollow, LLC v. King County, 121 Wn. App. 224, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3545 (Wash. Ct. App., Sept. 23, 2002)
Review denied by, Motion granted by Wellington River Hollow, LLC v. King County, 149 Wn.2d 1014, 70 P.3d 965, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 386 (2003)
Modified by, Motion denied by Wellington River Hollow, LLC v. King County, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 217 (Wash. Ct. App., Feb. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Wellington River Hollow, LLC v. King County, 110 Wn. App. 1083, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1352 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate developer appealed a judgment of the King County Superior Court, Washington, reinstating a $ 1,398 per unit school impact fees assessed by respondent county for the benefit of a school district, which was located partially in the county. A deputy hearing examiner had reduced the fee from $ 1,398 per unit to $ 668 per unit.


OVERVIEW: The developer argued that the school impact fees were incorrectly calculated and that they were not identical to fees imposed by other jurisdictions within the school district. According to the developer, the $ 1,398 per unit school impact fees assessed to it did not comply with the county's school impact fees ordinance. The developer wanted its fees reduced to zero. The instant court determined that the developer failed to demonstrate that its school impact fees were incorrectly calculated or that unusual circumstances rendered the fees unjust. The method used by the district averaged the available data from each school district within the county which had actual data. This method satisfied the concept of county-wide average as that term was used in the ordinance. The statutes and ordinances at issue in the case gave jurisdictions within a school district the discretion to impose school impact fees on new developments. That discretion meant that the amount of fees for comparable units could be different from one jurisdiction to another. The developer failed to show this discretionary treatment was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The district was awarded attorney fees on appeal following its compliance with the Washington Rules of Appellate Procedure.

Wright v. B&L Props., Inc.


No. 49386-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE

September 16, 2002, Filed

Review denied by Wright v. B&L Props., 149 Wn.2d 1014, 69 P.3d 876, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 406 (2003)
Related proceeding at Mut. of Enumclaw Ins. Co. v. Brokaw, 120 Wn. App. 1010, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 720 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee homeowners garnered a default judgment against appellant contractor in the Snohomish County Superior Court, Washington, on their breach of contract, negligent misrepresentation, and breach of warranty of habitability claims. The contractor filed a motion to vacate the judgment, but the trial court denied him relief. The contractor appealed.

The homeowners sued the contractor and attempted personal service, but found his address for private and business affairs was a private mailbox service. Sudden Vly Cmty. v. Water Dist. No. 10


No. 49827-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


113 Wn. App. 922; 55 P.3d 653; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2258



September 16, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to Publish Opinion October 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Case Also Reported at: 113 Wn. App. 922, 55 P.3d 653, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2258.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent community association brought a declaratory judgment action challenging appellant water district's decision to increase the water rates for association lot owners in addition to lot owners in other geographical areas after defendant city increased its rates to improve a watershed. The district appealed from the Superior Court of Whatcom County's (Washington) order granting the community association's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: To preserve the water quality in a reservoir, the city increased its water rates so it could fund land acquisitions in the watershed. As a result, the water district expected to pay the city about $ 55,000 more per year to purchase water for residents in two of four geographical areas. The association argued, and the trial court agreed, that the water district's decision to pass along the bulk water rate increase to all of its customers, including those who did not receive the water purchased, was arbitrary and unreasonable. The appellate court noted that the operation of utilities was a "proprietary function," and the appellate court would uphold the water district's ratemaking decision unless it was arbitrary, capricious or unreasonable. The appellate court held the district's decision to impose a uniform surcharge to cover the increased cost of purchasing bulk water from the city was not unreasonable. Because all residents drawing their water from reservoir would benefit from the land acquisitions financed by the city's rate increase, the water district had a rational basis for concluding that all of its customers should share equally in the cost of the rate increase.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court granting the community association's motion for summary judgment was reversed.

Arborwood Idaho v. City of Kennewick


No. 20523-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


113 Wn. App. 875; 55 P.3d 1170; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2162



September 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Motions to Publish September 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Case Also Reported at: 113 Wn. App. 1032, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2796.
Arborwood Idaho, L.L.C. v. City of Kennewick, 113 Wn. App. 1032, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2796 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant apartment complex challenged respondent city's monthly assessment on each household, business, and industry served by the city's emergency and medical services pursuant to former Kennewick, Wa. Mun. Code 9.36.050 (1989). The Superior Court of Benton County, Washington, granted the city's summary judgment motion and held the assessment was valid. The apartment complex appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city established an emergency medical and ambulance service for the use, health, and welfare of city residents pursuant to former Kennewick, Wa. Mun. Code 9.36.050 (1989). The apartment complex challenged the city's collection of the ambulance charge from the apartment owners rather than directly from the tenants. The trial court held that the question to be decided was whether the ambulance charge was a regulatory fee or a tax. The appellate court held that the ambulance charge was not an absolute or unavoidable tax as mere ownership of the property was not the basis for the tax. Assuming an excise tax was imposed, this tax was based on the occupancy of the rental units rather than the ownership of those units. No ambulance charge was assessed on units that were empty. The appellate court held that the fee was a valid regulatory fee as it (1) related to a direct benefit or service to the taxpayers, (2) the money collected was used exclusively for the establishment and maintenance of the ambulance service, and (3) there was a direct relationship between the fee charged to the apartment complex and the number of occupied units.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed as the monthly assessment constituted a valid regulatory fee.

Malted Mousse, Inc. v. Steinmetz


No. 27170-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


113 Wn. App. 157; 52 P.3d 555; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1963



August 23, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Malted Mousse, Inc. v. Steinmetz, 149 Wn.2d 1001, 67 P.3d 1096, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 326 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Malted Mousse v. Steinmetz, 150 Wn.2d 518, 79 P.3d 1154, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 812 (Wash., Nov. 13, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant purchaser, who started to purchase espresso equipment and training from plaintiff seller, gave the seller a $ 5,000 deposit, but stopped payment on his check. The seller sued the purchaser. An arbitrator found for the purchaser but denied the purchaser's request for attorney fees. The purchaser appealed to the Pierce County Superior Court, Washington, which denied the fees as well. The purchaser then appealed to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: The arbitrator denied the purchaser's request for attorney fees because the arbitrator believed that Washington's small claims statutes were unconstitutional in that they denied litigants equal protection under the law. The purchaser argued that he was the prevailing party in the arbitration and that, under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.250, he was entitled to attorney fees. He further argued that the arbitrator's basis for denying attorney fees was an error on the face of the award and that the instant court and the superior court could correct such error. The instant court agreed with both arguments. The instant court concluded that the arbitrator created a manifest procedural error by sua sponte declaring the small claims attorney fees statute unconstitutional. The arbitrator's refusal to follow the applicable attorney fee statute deprived the purchaser of any adequate remedy other than an appeal to the superior court on the sole issue of the denial of attorney fees. The superior court should have treated the purchaser's request for a trial de novo as an extraordinary writ challenging the arbitrator's refusal to follow the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to the superior court with instructions that it remand to the arbitrator with directions to determine and award the purchaser reasonable attorney fees.

State v. Clark


No. 49321-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1928



August 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

 State v. Clark, 113 Wn. App. 1019, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2744 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicting him of second degree robbery and sentencing him to life in prison under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA).


OVERVIEW: Defendant walked into a bank wearing a disguise and handed a teller a note reading "no alarm, no dye pack." The teller handed over the money from her till, and defendant left the bank. Defendant was arrested shortly after the robbery. Defendant argued that his prior Oregon convictions should not count as criminal history, as they were constitutionally invalid. Defendant also argued that his life sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment, that the POAA violated due process, and that it was an unconstitutional bill of attainder and an ex post facto law. The appellate court ruled that defendant failed to show that the Oregon convictions were constitutionally invalid on their face and the trial court did not error in counting them as criminal history. The appellate court found no other constitutional error. Defendant's repetition of criminal conduct aggravated the guilt of the last conviction and justified a heavier penalty, and defendant's sentence was the same as that for any defendant convicted in Washington of second degree robbery with the same or similar criminal history.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fife Enters. v. Wash. State Patrol


No. 20571-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FIVE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1909



August 13, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: CHELAN. Docket No(s): 01-2-00131-5. Judge signing: JOHN BRIDGES. Date filed: September 20, 2001.

Case Also Reported at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2714.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged a decision of the Superior Court, Chelan County (Washington), which affirmed the revocation of the company's contracts of appointments issued by respondent Washington State Patrol (WSP). The WSP cross-appealed on the issue of preemption, challenging the superior court's decision that the Federal Aviation Administration Authorization Act, at 49 U.S.C.S. § 14501(c), preempted parts of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.55.063.


OVERVIEW: The company operated three separately licensed tow truck subsidiaries. The WSP appointed the company's subsidiaries to tow vehicles on WSP's behalf. Later, the WSP sent a single letter to the company notifying it that the WSP was going to revoke its contract with the subsidiaries. After a hearing was held, an administrative law judge affirmed the revocation. The superior court affirmed. On appeal, the court also affirmed. The company had argued that its procedural due process rights were violated because it was not afforded a pre-deprivation hearing prior to revocation. The court held that an existing appointment was a protected property interest, and that an evidentiary hearing should ordinarily be held prior to revocation. However, the court did not find substantial prejudice to the company because it was afforded an extensive post-termination evidentiary hearing, and because the evidence supported revocation of each subsidiary's appointment. The court held that the Act preempted Wash. Rev. Code § 46.55.063 as it pertained to consensual towing, but not as it applied to nonconsensual towing, as per 49 U.S.C.S. § 14501(c)(2)(C).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment that upheld the revocation of the company's contracts and that held that certain state statutory provisions were preempted by federal law.

City of Seattle v. Mighty Movers, Inc.


No. 49104-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


112 Wn. App. 904; 51 P.3d 152; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1842



August 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by City of Seattle v. Mighty Movers, Inc., 148 Wn.2d 1020, 66 P.3d 637, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 226 (2003)
Reversed by City of Seattle v. Mighty Movers, Inc., 152 Wn.2d 343, 96 P.3d 979, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 555 (Wash., Sept. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 99-2-20203-1.SEA. Date filed in Superior Court: November 17, 2000. Superior Court Judge Signing: Richard F. McDermott.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City of Seattle, Washington banned the posting of temporary signs on city owned structures, and in violation of the ordinance, appellant moving company posted numerous signs advertising its service on utility poles throughout the city. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) found as a matter of law that the utility poles and other city owned structures were not a public forum, and the company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company argued that the city's anti-posting ordinance violated the Washington Constitution. The central issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred in concluding as a matter of law that posting on city owned properties, including utility poles, was not a traditional public forum. The appellate court ruled that the portion of a publicly owned pole which was located on or adjacent to a street or sidewalk in the City of Seattle within the reach of pedestrians and which had traditionally been used for posting was a traditional public forum. Since none of the city's cited interests were justified by banning all posting on the portion of publicly owned poles, the ordinance was not narrowly tailored to serve a compelling government interest. The appellate court ruled that the anti-posting ordinance, Seattle, Wash., Municipal Code § 15.48.100, was facially overbroad in violation Wash. Const. art. I, § 5. The appellate court invalidated as unconstitutional the application of the ordinance to the pole portion of the traffic control devices, utility poles and lampposts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

2049 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. 27140-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


112 Wn. App. 787; 51 P.3d 143; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1831



August 2, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Thompson, 148 Wn.2d 1020, 66 P.3d 638, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 229 (2003)
Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Thompson, 151 Wn.2d 793, 92 P.3d 228, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 445 (Wash., June 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Pierce County. Superior Court Docket No. 00-1-02645-7. Date Filed In Superior Court: March 19, 2001. Superior Court Judge Signing: Bryan Chushcoff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pierce County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted defendant of unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence that the police obtained when they arrested him at his home. According to defendant, his outstanding arrest warrant for failure to appear at a contempt hearing, which arose out of a child support issue, did not support the use of a nonconsensual entry into his travel trailer. Defendant challenged both the arrest and the subsequent searches. The instant court concluded that the police did not unreasonably use the "knock and wait" statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.31.040, under the facts of the case. The officers had a duty to arrest defendant once they knew of the arrest warrant, and there was no evidence of bad faith by the officers. The instant court also concluded that the searches following defendant's arrest were valid. It upheld the search of defendant's trailer under the emergency exception to the warrant requirement. Regarding the search of a boathouse, defendant assumed the risk that his parents, who along with defendant had control over the boathouse, would consent to police entry into the boathouse without his consent, even though defendant was present at the time of the entry.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2050 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Ealy v. City of Seattle


No. 48182-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1800



July 29, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2879.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-2-16223-4. Date filed: 02/08/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Robert Alsdorf.
Ealy v. City of Seattle, 112 Wn. App. 1049, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2879 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sued appellee ambulance service, police officers, and city in the Superior Court of King County, Washington, for the wrongful death of her son and for civil rights violations. The trial court found the doctrine of sovereign immunity applied and denied the mother's claims. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother's son died after a confrontation with police officers and paramedics, who were attempting to restrain him while transporting him to the hospital, after he was found disoriented and intoxicated in public. The mother unsuccessfully sued for wrongful death and violations of her son's civil rights. The mother appealed, arguing the trial court incorrectly applied the doctrine of state common law immunity and erred when it denied her individual claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The mother further contended defense counsel's comments concerning an inadmissible coroner's inquest warranted a new trial. The appellate court initially noted the trial court properly applied the doctrine of sovereign immunity and instructed the jury appropriately, and, because the defense applied, her civil rights claims necessarily failed. The appellate court held defense counsel's improper remark constituted a waiver of the error, as it was not so flagrant and ill-intentioned such that it evinced an enduring and resulting prejudice that was not otherwise neutralized by an admonition to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2051 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Vancouver v. Bleakley


No. 25978-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1793



July 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Docket No: 99-1-00502-3. Date filed: 05/01/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Roger A. Bennett.

Case Also Reported at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2204.
City of Vancouver v. Bleakley, 112 Wn. App. 1046, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2204 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for dismissal of the charge without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of obstructing a public servant in the Clark County District Court (Washington). The superior court affirmed. Defendant appealed, arguing the charging document omitted language of the necessary mental state. Respondent city argued defendant did not preserve his argument because he did not note a hearing before the trial court to have his demand for a bill of particulars met and did not make such a motion at trial.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant driving and knew from previous contact that defendant's driving license was suspended. Defendant would not cooperate with the officer and resisted verbal requests of the officer before finally submitting to arrest. Pro se, defendant demanded a bill of particulars before trial. There was no indication in the record before the appellate court that the prosecuting attorney responded to this demand. The appellate court noted that if a defendant challenged the charging document at or before trial, it construed the document strictly as opposed to a liberal construction where the issue was raised for the first time on appeal. Defendant sufficiently challenged the charging document before trial and was entitled to have the appellate court construe the charging document strictly. The appellate court found the citation omitted "wilfully," the specific intent required for the offense. Because specific intent was an essential element of the crime of obstructing a public officer, the citation was unconstitutional. Thus, the charging document lacked an essential element even under the less stringent posttrial construction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for dismissal of the charge without prejudice.

 

2052 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


No. 26158-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1796



July 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Carter, 112 Wn. App. 1046, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2205 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Carter, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 662 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 19, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a trial court order suppressing as evidence a weapon taken from respondent arms instructor by two criminal investigators employed by a county prosecutor's office. The instructor was charged with one count of possessing a machine gun, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9.41.190(1), .010(7). He moved to suppress the weapon on grounds of illegal search and seizure under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.6.


OVERVIEW: The investigators attended a weapons instruction course, for personal and not professional reasons, at which the instructor was the primary instructor. The State contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in concluding that the investigators were state agents and that the exclusionary rule applied. The appellate court held that a review of the record disclosed facts indicating that the investigators functioned as state agents. Although they attended the weapons instructor course on their own time, they made known their occupation as criminal investigators. They also threatened the instructor with arrest if he did not turn over his weapon. When one of the investigators called 911 dispatch to request assistance, he identified himself as an investigator in the prosecutor's office. Upon his arrival, the deputy examined the firearm, consulted with his superior, and allowed the investigators to put it into the evidence room at the county. Substantial evidence supported the trial court's findings and conclusions that the investigators were agents of the state and that seizing the rifle was unconstitutional. The trial court did not err in suppressing the illegally seized weapon.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2053 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Tukwila v. Deja Vu Lynnwood


No. 48678-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1718



July 22, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-2-06900-9. Date filed: 05/30/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Robert Alsdorf.

Case Also Reported at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2197.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cabaret challenged the orders of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) excluding its evidence of lost profits as a sanction for discovery violations and dismissing its damage claim for a lack of evidence, in the underlying action with appellee City of Tukwila. The city cross-appealed from a judgment awarding the cabaret attorney fees it incurred to set aside an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The cabaret argued that there was no discovery violation warranting exclusion of its lost profits evidence and that it could prove its damage claim without expert testimony. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the cabaret's discovery violations were deliberate and substantially prejudiced the city's ability to prepare for trial. The appellate court ruled that the trial court's sanction was not manifestly unreasonable or exercised on untenable grounds. As the cabaret's only expert witness designated to testify to lost profits was properly excluded, and the cabaret's other evidence was not sufficient to support its damage claim, dismissal was proper. In the appellate court's view, the cabaret's assertion that two other witnesses were capable of calculating damages was specious at best, and the appellate court rejected the cabaret's assertion that its business records alone established its lost profits with reasonable certainty. Furthermore, the appellate court ruled that it had no basis on which to disagree with the trial court's award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The orders and judgment were affirmed.

 

2054 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Miguel v. Guess


No. 20699-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


112 Wn. App. 536; 51 P.3d 89; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1706; 89 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 990



July 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Miguel v. Guess, 148 Wn.2d 1019, 64 P.3d 650, 2003 Wn. LEXIS 171 (Wash., Mar. 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT Whitman County. Superior Court No: 96-2-00190-1. Date filed in Superior Court: July 6, 1999, July 25, 2000 and May 17, 2001. Superior Court Judge signing: Richard Miller.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sued respondent hospital and doctor after she was dismissed from her position at the hospital. The employee believed that she was fired because she was a lesbian. The employee contended that public employment discrimination based solely on sexual orientation was irrational and actionable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The Superior Court, Whitman County (Washington) dismissed her claims on summary judgment. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended the superior court erred when it dismissed her equal protection claims against both the hospital and the doctor, and her claim against the hospital that its actions violated Washington public policy. The appellate court held that the employee raised material issues of fact with respect to whether the hospital and the doctor were state actors for the purposes of § 1983, and they denied her equal protection under the laws. But the employee did not have a claim based upon public policy, as her discharge did not violate a clear mandate of Washington public policy. On appeal, the hospital emphasized breach of patient confidentiality as the justification for the employee's termination. But, at the time, much of the emphasis was upon her relationship with the doctor and her inability to work with him. The evidence and the inferences from it supported the findings that the doctor refused to work with the employee because she was a lesbian. Those findings supported a conclusion that the hospital adopted and ratified the conduct of its employees as its final policy with respect to the treatment of the employee that was based upon her sexual orientation.


OUTCOME: The dismissal by the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for trial of the § 1983 claims against the hospital and the doctor. The dismissal of the employee's claim based upon public policy was affirmed.

 

2055 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 48777-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1692



July 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 001092756. Date filed: 06/11/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Dale Ramerman.

Case Also Reported at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2177.
State v. Jones, 112 Wn. App. 1038, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2177 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second degree assault and the Superior Court of King County (Washington) used three prior convictions to calculate an offender score of four. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court miscalculated his offender score when the State failed to prove either the existence of the Washington conviction for cocaine possession or that the remaining two out-of-state convictions were comparable to Washington felonies. The appellate court found that defense counsel acknowledged the offender score used by the trial court, effectively treating each of those offenses as equivalent to separate felonies in Washington. Implicit in defense counsel's acknowledgment was the determination that each of defendant's three prior convictions should be counted. Since defendant, through his attorney, virtually conceded that he had an offender score of four, and because the trial court imposed a sentence consistent with that offender score, defendant waived the right to challenge the length and computation of the sentence imposed. Since defendant had not shown that the outcome would have been different had defense counsel not made the admissions and acknowledgments, defendant failed to established a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2056 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Van Blaricom v. Kronenberg


No. 47666-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


112 Wn. App. 501; 50 P.3d 266; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1686



July 15, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 99-2-03596-8 SEA. Docket No: 99-2-03596-8. Date filed in Superior Court: January 18, 2001/January 19, 2000. Superior Court Judge Signing: The Honorable Linda Lau. Date filed: 10/16/2000.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit brought by plaintiffs, husband and wife, against defendant attorney for violation of due process under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, abuse of process, defamation, invasion of privacy, false light, malicious prosecution, duress, and coercion, the King County Superior Court, Washington, dismissed most of the claims on summary judgment. Plaintiffs appealed the order granting summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The attorney, who represented a third party in a lawsuit against the husband, used Wash. Rev. Code § 6.25.070(2) to obtain prejudgment writs of attachment on plaintiffs' real property. Plaintiffs did not receive notice of the lawsuit or the writs until after the writs had been issued. Plaintiffs alleged that the attorney was liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because he knew or should have known that, absent exigent circumstances, writs of attachment without prior notice and an opportunity to be heard violated their due process rights. The attorney asserted that a release of the third party precluded any claim against him based on the prejudgment writs of attachment. The instant court held that the prejudgment attachment of real property without prior notice and a hearing violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment in the absence of exigent circumstances. However, a partial summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs was not appropriate. In addition to proving that their due process rights were violated, plaintiffs were required to demonstrate that the attorney knew or should have known Washington's ex parte prejudgment writ of attachment procedure was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The instant court reversed the trial court's order of summary judgment with respect to plaintiffs' § 1983 claim and the claim for abuse of process. The instant court affirmed the remainder of the summary judgment order.

 

2057 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Achen v. Clark County


No. 26886-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1523



July 2, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 98-2-01641-1. Date filed: 12/14/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Barbara D. Johnson.
Achen v. Clark County, 112 Wn. App. 1034, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2364 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part, remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developers appealed a judgment of the Clark County Superior Court, Washington, dismissing several of the developers' takings-related claims against defendant county. The county cross-appealed the trial court's dismissal of the developers' state law tort claims without prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The developers set forth nine causes of action: (1) violation of procedural due process; (2) violation of substantive due process; (3) violation of equal protection; (4) illegal spot zoning; (5) temporary taking; (6) negligence - breach of special relationship; (7) wrongful interference with business expectancy; (8) damages and attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988; and (9) inverse condemnation. The instant court noted that Washington case law supported the developers' position that substantive due process claims involving property rights were independent of the takings claims. Thus, the trial court erred by granting summary judgment on the developers' substantive due process claim to the extent that the substantive due process claim relied on arbitrary and capricious state action. The developers' substantive due process claim was ripe and formed the basis for the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. However, because the developers did not seek a variance, their takings claim was not ripe. The trial court did not err in dismissing the developers' state tort claims without prejudice. The developers' spot zoning claim sounded in substantive due process and equal protection, not tort.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part and affirmed in part, and the case was remanded for a new trial. The instant court reversed the dismissal of the developers' substantive due process claim. It affirmed the remainder of the holdings of the trial court with regard to both the appeal and the cross appeal, except for the developers' equal protection claim, which it remanded for the trial court's determination.

 

2058 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCarty


No. 24725-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1198



May 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 95-1-00813-9. Date filed: 04/26/1999 Judge signing: Hon. Gordon L. Godfrey.

Case Also Reported at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 2029.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Thurston County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted him of money laundering, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.83.020(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an attorney, borrowed money from his client, a known drug dealer. On appeal, defendant argued that § 9A.83.020(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because the statute did not adequately define the term "financial transaction" and did not provide ascertainable standards of guilt to protect against arbitrary enforcement. The instant court concluded that the statute was neither vague nor overbroad as applied to defendant's actions. Defendant failed to prove that an ordinary person would not be on notice that the money laundering statute prohibited borrowing the proceeds of illegal drug activity. When defendant borrowed the money from his drug dealing client, he engaged in what was clearly a financial transaction under both common understanding and the statutory definition of that term. Defendant knew that the money he borrowed was the proceeds of methamphetamine sales. As applied to these facts, defendant's vagueness argument failed. Defendant also failed to show that the statute was overbroad. Enforcement of the statute against defendant was not arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2059 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chisom


No. 47718-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 816



May 6, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 001040365. Date filed: 12/05/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Carol Schapira.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the King County Superior Court, Washington, of delivery of cocaine and a sentencing enhancement of committing the crime within 1,000 feet of a school bus route stop. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the amended information charging the sentencing enhancement was not filed until after conclusion of the trial; (2) the trial court erred in denying his request to appoint separate counsel because of an actual conflict between his interests and that of his attorney; and (3) Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435, the statute under which he was convicted, was unconstitutionally vague because a person of reasonable intelligence had no means of identifying the location of the school bus stop in the vicinity of the drug transaction. The instant court held that the trial court did not lose subject matter jurisdiction. The amended information complied with the requirements of Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 2.1(d). The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying substitution of counsel, as there was no indication in the record that defendant and his attorney had an actual conflict of interest. The instant court rejected defendant's contention that Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435 was unconstitutionally vague because the location of the bus stop was readily available in the school district's transportation office.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2060 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baldwin


No. 47865-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


111 Wn. App. 631; 45 P.3d 1093; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 782



May 6, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

As corrected by 119 Wn. App. errata.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Baldwin, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 4 (Wash. Jan. 8, 2003).
Review granted by State v. Baldwin, 148 Wn.2d 1001, 60 P.3d 1211, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 4 (2003)
Affirmed by State v. Baldwin, 150 Wn.2d 448, 78 P.3d 1005, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 738 (Wash., Nov. 6, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Snohomish, Washington, which convicted her of three counts of identity theft and two counts of forgery, and imposed an exceptional sentence premised on the crimes being major economic offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant used three different false identities with matching driver's licenses. She acquired title to four different vehicles using two of these names, bought auto insurance and homeowners insurance under the false names, possessed a social security card in one of the names, and had acquired two credit cards in one of the names. She also managed to buy a home under one of the names. An exceptional sentence was imposed because defendant utilized a complicated scheme to purchase a home and several automobiles with the stolen identities. The appellate court found that: (1) the trial court's evidentiary rulings were proper, (2) the evidence was sufficient for the jury to convict on all three counts of theft of identity, (3) the theft of identity and forgery counts did not constitute the same criminal conduct or violate double jeopardy because they involved three separate victims and the crimes were not the same in law or in fact, (4) the convictions of theft of identity and forgery did not merge because none of the crimes were crimes of degree or lesser included offenses, (5) the sentence imposed was not clearly excessive, and (6) the sentencing statutes were not vague or arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The superior court's judgment was affirmed.

 

2061 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tsoi


No. 47468-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 719



April 22, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-08734-4. Date filed: 09/27/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Nicole Mac Innes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his theft conviction for unlawful issuance of a bank check entered in the Superior Court of King County (Washington), asserting that the permissive inference instruction on intent to defraud was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress his bank account records. He also appealed the order granting his motion for a new trial on the theft of a firearm charge.


OVERVIEW: According to a wholesaler's records, defendant gave it 15 insufficient funds (NSF) checks in return for merchandise. The appellate court noted that permissive inference instructions were unconstitutional, unless it could at least be said with substantial assurance that the presumed fact was more likely than not to flow from the proved fact on which it was made to depend. In defendant's case, the presumed fact, intent to defraud, more likely than not flowed from the facts proven at trial. Accordingly, there was sufficient evidence supporting the trial court's decision to give the inference. Further, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the evidence seized in a warrantless search of defendant's bank account records, as a person who wrote or passed a bad check drawn on his or her bank account could not have any justifiable expectation that the status of the account at that time would remain private. Finally, the trial court properly granted defendant a new trial on the theft of a firearm because of an error in the "to convict" instruction, and the State could properly choose to retry him for the crime charged in the information.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court was affirmed.

State v. Carter


No. 26158-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 662



April 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.  RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn, Substituted opinion, Reconsideration denied: State v. Carter, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1796 (Wash. Ct. App. July 26, 2002).
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Reconsideration denied by State v. Carter, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1796 (Wash. Ct. App., July 26, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 99-1-01367-9. Date filed: 06/16/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Leonard W. Kruse.
State v. Carter, 111 Wn. App. 1015, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1592 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two criminal investigators employed by the county prosecutor's office took a weapon from defendant. The prosecutor's office charged defendant with one count of possessing a machine gun, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9.41.190(1), .010(7). The Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) granted defendant's motion to suppress the weapon on grounds of illegal search and seizure and dismissed the charges against him. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prosecutor's employees examined defendant's machine gun when they attended a weapons instructor course on their own time. They believed that the gun had been illegally modified. Defendant claimed that the prosecutor's employee's were acting as state agents at the time they opened his weapon to inspect the interior and later when they seized the weapon, and thus, their actions were tantamount to a warrantless search and seizure in violation of the Fourth Amendment and Wash. Const. Art. I, § 7. The appellate court held that the record disclosed that the two employees functioned as state agents. Inter alia, although they attended the course on their own time, they made known their occupation as criminal investigators for the county prosecutor's office. They also threatened defendant with arrest if he did not turn over his weapon. They admitted telling defendant that he had two choices, either turn the firearm over to them for testing or they would call the sheriff, who would probably arrest him. There was substantial evidence that supported the trial court's findings and conclusions that the employees were agents of the state and that the seizure was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2063 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Evergreen Freedom Found. v. Wash. Educ. Ass'n


No. 25272-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


111 Wn. App. 586; 49 P.3d 894; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 3408



April 19, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended by Order of the Appellate Court May 7 and June 14, 2002.
Review denied by State ex rel. Evergreen Freedom Found. v. Wash. Educ. Ass'n, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 178 (Wash., Mar. 7, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent union conducted a campaign opposing two statewide ballot initiatives. Appellant foundation sued the union, alleging that the union was a political committee under the Washington Public Disclosure Act and had not made the appropriate financial disclosures regarding its opposition. The Thurston County Superior Court (Washington) held that the union was not a political committee. The foundation appealed. The union cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The initiatives, which did not pass, would have allowed charter schools and the use of education vouchers. The union, which represented employees in public schools, opposed both initiatives in part with a contribution for the campaign from a national teacher's union which it did not report. The foundation, the sponsor of the initiatives, challenged the definition of political committee and the methodology the trial court used to determine whether the union met that definition. The instant court agreed with the trial court that the union was not a political committee. If the union had been a political committee, it would have had to file detailed reports of all bank accounts, all deposits and donations, and all expenditures, including the names of each person contributing funds. The union was not a political committee as a maker or receiver of expenditures. The trial court correctly held that an organization was a political committee if one of its primary purposes was to affect governmental decision making by supporting or opposing candidates or ballot propositions, and it made or expected to make contributions in support of or in opposition to a candidate or ballot measure.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

2064 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Seattle v. McCoy


No. 48578-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


112 Wn. App. 26; 48 P.3d 993; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 558



April 1, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Appellant's Motion to Publish June 13, 2002.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed an order of the King County Superior Court, Washington, which granted attorney fees and costs to respondent property owners, pursuant to Washington's eminent domain statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 8.25.075.


OVERVIEW: The issue in the case was whether the attorney fee provision set forth in § 8.25.075 applied in the context of drug nuisance abatement proceedings. The city argued that the plain language of the provision restricted the application of the statute to proceedings instituted in a formal exercise of the eminent domain power. The owners argued that the proceeding instituted by the city was in effect a condemnation proceeding because the city was seeking to close the property, to prohibit its use for any purpose for one year, and to give custody and control of the property to the court. The instant court agreed with the city that the attorney fees provision set forth in § 8.25.075 did not apply to drug abatement actions. Even assuming the city was acting as a condemnor in the proceedings, § 8.25.075 did not apply, because in initiating the abatement action, the city was not attempting to acquire the owners' property. The instant court rejected the owners' argument that the fee award should be upheld under a theory of inverse condemnation. The owners never made a claim of inverse condemnation at the trial court level and did not prevail as plaintiffs in an inverse condemnation action.


OUTCOME: The instant court reversed the trial court's fee award to the property owners.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought an assessment adjustment of a school impact fee from respondent county, but that request was denied. The developer sought review. 2066 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Hecker v. Cortinas


No. 26256-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


110 Wn. App. 865; 43 P.3d 50; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 532



March 29, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellee ex-husband filed a petition in the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington) seeking a permanent domestic violence protection order against the appellant ex-wife. The court granted the order, and the ex-wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ex-wife argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in granting an order of protection for the ex-husband and his wife because the evidence was insufficient to support the issuance of a protection order. The court of appeals disagreed. There was no requirement of the infliction of physical harm; rather, the infliction of fear of physical harm was sufficient. The record supported the trial court's finding of fear of physical harm sufficient to warrant issuing the protection order. The ex-wife appeared uninvited at the ex-husband's house, pounded on the exterior wall, demanded that the husband's wife come outside, followed the family, and was involved in a physical altercation with the wife. The ex-wife threatened to shoot the ex-husband and his wife and then kill herself. The ex-husband was in fear that the ex-wife would carry out her threats to kill him and his wife. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to warrant the trial court to issue a protection order.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Schlindwein


No. 47386-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 492



March 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Skagit County. Docket No: 91-3-00455-9. Date filed: 05/15/2000.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1300.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed a support modification action seeking additional support from appellant father. An additional modification action was filed by appellee mother seeking an order for postmajority educational support from the father. The Skagit County Superior Court (Washington) ruled that post secondary support was appropriate. The father's motions for reconsideration were denied and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties had one child who was a senior in high school at the time of the instant action and who intended to go to college. The original 1993 divorce decree did not address child support after the age of 18. The appellate court noted courts had the power to modify the decree and order postmajority educational support in compelling circumstances. The child's subsequent showing of ability to attend college could be considered a substantial change of circumstances justifying a modification. Similarly, the minimal entry in the original child support order that postsecondary educational support did not apply was not proof of an agreement between the parties that there would be no eventual support. At the time of the entry of the order, the children were too young for the court or the parents to know whether postsecondary support would be appropriate. However, the trial court failed to make findings on the relevant statutory factors under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.19.090, as to how dependant the child was in relying upon her parents for postsecondary educational support. Therefore, the trial court abused its discretion by perfunctorily ordering postsecondary educational support.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the applicable statute.

 

2068 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mattson


No. 46188-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 517



March 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.    [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 98-1-09413-0. Date filed: 02/18/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald Kessler.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1296.
State v. Mattson, 110 Wn. App. 1069, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1296 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) for indecent liberties by forcible compulsion arising from an incident in which defendant had sexual contact with 15 year old. Because he had a 1985 conviction for statutory rape, he was sentenced to life in prison without parole under the two strikes provision of Washington's Persistent Offender Accountability Act (the two strikes law).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his attorney was ineffective, as he did not offer an instruction for third degree child molestation as a lesser-included offense of the charged offense of indecent liberties with forcible compulsion and referred to defendant's statements to the police during closing. Defendant argued that third degree child molestation should have been considered a lesser-included offense of indecent liberties, even though the lesser offense contained elements that the charged offense did not, because any time the elements for child molestation were satisfied, the elements for indecent liberties would also be satisfied. The appellate court held that no Washington court concluded that third degree child molestation was a lesser-included offense of indecent liberties with forcible compulsion. Given that lack of authority, the court could not conclude that counsel's failure to request an instruction for third degree child molestation was conduct that fell below an objective standard of reasonableness. Defendant's counsel was not ineffective during closing argument. Counsel's theory was supported by the evidence and did not undermine defendant's account of the incident.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a lesser-included instruction, there was no prosecutorial misconduct or evidentiary error. Defendant's prior conviction was properly used as a strike for sentencing purposes, his sentence did not amount to cruel and unusual punishment, and the two strikes law did not violate due process or other constitutional protections.

State v. Bell

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 442

The court further determined that, as appellant's post-conviction relief motions were meritless, the trial court properly exercised its discretion under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. State v. Adams


No. 26336-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 398



March 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 8, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 640.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 001002347. Date filed: 08/18/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Richard D. Hicks.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1222.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) convicting him of custodial assault.


OVERVIEW: While a resident at a juvenile corrections institution, defendant got into a fight with another resident. While the corrections officer intervened, defendant struck him on the chest, below the chin, in the nose, and on the side of his neck. Defendant argued the jury was improperly instructed. The following jury instruction was given: if a person intended to assault a particular individual, and by mistake, the assault took effect upon an unintended individual, the law holds that the intent to assault transferred to the unintended individual or individuals as well. The appellate court ruled that, as defendant's specific intent to assault the named victim was neither a statutory nor a common law element of assault, the transferred intent instruction did not create an uncharged alternative means of committing assault. Also, the instruction did not require the jury to presume any element of assault and accurately defined the doctrine of transferred intent. Furthermore, as the State did not need to prove that defendant intended to assault the officer, the instruction provided an accurate statement of the law relevant to the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wash. Indep. Tel. Ass'n v. WUTC


No. 26832-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


110 Wn. App. 498; 41 P.3d 1212; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 390



March 8, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Wash. Indep. Tel. Ass'n v. Wash. Utils. & Transp. Comm'n, 147 Wn.2d 1008, 56 P.3d 566, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 614 (2002)
Affirmed by Wash. Indep. Tel. Ass'n v. Wash. Utils. & Transp. Comm'n, 149 Wn.2d 17, 65 P.3d 319, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 208 (Wash., Mar. 20, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant independent telephone association appealed the Thurston County Superior Court's (Washington) denial of its petition for review of the appellee Washington Utilities and Transportation Commission's (WUTC) designation of a cellular carrier as an additional eligible telecommunications carrier (ETC) in several rural service areas already served by the association's members.


OVERVIEW: The association argued, inter alia, that the WUTC violated the association's due process rights because each of its members' status as the existing, exclusive ETC for its respective service area was a significant, protected, property interest. The court of appeals disagreed. The plain language of 47 U.S.C.S. § 214(e) demonstrated that Congress contemplated more than one ETC for rural service areas. 47 U.S.C.S. § 214(e)(2) did not protect rural telephone companies from competition; on the contrary it gave WUTC discretion to designate more than one ETC in a rural service area. Because exclusive ETC status was not a protected interest entitling the associations members to procedural due process under federal law, the claim of denial of due process failed, and therefore, the WUTC did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2072 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jennings


No. 48295-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 375



March 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 98-1-10136-5. Date filed: 02/01/2001. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald Kessler.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted in the King County Superior Court (Washington) of delivery of a controlled substance. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the defendant sold cocaine to an undercover officer, other officers arrived and arrested the defendant and his brother. The officers found no drugs or money on either of them. An investigator interviewed the defendant in his cell and the defendant became agitated and threatened that next time he would start shooting police. Those statements were admitted at trial. The defendant argued that the trial court erred by admitting those statements. The court of appeals agreed. The case presented a credibility contest between the arresting officer and the defendant's brother, who denied that a transaction occurred. The State called no observation officers as witnesses. No buy money was recovered and no additional drugs were recovered. The detail with which the officer described the defendant served to confirm that he saw the defendant that night but did not corroborate that the defendant delivered any drugs to the officer. If the jury believed the brother, the officer did not contact the defendant and thus necessarily did not buy drugs from him. The inflammatory threat evidence invited the jury to convict the defendant because he was a threatening, violent young man.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

W. Ports Transp., Inc. v. Emp. Sec.


No. 48294-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


110 Wn. App. 440; 41 P.3d 510; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 347; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P9028



March 4, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent transportation company terminated its driver's "Independent Contractor Agreement," which contained various requirements dictated by federal regulations governing motor carriers that utilize leased vehicles-with-drivers. The appellant employment security department (department) granted unemployment compensation to the driver. The Superior Court for King County (Washington) reversed. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed the superior court and reinstated the department's ruling. The transportation company contended that the driver was not an employee, but an independent contractor exempt from coverage under Wash. Rev. Code § 50.04.140. The personal services that the independent contractor performed for the transportation company constituted "employment," as defined by § 50.04.140, and did not fall within the exemption provided by § 50.04.140. Federal statutes and underlying federal regulations that permitted authorized carriers to engage in interstate commerce utilizing leased trucks-with-drivers were designed to place complete responsibility for possession, use, operation, and control of leased equipment on the authorized carrier, regardless of whether, under common-law principles, the lessor, or driver provided by the lessor of the equipment, might be an independent contractor or an employee of the authorized carrier. That statutory and regulatory scheme did not preempt state employment security law by which a person who might be an independent contractor under federal transportation or common-law principles might nevertheless be entitled to compensation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

2074 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Berrier


No. 26171-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


110 Wn. App. 639; 41 P.3d 1198; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 344



March 1, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a short-barreled shotgun, second degree unlawful possession of a firearm, and unlawful possession of a controlled substance. The Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) imposed firearm sentence enhancements on counts I and III. Defendant appealed, arguing that his weapon was not a firearm, as it was unloaded, and that it violated equal protection to enhance the sentence on Count I.


OVERVIEW: The police were investigating loud music when they found defendant in his car in possession of a shotgun with the butt end removed. On appeal, the appellate court held: (1) an unloaded or even inoperable firearm was still a firearm under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.010(1); (2) defendant was still "armed" under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310(3) (Recodified at Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.510(3)), even though there were no bullets for the firearm; (3) because defendant was holding the firearm and admitted he had modified it to shoot from his hip, the evidence was sufficient to support his conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.190(1); and (4) however, it violated equal protection to enhance defendant's sentence for unlawful possession of a short-barreled shotgun under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310(3)(f) (2000) (Recodified at Wash. Rev. Code. § 9.94.510 (3)), because under that statute similarly situated persons possessing a machine gun, which was also criminalized by Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.190(1), could not have their sentences enhanced.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed, but because the sentence enhancement was unconstitutional as applied to count I, the appellate court vacated that portion of the and remanded the matter for resentencing.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of delivery of methamphetamine, and returned a special verdict finding that the deliveries took place within 1,000 feet of a school ground. State v. Ulbricht


No. 26363-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 299



February 20, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 99-1-03125-5. Date filed: 07/28/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Sergio Armijo.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant challenged the judgment of the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington), which convicted the defendant for felony eluding, a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.024.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant argued that the trial court's improper instruction allowed the jury to infer that the defendant had a wanton or willful disregard for the lives or property of others, if evidence of the defendant's driving supported such an inference. The defendant contended that the instruction unconstitutionally created a mandatory presumption and required him to either rebut the inference or concede that element, and thereby relieved the State of its burden of proof. The defendant also claimed that the evidence was insufficient to show that he drove in a wanton and willful manner. The court found neither contention meritorious and affirmed. The appellate court rejected the defendant's jury instruction claim, because the defendant proposed the instruction and thus invited the error. The court also found that the evidence was sufficient to prove that the defendant drove with wanton or willful disregard for the safety or property of others. The testifying police officer described the defendant driving 72 mph in moderately heavy rush hour traffic, changing lanes without signaling, and, while being pursued, forcing cars to give up their right of way to avoid an accident.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Det. of W.R.G.


No. 26087-5-II, 26871-0-II (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


110 Wn. App. 318; 40 P.3d 1177; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 262



February 15, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant patient appealed the order of the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington), which involuntarily committed him to a state hospital.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in committing him because there was no finding that he was in custody as a result of conduct in which he attempted or inflicted serious harm upon anyone, and thus, the trial court erred in instructing the jury that there was conclusive evidence deciding that issue. Although the jury should not have reached the fourth question dealing with less restrictive alternatives unless it first found proof of all the necessary elements for an involuntary commitment, the verdict form did not advise the jury not to answer question four unless it was satisfied that the State had proven the "taken into custody" element. Consequently, the verdict form did not provide conclusive evidence that the jury found that the patient came into custody as a result of conduct in which he attempted or inflicted serious harm upon the person of another or himself. Thus, the trial court erred in giving instruction four. However, because there was other evidence to support the commitment, the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cole


No. 25990-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 302



February 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Amending Opinion October 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 99-1-01375-0. Date filed: 05/26/2000. Judge signing: Hon. M. Karlynn Haberly.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1009.
State v. Cole, 110 Wn. App. 1029, 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 1009 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of child molestation. The Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) denied the defendant's motion to suppress and sentenced the defendant to life in prison under the persistent offender statute. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's relatives went to the house where he was living to tell the victim's mother that defendant was molesting the victim. Defendant was at home when the relatives arrived. Defendant's cousin called 911 and asked the police to be sent, as a suspected child molester was in the house. The cousin told the 911 operator that they were not going to let defendant leave. Defendant admitted to molesting the girls to his relatives. When the police arrived, defendant was advised of and waived his Miranda rights and confessed to molesting the child. The appellate court held that the absence of police conduct precluded a finding that defendant's confession was involuntary. The family did not become state actors just because the 911 operator said "okay" when defendant's cousin said they were not letting him leave. Defendant's confession to the police was also voluntary, as he was not promised anything in return for his confession or coerced. Because a comparability clause was not included in the two-strikes statute at the time of defendant's prior offense, that offense could not be counted as a comparable strike offense. The court vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, but the life sentence was vacated and the court remanded for resentencing.

Valerio v. Lacey Police Dep't

110 Wn. App. 163; 39 P.3d 332; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 167



February 1, 2002, Decided

OVERVIEW: On review of his forfeiture proceeding, appellant argued that: (1) his forfeiture hearing was untimely; (2) the City failed to prove that he used or intended to use the money for an illegal drug business; and (3) the forfeiture statute, Wash. Sheng-Yen Lu v. King County


No. 47647-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


110 Wn. App. 92; 38 P.3d 1040; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 148; 159 Oil & Gas Rep. 1181



January 28, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants neighbors filed a declaratory judgment action directing respondent county to decide, prior to establishment of the final configuration of mining activities, whether a conditional use permit (CUP) was required for a proposed mining project. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) dismissed the action. The neighbors appealed.


OVERVIEW: A timber company agreed to develop property as a gravel mine and then ultimately donate the land to be held in trust for the county. The project was intended to protect public views and transfer private land to long-term public ownership and timber use. The lower portion of the proposed property identified three improvements within one-quarter mile of a building on the property of one of the neighbors. The county decided that it would wait to determine if the timber company needed to obtain a conditional use permit (CUP) for the proposed mining project. The neighbors originally filed a proceeding under the Land Use Petition Act (LUPA), but later dismissed that action before a decision was rendered. The appellate court held that LUPA provided the exclusive means of review for land use decisions, whether they were quasi-judicial or ministerial. The appellate court found that because LUPA provided an adequate alternative remedy, the case was not ripe for judicial review. The court also reviewed the language in LUPA and held that courts should generally defer to local jurisdictions until a final determination on the use of land was made by the highest body or officer.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the action was affirmed.
