State v. Law


No. 19655-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


110 Wn. App. 36; 38 P.3d 374; 2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 93



January 17, 2002, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was charged in the Franklin County Superior Court (Washington) with second degree escape. The court dismissed the charge after concluding that the defendant should have been charged with the more specific and less serious crime of willful failure to return from furlough. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court correctly dismissed the case because he would get more jail time if the escape statute applied, and therefore, his equal protection rights would be violated. The court of appeals disagreed. The defendant's equal protection argument failed because he was not similarly situated to felons who took leave via furlough. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 72.66.016, a prisoner was not eligible for furlough until the prisoner had served a defined minimum amount of his or her sentence. Even when under the jurisdiction of the department of corrections the secretary could not furlough an inmate until the defined minimum had been served. The defendant had his entire sentence before him when given temporary release by the court for a dentist visit. Thus, his situation and the corresponding deterrents were different. Providing for greater deterrents in perceived higher risk situations was a rational basis for treating escape more severely than failure to return from furlough. That was true even when the escape conviction was premised upon the failure to return from an authorized leave. Therefore, trial court erred in dismissing the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

2083 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Pers. Restraint of Stone


No. 19538-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 27



January 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: DOUGLAS. Docket No(s): 99-1-00071-8. Judge signing: JOHN HOTCHKISS. Date Filed: December 6, 1999. Date first filed in Court of Appeals: August 31, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought relief from personal restraint imposed for his Douglas County Superior Court (Washington) conviction upon his plea of guilty to second degree unlawful possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the trial court miscalculated his offender score by separately counting pre-July 1, 1986 concurrently served convictions and thus imposed a sentence not authorized by the Sentencing Reform Act of 1981 (SRA). The State conceded that petitioner's offender score should have been calculated at 6, not 10, but it argued that the error could not be corrected due to either a stipulation or invited error by petitioner. The instant court agreed with petitioner and granted his requested relief of remand to the trial court for resentencing. Petitioner's pre-July 1, 1986 convictions were improperly counted separately in the offender score calculation and should have counted as one offense, regardless of whether they were the same or separate criminal conduct. Former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.360(5)(a)(ii) (recodified as Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.525 (2001))had to be applied to correct petitioner's offender score. Invited error did not apply, and the stipulation did not prevent this result. Petitioner's requested remedy of remand for resentencing was proper to correct his sentence based upon the miscalculated offender score.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's personal restraint petition was granted to the extent that the matter was remanded for recalculation of his offender score and standard range and resentencing in accordance with the provisions of the SRA.

Caltagirone v. Clark County


No. 26077-8-II, 26233-9-II (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2002 Wash. App. LEXIS 9



January 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE: RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 98-2-03393-6. Date filed: 06/02/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Edwin L. Poyfair.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant property owners appealed a judgment of the Clark County Superior Court (Washington), which affirmed a hearing examiner's decision denying them a conditional use permit for a convenience store, retail space, and a gasoline station. The convenience store and retail space were eventually approved as a permitted use. Respondent county cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners who owned a parcel of land along a state highway unsuccessfully applied for a conditional use permit to build a convenience store with four double-sided gasoline pumps. The county argued that the owners failed to exhaust their administrative remedies by not appealing to the board of county commissioners. The owners argued, among other things, that the hearing examiner incorrectly applied the substantial evidence standard of review and should have applied the deferential common law standard. The instant court held that the trial court properly retained jurisdiction even after it remanded the administrative decision and that the owners were not required to appeal the examiner's remanded decision to the county commissioners. The trial court correctly accepted the examiner's determinations regarding the weight and credibility to be given to reasonable but competing inferences. Substantial evidence supported the decision that a gas station would have been detrimental to and not necessary for the rural community. The examiner did not place too much weight on community displeasure and did not engage in unlawful procedure or act in an arbitrary and capricious manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The county was not entitled to attorney fees on appeal. The owners substantially prevailed in the trial court because the plan for the convenience store was approved, and the trial court remanded the examiner's first decision.

State v. Teuber


NO. 47662-9-1


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


109 Wn. App. 640; 36 P.3d 1089; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2808



December 24, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied August 7, 2002, Reported at: 146 Wn.2d 1021, 52 P.3d 521, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 496.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, appealed a judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which found him guilty for felony hit and run and imposed an exceptional sentence of 24 months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had an extensive history of traffic related misdemeanors and infractions, argued that: (1) the evidence of his use of methamphetamine was not relevant to the crime of hit and run; (2) the trial court erred in imposing an exceptional sentence; and (3) Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120 (the felony sentencing statute) and Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.390 (statutory guidelines for imposing exceptional sentences) were unconstitutionally vague. The instant court rejected defendant's arguments. The State's evidence of defendant's drug use prior to the incident was relevant to prove the ultimate issue at trial - that he was responsible for the hit and run; the evidence tended to disprove his version of the events by showing that he had a motive to be driving at the time of the accident and a reason to be on the route where the accident occurred. Defendant's extensive history of traffic related misdemeanors and infractions was a compelling reason justifying an exceptional sentence. Regarding defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the statutes in question, the instant court noted that it had rejected this argument on three previous occasions and declined to revisit it.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment and sentence were affirmed.

In re Pers. Restraint of Bowman


No. 46585-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


109 Wn. App. 869; 38 P.3d 1017; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2755



December 24, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), sentencing him to 30.75 months for the charge of solicitation to deliver cocaine, imposed pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.410.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28.030 and Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401. At sentencing the trial court determined that defendant's standard range was 30.75 to 40.5 months. Defendant argued it was not clear whether the legislature intended solicitation to be charged under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28 et seq. or as an offense under the Uniform Controlled Substances Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50 et seq. Offenders, such as defendant who solicited a delivery, were subject to a five-year maximum sentence. Offenders who attempted or conspired to commit delivery were subject to a one-year maximum sentence. Defendant asserted that this ambiguity required that the rule of lenity be applied in his favor, resulting in a maximum 12-month sentence. The court ruled that solicitation to deliver was an offense under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.28 et seq., not Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50 et seq. Under the plain language of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.408, the expressed legislative inclusion of attempt and conspiracy was exclusive, and the implied inclusion of solicitation was barred.


OUTCOME: Defendant's personal restraint petition was denied.

Bry v. City of Seattle


No. 46076-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2785



December 24, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-1-05608-6. Date filed: 01/25/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Nicole Mac Innes.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which affirmed his conviction in a lower court for harassment. The instant court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the "mental health" language in the harassment ordinance. On appeal, defendant argued that the "mental health" means of committing harassment was unconstitutional and that the "bodily injury" means was not supported by sufficient evidence. The instant court noted that while defendant's motion was pending, the Washington Supreme Court held in State v. Williams that a nearly identical harassment statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad to the extent it referenced the victim's "mental health." In light of Williams, defendant moved for the instant court to reverse. The instant court concluded that because the challenged portion of the harassment ordinance was identical in all material respects to the "mental health" language struck down in Williams, and because the jury's verdict may have rested on that portion of the ordinance, it had to reverse defendant's conviction. However, there was sufficient evidence to support a harassment conviction under the alternative means of threatening to inflict "bodily injury." Thus, the instant court rejected defendant's contention that the case had to be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

State v. Sutton


No. 46748-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2790



December 24, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 98-1-07679-4. Date filed: 05/25/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Carol Schapira.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted in the King County Superior Court (Washington) of child rape. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in finding the victims, who were three and four years old, competent to testify. If a child could relate contemporaneous events, the court could infer the child was competent to testify about the abuse incidents. The trial court found that the girls had demonstrated independent recollection of the time frame in which the rapes occurred, including memories of the house where they lived, the other people who lived there, and their ages. Both girls demonstrated to the court's satisfaction that they knew the difference between telling the truth and a lie, and the consequences of a lie. At the competency hearing, it was not necessary to make them answer questions about the specific acts of sexual abuse committed by the defendant. Because the girls were capable of relating contemporaneous events, the trial court had tenable grounds to find them competent. Therefore, the trial court did not err in finding the victims competent to testify.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Baldwin


No. 19390-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


109 Wn. App. 516; 37 P.3d 1220; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2748



December 20, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied December 3, 2002, Reported at: 147 Wn.2d 1020, 60 P.3d 92, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 750.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was stopped on suspicion of driving under the influence. He admitted to drinking a glass of wine and taking an antidepressant the night before. Defendant refused to allow a blood test. His refusal was admitted into evidence, and he was convicted of driving under the influence. On appeal, the Superior Court, Spokane County, Washington, affirmed the conviction. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant alleged that the implied consent statute was unconstitutional as applied to drug cases and argued that refusal to submit to a blood test for drugs may not be referenced in a criminal trial. Defendant also alleged that the driving under the statute did not authorize blood draws based on suspicion of drug impairment. The court of appeals held that: (1) the blood test for drugs was justified under the circumstances of this case; (2) the implied consent statute was constitutional as applied to drug cases; (3) the admission of defendant's refusal complied with legislative intent; and (4) the Washington Supreme Court recently rejected the reasoning in Beigh (a case relied on by defendant), thus, since defendant was given the choice to submit to the blood test or to lose his license and to possibly have his refusal admitted at trial, the trooper had statutory authority to request the blood test pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.308(2).


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

2090 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Votava


No. 19910-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


109 Wn. App. 529; 37 P.3d 296; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2750



December 20, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Votava, 56 P.3d 566, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 613 (Wash. Oct. 10, 2002).
Review pending at State v. Votava, 147 Wn.2d 1014, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 467 (2002)
Review granted by State v. Votava, 56 P.3d 566, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 613 (Wash., 2002)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Votava, 149 Wn.2d 178, 66 P.3d 1050, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 287 (Wash., Apr. 17, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State obtained discretionary review of an order of the Superior Court Spokane County (Washington), which reversed defendant's conviction for being in physical control of a vehicle while under the influence of liquor. The superior court remanded the case for retrial and held the district court erred in declining to instruct the jury on the affirmative defense in Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.504(2) .


OVERVIEW: A trooper saw defendant's vehicle, with its engine running and its headlights on, in a Spokane parking lot. The vehicle was illegally parked with its nose on the curb of the roadway. Defendant was asleep in the driver's seat. The trooper awakened defendant, conducted a field sobriety test, and concluded he was under the influence of alcohol. Breath tests later confirmed that conclusion. Defendant claimed he had not driven the car to the parking lot. He claimed that a friend drove him and his car from the bar where they had been drinking to the lot, parked it, and then left them there. The court of appeal held that the superior court clearly was wrong when it stated § 46.61.504(2) provided an affirmative defense, if the vehicle was moved off the roadway. Subsection (2) permitted that defense for a person only if the person had moved the vehicle safely off the roadway. The statute unambiguously required that the person asserting the defense be the same person who moved the vehicle. Because there was no evidence defendant moved the vehicle to the place where the trooper found it, the defense was not available to him.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court was reversed.

Jensen v. City of Everett


NO. 47077-9-1


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2749



December 17, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: County: Snohomish. Docket No(s): 94-2-04827-7. Judge signing: Joseph A. Thibodeau. Date entered: July 5, 2000.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Enforcing an Environmentally Sensitive Areas Ordinance, respondent, the City of Everett, Washington, sanctioned appellant landowners for clearing trees to create a view on their property. Appellants sought review of the order of the Snohomish County, Washington, dismissing their challenge to the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Landowners claimed that enforcement of an Environmentally Sensitive Areas Ordinance was: (1) preempted by the Forest Practices Act; (2) unconstitutionally vague; and (3) violated his right to due process and equal protection. Under Everett, Wash., Mun. Code § 19.37.010, an action could be undertaken by any person which results in any alteration of an environmentally sensitive area. The appellate court rejected the facial challenge to the ordinance. A person reading § 19.37.010 would not have to guess to realize that the cutting of trees above a creek in an environmentally sensitive area modified the natural environment and therefore constituted a development, alteration, or use that required city approval. Therefore, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. Additionally, the ordinance was not preempted by the Forest Practices Act, and landowners failed to show that the application of it violated their right to due process and equal protection. Attorney fees were properly awarded to the city as prevailing party.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. McKinnon


No. 25805-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


110 Wn. App. 1; 38 P.3d 1015; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2666



December 7, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 25, 2002.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington) of failing to register as a sex offender. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in convicting him because his counsel was ineffective for failing to call the trial court's attention to case law which supported his position. The court of appeals agreed. Defense counsel should have known of, and called to the trial court's attention, two cases. One of which had been decided nearly a year earlier, the other nearly five months earlier. Each directly supported the defense the defendant was asserting. Prejudice was also shown because the record did not show with certainty why the trial court convicted. It would have realized it was incorrect, of course, if it had reviewed the case law. Therefore, counsel was ineffective and the defendant was prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Cuble


No. 26258-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


109 Wn. App. 362; 35 P.3d 404; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2647



December 7, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington), which convicted him of first degree unlawful firearm possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the information and the to-convict instruction lacked the essential element of knowledge. Defendant did not challenge the information's or the instruction's omission of knowledge as an element of unlawful firearm possession at his trial. The instant court concluded that the information was not defective; its included terms "unlawfully and feloniously" sufficed to charge the knowledge element. However, the instant court agreed with defendant that the to-convict instruction was erroneous because it omitted knowledge as an element, and it failed to instruct the jury that the burden was on the State to prove that defendant knew he was in possession of the firearm. The to-convict instruction, coupled with the unwitting possession instruction, displaced the burden of proving knowing possession from the State to defendant. The deficient to-convict instruction standing alone was reversible error in light of the defense that defendant neither possessed nor knew about the firearm. The unwitting possession instruction amplified the prejudice by wrongly placing the burden to prove lack of knowledge on defendant, without the State having first proved knowing possession.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Bolar v. State (In re L.B.)


No. 48603-9-I/48602-I [Consolidated]


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2644



December 3, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-7-50013-8. Date filed: 04/05/2001. Judge signing: Hon. James Doherty.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sister of two brothers appealed a judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which denied the sister's motion to intervene in her brothers' dependency actions. The instant court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: The sister sought to intervene in her brothers' dependency actions for the purpose of establishing a right to telephone contact and visitation with her brothers. The sister argued that the trial court erred in ruling that she did not have a right to intervene in the proceedings under Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 24(a)(2). She also contended that it was an abuse of discretion for the trial court to deny her motion to intervene permissively. She also claimed a common law and constitutional right to intervene. The instant court concluded that there was no right to intervene under the Washington Civil Rules, the United States Constitution, or the common law. The trial court's refusal to allow the sister to intervene was not an abuse of discretion. The instant court noted that family members other than siblings had significant interests in the dependency actions of children, but did not have a right to intervene, and the instant court saw no reason why the result should be different in the case of a sibling. The trial court's decision to deny intervention because it found that intervention would have prejudiced the interests of the brothers was not manifestly unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 Walker v. City of Kennewick, 101 Wn. App. 1024, 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 1423 (2000)

Russell v. Jeffers


No. 19275-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2508



November 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3211.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: ASOTIN. Docket No(s): 98-2-00252-8. Judge signing: JOHN LYDEN. Date filed: July 24, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part, and the forfeiture action was dismissed..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner family was served with notices of seizure and forfeiture of property connected with drug transactions. They removed the case to the Asotin County Superior Court (Washington) which found that the items were all properly seized except for certain bank and retirement accounts, and proceeds from an insurance policy. The family and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State seized various personal property that was used in the sale of illegal drugs, and also some bank and retirement accounts. The court addressed whether the procedures mandated by Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.505 had been followed. A court's authority to order a forfeiture of property derived solely from the statute. The statute thus provided the exclusive mechanism for forfeiting property allegedly used in drug trafficking. The government was estopped from proceeding in a forfeiture action if it failed to follow statutory procedures. When real or personal property was seized under the statute without a prior adversarial hearing, due process required that such a hearing be held within 90 days. The State argued that the 90-day requirement did not apply when a claimant removed a forfeiture action to a court. There was no logical basis for such a distinction. Because a hearing of some type was required within 90 days, it made no difference for due process purposes in what forum such a hearing was held. The State failed to initiate the hearing process within 90 days. The delay thus violated the family's right to due process.


OUTCOME: The part of the judgment which excluded property was affirmed, the part of the judgment which forfeited property was reversed, and the forfeiture action was dismissed.

Shoreline v. Club for Free Speech


No. 47569-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


109 Wn. App. 696; 36 P.3d 1058; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2511



November 13, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported in Table Case Format at: 109 Wn. App. 1015, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3218. Order Publishing Opinion December 18, 2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought an injunction against defendant club requiring it to comply with the Shoreline, Wash., Municipal Code 5.10.070(A)(6) adult cabaret ordinance. The club counterclaimed on Constitutional issues. The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted the city's motion for summary judgment, and imposed a permanent injunction against the club that required it to comply with the adult cabaret ordinance. The club appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court issued an injunction against a previous club and it ceased operation. On the same day the defendant club began operating a non-profit private membership club featuring live adult entertainment at the same location, in a commercial zone. Police officers misrepresented their identities and became members of the club, conducting surveillance of the club's activities and witnessing violations of the adult cabaret ordinance, including the four-foot rule. The appellate court found that: (1) the club members were not entitled to constitutionally-protected freedom of association rights to make choices to enter into and maintain certain intimate human relationships because it was not a small group, and the club's operations were nearly identical to its predecessor; (2) there was no evidence that the city required the club to admit police officers into membership; (3) the adult cabaret ordinance did not preclude the club from revoking membership to anyone; (4) the adult cabaret ordinance as applied did not violate its members' rights to associate; and (5) the adult cabaret ordinance applies in the same manner to club members as it does to anyone else.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

2100 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lane


No. 45702-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2513



November 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3212.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-02888-7. Date filed: 11/02/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Harriett M. Cody.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pleaded guilty to drive by shooting and entered an Alford plea of guilty to second degree assault while armed with a firearm in the Superior Court of King County (Washington). The defendant was sentenced to a total of 93 months. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in failing to count his prior juvenile offenses and the two charged crimes as the same criminal conduct in calculating his offender score. The court of appeals disagreed. The defendant's motor vehicle theft, eluding, and possession offenses were not the same criminal conduct because they did not share the same objective intent and they involved different victims. His intent in the theft was to drive a stolen car, while his intent in the possession was to possess drugs. His intent in eluding was to avoid being arrested. His eluding did not further the other two crimes. Commission of one crime merely to escape the consequences of another crime represented a change in intent. Where a defendant had the opportunity to decide to end the criminal incident but went on to commit additional crimes, the later crimes did not further the earlier crimes. Moreover, the crimes had different victims. The theft victimized the car's owner, while possession of cocaine victimized the public in general. The victims of the eluding included the pursuing officers and all of the civilians he endangered through his driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2101 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. Bd. of Indus. Ins. Appeals


No. 46991-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


109 Wn. App. 88; 34 P.3d 267; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2537



November 13, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant veteran submitted his job application to the respondent board of industrial insurance appeals (Board). The board granted the veteran an interview, but eventually offered the position to another candidate. The veteran sued the board to enforce the veteran's preference established by Wash. Rev. Code § 73.16.015. The Superior Court, King County (Washington), granted the board's motion for summary judgment, and the veteran appealed.


OVERVIEW: The veteran argued that the statute obligated the board to select him for the position over the non-veteran applicant, as by meeting the board's advertised minimum required qualifications of a law degree and membership in the bar, he showed that he had the necessary capacity to discharge the duties of the position. The successful candidate, a non-veteran, also had considerable experience as a lawyer in the field of industrial insurance and, unlike the veteran, had experience as a supervisor. The appellate court held that in order to comport with the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the Washington Constitution, the statutory preference applied only where a veteran possessed qualifications that were substantially equal to those of non-veteran applicants. Because the veteran in the case at bar possessed only the minimum qualifications, the trial court properly dismissed the suit. Statutory veteran's preferences were generally held to be unconstitutional, if they afforded an absolute preference for veterans in employment that required special skills and abilities beyond the discipline, loyalty, and public spirit properly presumed to be characteristic of veterans.


OUTCOME: The dismissal by the trial court was affirmed.

Scearcy v. City of Tacoma


No. 26648-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2473



November 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied June 4, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 381. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3170.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 002099211. Date filed: 10/17/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Stephanie A. Arend.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee appealed his termination by respondent city to the civil service board (Board), which reinstated him. The employee then appealed the suspension to the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington), requesting that it issue a writ of certiorari to review the Board's decision. The city moved to dismiss the writ, and the superior court granted the motion. The employee appealed the denial of the writ of certiorari to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the city, and was terminated from his position because of inappropriate conduct, including using racial epithets and profane language. The Board concluded the conduct warranted discipline but, in light of the city's poor management practices, that termination was not appropriate. The employee claimed that the Board violated a binding union contract that required progressive discipline prior to his termination. However his brief to the trial court did not contain the progressive discipline materials the employee claimed were violated. The appellate court noted the Board's review of personnel policy was not considered a judicial function. The only remaining source of jurisdiction for the appellate court, and the trial court in its appellate capacity, was the appellate court's inherent constitutional power. This review was thus limited to a demonstration that the board acted either illegally or in an arbitrary and capricious manner. The Board conducted three hearings that provided both sides an opportunity to present evidence in the matter and the employee failed to demonstrate that the Board acted illegally or in an arbitrary and capricious manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court denying the writ of certiorari was affirmed.

 

2103 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


City of Lakewood v. Olson


No. 25928-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2475



November 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3167.


PRIOR HISTORY: District Court County: Pierce. Docket No: 99-2-07371-7. Date filed: 04/07/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Frederick B. Hayes.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent business owner appealed a municipal court citation for failure to bring non-conforming signs into conformance following a change in nature of the business. By way of discretionary review, the appellant city sought review of the Superior Court of Pierce County ruling that the city's sign ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Before the City incorporated, the business owner bought a building in which he subsequently leased space to successive retail businesses. The business owner had historically used signs on the property to advertise the businesses. Subsequently the city charged the business owner with violating Lakewood, Wash., Mun. Code § 18.45.160(C), for failure to bring the signs into conformance when the nature, name, and ownership of the tenants' businesses changed. The appellate court noted that non-conforming uses were disfavored and were subject to subsequently enacted, reasonable, police power regulations. Further, the city's sign ordinance promoted several public purposes: (1) to increase the effectiveness of individual signs; (2) to control dangerous conflicts between traffic control signs and advertising signs; (3) to promote safety, comfort, and well-being of the users of city streets; (4) to enhance the city's visual character; and (5) to permit and to encourage sign designs responsive to public needs. Finally, the appellate court held the city's sign ordinance was a reasonable regulation enacted to protect community health and safety, and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court holding that the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to the business owner was reversed.

 

2104 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Gerean v. Martin-Joven


No. 19708-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


108 Wn. App. 963; 33 P.3d 427; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2454



October 30, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied June 4, 2002, Reported at: 146 Wn.2d 1013, 51 P.3d 88, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 395.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff filed suit against the defendant in the Spokane County Superior Court (Washington) for damages she sustained when the defendant allegedly ran a stop sign and hit her. The court granted the defendant's motion to dismiss for insufficient service of process and the plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiff's process server served the complaint on the defendant's father at the defendant's former place of residence, and the father gave the complaint to the defendant the following day. The plaintiff argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by dismissing the suit because: (1) the father delivered the complaint to the defendant; and (2) the defendant waived the right to assert the defense by her tardiness in alerting the plaintiff to any deficiency. The court of appeals held that the trial court had not erred because: (1) the plaintiff's argument that the defective substitute service was cured if the summons was fortuitously delivered by a person who was over the age of 18 and not a party to the lawsuit boiled down to the argument that actual notice was sufficient, but actual notice did not constitute sufficient service; and (2) the defendant's notice of appearance reserved all defenses, she asserted the defense both in her answer and by motion, she alerted the plaintiff that the method of service was a matter of interest to the defense, and she asked for a copy of the affidavit of service, but the request was ignored.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stewart v. Omak Sch. Dist. No. 19

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE

PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: OKANOGAN. Docket No(s): 00-2-00163-2. Judge signing: JOHN BURCHARD. Date filed: November 13, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher challenged the order of the Superior Court, Okanogan County, Washington granting summary judgment and dismissing the teacher's claim seeking compensation for teaching an overload of students.


OVERVIEW: The teacher argued that: (1) the time limit of Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.645.010 applied only to administrative decisions interpreting school policy or employment contracts; and (2) respondent school district's failure to notify her of the 30-day time limit denied her due process. The appellate court determined that: (1) § 28A.645.010 applied to all administrative decisions by a school board or official, and the court had no jurisdiction to hear the teacher's case because she waited at least six months to appeal the decision in superior court; and (2) there was no violation of due process as the teacher had no property interest requiring the due process protections in public employment or in correct personnel decisions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order.

 

2106 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


No. 19320-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TEN


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2332



October 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: County: YAKIMA. Docket No(s): 00-1-00210-1. Judge signing: C. JAMES LUST. Date filed: May 5, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Superior Court for Yakima County (Washington) of drive-by shooting. Wash. Rev. Code. § 9A.36.045. He appealed and contended that the court erred by: (1) giving a mandatory presumption jury instruction; (2) allowing testimony that defendant had access to a gun; and (3) denying Mr. Rodriguez's motion for a mistrial after a witness mentioned that defendant had been in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's former girlfriend testified that while they were dating, he showed her a gun and indicated he got it from his brother's room. The appellate court concluded that access to a gun had some relevance in proving the crime of drive-by shooting. However, the relevance of that evidence was limited. The State produced no evidence that the gun was used in the shooting. The relevance of the evidence was outweighed by its prejudicial effect. The admission of essentially character evidence was error. Defendant also argued that the permissive inference language of the questioned jury instruction was unconstitutional. Defendant's evidence consisted of testimony that he was somewhere else at the time of the shooting. Under those circumstances, the inference instruction was a mandatory inference, which violated defendant's constitutional rights. The instruction to which defendant assigned error violated his rights because it shifted the burden of production on an element of the crime from the State to defendant. The error was not harmless because the court was not convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that any reasonable jury would have reached the same result without the error.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed and the case remanded for a new trial.

In re Pers. Restraint of Marler


No. 45086-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


108 Wn. App. 799; 33 P.3d 743; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2312



October 22, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a personal restraint petition challenging various decisions of the Washington Indeterminate Sentence Review Board (board) relating to her parole, and to calculation of her good time.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of murder for hire and was sentenced to life in prison, with a minimum term to be fixed by the board. The board set the inmate's minimum term at 312 months, the high end of the Sentencing Reform Act of 1981, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.94A. (2000), range. The mutual agreement program (MAP) process for the inmate was ordered in March 2000. By August 2000, when she filed the supplement to her personal restraint petition, the inmate had heard nothing. Sometime before January 2001, the inmate received a draft of the MAP. By the time of oral argument in May 2001, no MAP had been approved. The appellate court found that: (1) the board violated Wash. Rev. Code § 9.95.009(2), and its own procedures by imposing a MAP with no time frame; (2) the inmate's accrual of statutory good time before and during the MAP process had to be clarified; and (3) all of the inmate's other arguments, were either not well taken or were moot.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted in part and the matter was remanded to the board with instructions to fix a new minimum term, essentially, to immediately implement a MAP, and to delineate clearly the effect of a MAP upon accrual of statutory good time. In all other respects the petition was denied.

State v. Schilling

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2343

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicted defendant of unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, while armed with a firearm, and first degree unlawful possession of a firearm. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant claimed that: (1) the seizure of the evidence used against him was unconstitutional; (2) trial counsel's failure to challenge the seizure deprived him of his constitutional right to effective assistance of counsel; and (3) there was insufficient evidence to support either conviction. In his pro se supplemental brief, defendant claimed the prosecutor improperly commented on his pre-arrest silence and violated an order in limine. The court of appeals addressed only the issues of sufficiency of the evidence and the prosecutor's comments on defendant's pre-arrest silence. The court of appeals held that: (1) it was sufficient to show that defendant had dominion and control of another person's car trunk and the weapon within it; (2) the evidence supported the verdict that defendant was armed with a deadly weapon while manufacturing methamphetamine; and (3) the State tainted the verdict by encouraging the jury to infer from defendant's silence that he knew that the drugs and the gun were in the trunk of the car, and the untainted evidence was not so overwhelming as to establish guilt.


OUTCOME: The convictions were reversed and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Edwards


No. 46183-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2277



October 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-03251-5. Date filed: 01/24/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Norma S. Huggins.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of second degree burglary in the Superior Court of King County (Washington). The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant had been convicted several times of shoplifting at a department store. The store issued a criminal trespass warning that barred her from entering the store for two years. She entered the store within two years and attempted to shoplift some things. The defendant argued that the criminal trespass warning was unconstitutional, and therefore could not support the unlawful entry element of burglary. The court of appeals disagreed and declined to consider the constitutional argument. The defendant also asserted that she entered the store on April 17, 1999, with a good faith belief that the 1997 warning was invalid because a municipal court had previously found a 1995 trespass warning invalid and because of assurances provided by the store's security manager. As part of the trial stipulation, she acknowledged that she received the criminal trespass warning and that the store security manager called two days later and advised her that she was not welcome inside any of the department store's locations. That notice sufficiently advised the defendant that she was no longer licensed, privileged, or otherwise invited to be on the store's property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Eidson v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 48275-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


108 Wn. App. 712; 32 P.3d 1039; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2648



October 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals November 21, 2001.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. As Amended by Order of the Supreme Court November 21, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2592.


PRIOR HISTORY: 108 Wn. App. 712, 32 P.3d 1039.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent department of licensing issued charges against respondent appraiser in connection with two appraisal reports he prepared. A hearing was held, and the administrative law judge (ALJ) issued an order revoking the appraiser's real estate appraiser's license. On review, the director of the department sustained the ALJ's order. On judicial review, the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington affirmed the director's order.


OVERVIEW: The department concluded that the two appraisals about which it had received complaints contained significant errors and/or deficiencies and contained unsupported value assignments. On appeal, the appraiser argued that the department should have been required to prove its case by clear and convincing evidence rather than by a preponderance of the evidence. The appellate court determined that, as appraiser disciplinary proceedings involved violations of objective standards of conduct, the interests of the license holder and the public would be protected with the less stringent preponderance of the evidence standard. The court declined to disturb the order sanctioning the appraiser for failing to produce one of the contested appraisals; there was nothing in Wash. Rev. Code § 18.140.160(9) to suggest that the appraiser must have acted knowingly or intentionally. Although the court found that some of the director's findings were not supported by substantial evidence, those that were also violated the Uniform Standards of Professional Appraisal Practice and demonstrated a failure to exercise due diligence. Reconsideration of the sanction imposed was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the director's conclusion that the appraiser violated the Real Estate Appraiser Act and remanded for reconsideration of the sanction imposed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant had been convicted of indecent liberties with a child in 1976. Shortly before he was to be released after completing his sentence for his 1976 conviction, the State filed a petition to have him committed to the custody of the Washington Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS). The court granted the State's commitment petition and the defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that the trial court erred by committing him to DSHS because: (1) he suffered from a mental disease or defect, and he possessed a specific characteristic that precluded him from being an sexually violent predator (SVP); and (2) the offered treatment was inadequate to accommodate his developmental disability, and therefore, it should have civilly committed him under Wash. Hirsch v. State


No. 26176-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2267



October 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 99-2-01010-5. Date filed: 06/30/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Richard D. Hicks.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An administrative law judge determined appellant parents' obligation to respondent Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS) for the support of their incarcerated child. The DSHS Board of Appeals and the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) affirmed. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents' adopted son was committed to a juvenile detention facility. Using a cost schedule created under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.220(3), the department determined the parents' monthly obligation for their son's care and maintenance. The court of appeals held that: (1) DSHS correctly determined the parents' support obligation by applying § 13.40.220(3) without considering their circumstances; (2) application of the reimbursement schedule without regard to mitigating circumstances was not arbitrary or capricious; (3) § 13.40.220(3) did not violate equal protection or impermissibly distinguish between parents of juvenile offenders, who were required to pay support, and parents of juvenile offenders convicted as adults, who were not required to pay support, as a rational basis existed for the distinction; (4) substantive due process was satisfied, as the requirement of § 13.40.220(3) was rationally related to the goal of making parents responsible for the cost of their child's support; and (5) due process was satisfied, as the parents received adequate notice and a fair opportunity to be heard and took full advantage of the administrative appeal process.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

State v. Karas


No. 26493-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


108 Wn. App. 692; 32 P.3d 1016; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2258



October 12, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) to residential burglary and violation of a domestic violence protection order. Defendant argued on appeal that the Domestic Violence Prevention Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.50, was unconstitutional and the domestic violence order was invalid.


OVERVIEW: A permanent protection order excluding defendant from entering a residence was issued. After entering the residence, defendant was charged with residential burglary and violation of a protection order. Defendant argued that the Domestic Violence Prevention Act lacked procedural due process protections. He also argued that the superior court commissioner lacked authority to issue a permanent protection order. Defendant failed to establish the protection order's invalidity. The Act's provisions satisfied the two fundamental requirements of due process: notice and a meaningful opportunity to be heard by a neutral decisionmaker. Considering the minor curtailment of defendant's liberty and the significant public and governmental interest in reducing the potential for irreparable injury, the Act's provision of notice and a hearing satisfied the inherently flexible demands of procedural due process. Wash. Rev. Code § 2.24.040 included the power to issue permanent protection orders.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

N. Kitsap Coordinating Council v. Kitsap County


No. 46624-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2232



October 1, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 96-2-32502-3. Date filed: 04/05/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Ann Schindler.



DISPOSITION: Trial court reversed and the County's approval of the Screen's PUD and UUP applications reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant land owners applied for a planned unit development (PUD) and an unclassified use permit (UUP) in order to develop their land. Their applications were approved under the Kitsap County, Wash., Zoning Ordinance § 14(a) (1983). The appellees a community organization appealed the approval. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) found for the community organization. The land owners appealed and the organization cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reversed the county's approval of the PUD on the basis of a court of appeals' decision that was partially reversed shortly after the trial court issued its decision. The court on appeal held that because the trial court's only basis for having reversed the county's approval of the PUD had been trumped, the approval of the PUD had to be reinstated. The court also held that, although the land owners had not applied for a plat subdivision concurrently with their PUD application or at any other time during the approval process their PUD was vested under the terms of Kitsap County, Wash., Interim Zoning Ordinance § 455.100 (1995). Additionally, the Kitsap County, Wash., Zoning Ordinance (1983) did not require that a plat application accompany a PUD application in order for the PUD application to be complete. The organization's argument that common space must be commonly owned also failed. Status as open space was to be determined by use, not ownership according to the definition in the Kitsap County, Wash., Zoning Ordinance § 3(c)(55) (1983). The organization had failed to carry its burden to establish that the county erroneously interpreted its ordinances.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and the approval of the PUD and UUP applications were reinstated.

In re Det. of Jones


No. 44442-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2237



October 1, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 97-2-23737-8. Date filed: 03/15/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Joan E. Dubuque.
In re Det. of Jones, 108 Wn. App. 1026, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3004 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which ordered him committed, pursuant to a jury verdict, as a sexually violent predator under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, who had been convicted of rape and burglary, argued that the trial court failed to properly exercise its discretion in failing to excuse a potential juror for cause. The instant court agreed, noting that the juror in question candidly indicated that she was a recent victim of rape, the same type of offense as that committed by petitioner. The potential jury stated that because of her past circumstances she would have had a difficult time being impartial. Nothing in the potential juror's responses to the deputy prosecutor's attempt to rehabilitate her through his questions and statements truly indicated that she could in fact lay her bias aside. While the potential juror stated that she hoped she could do so, nowhere in the exchange with the prosecutor did he elicit a statement from her that she could be fair and impartial in light of her experience as a victim of rape. Her original assertions were strong indications of actual bias, bias that could not likely be set aside. Thus, the trial court abused its discretion in failing to excuse the potential juror for cause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Custody of R.R.B.


No. 25690-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


108 Wn. App. 602; 31 P.3d 1212; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2162

Review granted by Rosenthal v. Budack (In re R.R.B.), 145 Wn.2d 1033, 43 P.3d 21, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 224 (2002)
Review denied by Rosenthal v. Budack (In re R.R.), 151 Wn.2d 355, 2004 Wash. LEXIS 441 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent petitioned for custody of his biological child under the nonparental custody statute, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 26.10. The Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) granted the petition, and ordered appellants, the child's adoptive parents, to pay current and back child support. The court also ordered visitation as determined by the child and her counselor. The adoptive parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that: (1) Wash. Rev. Const. art. I, § 7 was intended to afford greater privacy protection outside the search-and-seizure context than the federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pauling


No. 46492-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


108 Wn. App. 445; 31 P.3d 47; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2084



September 17, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Pauling, 146 Wn.2d 1001, 45 P.3d 551, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 262 (Wash. May 1, 2002).
Review granted by State v. Pauling, 146 Wn.2d 1001, 45 P.3d 551, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 262 (2002)
Reversed by State v. Pauling, 149 Wn.2d 381, 69 P.3d 331, 2003 Wash. LEXIS 369 (2003)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Pauling v. McKenna, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33595 (W.D. Wash., Sept. 8, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed charges against the defendant for extortion. The Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington), convicted the defendant on two counts of second-degree extortion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim and the defendant lived together for several months before the victim terminated the relationship, and left behind sexually explicit photographs of herself. The victim's neighbors received letters purportedly from her, but sent by the defendant, that introduced her as a porn star, included copies of the photographs, and listed an Internet address. Defendant also sent the victim a letter demanding payment of a debt, for which he had received a default judgment, and stated that if she paid the debt he would be out of her life and hoped it wouldn't be necessary for him to let her neighbors know what kind of a person she was. The court concluded that the defendant's acts were wrongful, and constituted both the tort of defamation and intentional infliction of emotional distress; however, the extortion statute did not contain a wrongfulness element. Therefore, the court determined that the extortion statute was impossibly overbroad because it was not limited to wrongful threats and did not include any defenses that would limit its reach; the extortion statute substantially burdened a wide range of protected speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

2119 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beckham


No. 25810-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2096



September 14, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Wahkiakum County. Docket No: 99-1-00019-1. Date filed: 04/03/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Joel M. Penoyar.



DISPOSITION: Beckham's conviction for unlawful hunting affirmed, his conviction for waste of wildlife reversed, and remanded to trial court for dismissal of this charge with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Wahkiakum County, Washington, which convicted him of unlawful hunting and waste of wildlife in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 77.15.410(2), 77.15.170(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot two elk out of season and left them to decay where they fell. The charging document alleged that the defendant "did kill, take, or possess game animals; to-wit: elk, having a value of $ 250 or more, and did recklessly allow such wildlife to be wasted." The trial court found that the State failed to prove the value of the elk, and allowed the State to amend the charging document to delete the value. Defendant's counsel objected to the witness's use of the term "poaching." The appellate court found that: (1) the trial court did not err in admitting the testimony of the fish and wildlife agent because he had personal knowledge he acquired through his investigation of the elk remains, his perceptions formed a rational basis for his testimony, and his testimony helped the trier of fact, (2) defense counsel was not ineffective because he did object to the use of the term "poaching," and the danger of confusing the jurors was minimal, and (3) the trial court erred in amending the charging document because the amendment removed an essential element of the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for unlawful hunting was affirmed. Defendant's conviction for waste of wildlife was reversed, and remanded to trial court for dismissal with prejudice.

 

2120 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Finder v. Finder


No. 26212-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2097



September 14, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 98-3-00791-2. Date filed: 06/23/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Roger A. Bennett.



DISPOSITION: Trial court affirmed on all issues except release regarding Richard's medications.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant father appealed from the parenting plan order of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) entered pursuant to his divorce with the appellee mother. The court ordered that the father not have overnight visits with the children, that the mother have regular access to his prescription records, and that he was required to store his medications in a gun safe. The mother cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by: (1) denying him overnight visitation with his children without finding misconduct; and (2) ordering him to execute a release giving the mother access to his prescription drug records. The court of appeals held that: (1) the trial court had not erred because the trial court was concerned with the father's current ability to care for the children overnight, considering the medications he took daily and the effect they had on his attentiveness; the court's ruling did not address past misconduct that had now been remedied, but rather, it acknowledged a long history of depression, back pain, and insomnia that necessitated the current and likely continuing use of medications; and (2) the trial court had erred because it made no findings that the mother had any medical training or knowledge that would justify her monitoring the father's prescription usage; without such knowledge, an increase in dosage or change in medication would mean nothing to her, yet would likely be used to create parental conflict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to all issues except the mother's access to the father's medication records.

 

2121 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Seattle v. Patu


No. 45284-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


108 Wn. App. 364; 30 P.3d 522; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2055



September 10, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review granted: City of Seattle v. Patu, 145 Wn.2d 1034, 43 P.3d 21, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 232 (Wash. Apr. 2, 2002).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Seattle Municipal Court (Washington) on two counts of obstructing a police officer, in violation of Seattle, Wash., Code § 12A.16.010(A). The instant court granted discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) the ordinance was overbroad because the ordinance did not require that any actual interference with a police investigation occurred; (2) the ordinance was facially vague; (3) the ordinance was vague as applied to him; and (4) the trial court failed to issue a limiting instruction on the proper use of his prior conviction for false reporting. The instant court held that the ordinance was not overbroad. Because the ordinance required actual obstruction of an investigation in progress, the ordinance did not give officers unfettered discretion to limit mere verbal challenges to police action. The ordinance was both content neutral and narrowly tailored to serve a significant government interest. Defendant could not challenge the ordinance as facially vague as applied to others unless he could show that it was vague as applied to him. Although the trial court's "to convict" jury instruction was constitutionally deficient, the instant court did not grant relief because defendant invited the error by proposing the faulty instruction. Any error arising from the trial court's failure to include a limiting instruction was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2122 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 45061-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2047



September 6, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 5, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 60.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-1-03013-7. Date filed: 07/20/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Brian D. Gain.



DISPOSITION: We hold that any error in failing to require a return from the State was harmless. We affirm the superior court's denial of the petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The King County Superior Court (Washington) denied defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order contained no findings of fact and provided no explanation for the denial of the petition. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying the petition without first requiring a return or a response to the petition by the State. The instant court held that defendant was not entitled to a full response by the State and that the trial court did not need to conduct a hearing before denying the petition. Requiring a specific response by the State and a hearing upon the mere filing of a petition for writ of habeas corpus would have required all correctional facilities to transport the inmate to a court for a hearing without any regard to how frivolous the petition might be. The instant court declined to read Wash. Rev. Code § 7.36.100 as requiring the State to submit a legal memorandum in opposition to the petition. The State's failure to file a return in the case did not require remand, as defendant did not demonstrate that he suffered any prejudice from the absence of the return. Any error in failing to require a return from the State was harmless. All of the issues raised by defendant were either frivolous or had been previously decided.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus was affirmed.

State v. Black


No. 25731-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2030



August 31, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 5, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 129.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 99-1-00845-8. Date filed: 03/10/2000. Judge signing: Hon. John A. McCarthy.
State v. Black, 108 Wn. App. 1004, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2917 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicting him for first degree rape of a child.


OVERVIEW: On review following his jury conviction for first degree rape of a child, defendant argued that the prosecutor's closing argument prejudicially focused on his right to remain silent, especially in light of the staleness of the evidence. The appellate court agreed. At trial, the right against self-incrimination prohibited the State from forcing the defendant to testify. Moreover, the State could not elicit comments from witnesses or make closing arguments relating to a defendant's silence to infer guilt from such silence. Therefore, the prosecution could not use at trial the fact the defendant stood mute or claimed his privilege in the face of accusation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded for new trial.

Degel v. Buty


No. 45544-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


108 Wn. App. 126; 29 P.3d 768; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2011



August 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 5, 2002, Reported at: 145 Wn.2d 1031, 42 P.3d 975, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 135.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice case against defendant doctor, who delivered a brain damaged baby, plaintiff mother appealed a judgment on a defense jury verdict entered by the King County Superior Court (Washington). The mother also appealed the trial court's denial of her posttrial motions for a directed verdict or a new trial on the issue of informed consent.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue was whether the doctor failed to obtain the mother's informed consent when he artificially ruptured the mother's membranes in order to attach an electrode for the purpose of internally monitoring the fetus. The mother contended, among other things, that the informed consent statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 7.70.050, on which the informed consent jury instruction was based, was unconstitutional. She also argued that the trial court erred by giving the informed consent instruction. The instant court held that the mother failed to establish that the objective standard regarding causation in § 7.70.050, which had been adopted by a vast majority of jurisdictions, was unconstitutional. The standard for recovering damages in a lawsuit against a doctor had no bearing on the patient's freedom to choose medical procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Magnusson


No. 45266-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


108 Wn. App. 109; 29 P.3d 1256; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 2013



August 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father filed a petition for modification of the child parenting plan based on moving his residence to another city. The Superior Court of Skagit County, Washington, entered a modification order adopting the father's plan, and the mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The original parenting plan provided that the child would spend alternating weeks with each parent. At that time, the residences of the mother and father were close. The father moved to another city to get a job. The trial court modified the plan so that the father's visitation was every other weekend, and provided that when the father was away he could designate his family members to care for the child. The appellate court found that: (1) the trial court's modification of the parenting plan was lawful because it did not interfere with the mother's parental rights in that the father was given the right to designate those members of his family who were authorized to care for the child while he was gone, (2) the adequate cause determination provided no basis for vacation of the modified parenting plan, (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by allowing the amendment to the petition, (4) the mother was not awarded attorney fees because she raised no meritorious issues, and (5) the father was properly awarded attorney fees because the mother had been intransigent, and had made the litigation protracted and expensive.


OUTCOME: The order modifying the parenting plan was affirmed. The father was awarded attorney fees on appeal.

In re Det. Of Davenport


No. 18653-9-III, 18654-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FIVE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1990



August 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 5, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 131. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3434.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: FRANKLIN. Docket No(s): 96-2-50154-1 (No. 18653-9-III), 99-2-50349-2 (No. 18654-7-III). Judge signing: HON. DENNIS D. YULE. Date filed: August 27, 1999 (No. 18653-9-III), July 1, 1999 (No. 18654-7-III).
In re Detention of Davenport, 107 Wn. App. 1059, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 3434 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent State detained appellant inmate as a sexually violent predator, it failed to hold a timely probable cause hearing. The Superior Court, Franklin County, Washington, dismissed the sexually violent predator petition, but allowed the State to re-file. After a probable cause hearing, the superior court found probable cause existed to establish that the inmate was a sexually violent predator. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the inmate alleged inter alia that: (1) it was error to dismiss the earlier petition without prejudice and to allow the State to refile; (2) it was error not to dismiss the later petition; and (3) it was error to find the State did not need to prove the inmate's mental disorders impaired his volitional control to the degree he could not control his impulses. The court of appeals held: (1) that the failure to hold a probable cause hearing within 72 hours did not require dismissal, absent evidence that the failure to hold the hearing adversely affected the outcome of the trial; (2) because the inmate failed to show that the failure to hold his probable cause hearing within 72 hours adversely affected the outcome of his trial, the superior court did not err by dismissing the petition without prejudice and allowing the State to file a new petition; (3) the State's motion to redesignate the remaining portion of the inmate's appeal as a discretionary review proceeding was granted; and (4) the superior court did not commit probable error.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

State v. Allen


No. 46225-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1899



August 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-08738-7. Date filed: 03/03/2000.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for intimidating a judged pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.72.160 in the Superior Court of King County (Washington), claiming that the statute was overly broad, his attorney was ineffective, and the trial court abused its discretion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for making a phone call threatening a judge, claiming someone else did it. The appellate court held that although § 9A.72.160 concerned private speech, it was not overly broad. It was narrowly tailored, closely related to a significant state interest, and the words themselves were not criminalized. Defendant's unwarranted concerns did not render the statute overbroad. Counsel moved to admit other suspect evidence before the trial began, but made a tactical decision not to renew the motion. Defendant failed to overcome the strong presumption of competence. He also failed to explain why the judge's opinion as to who committed the crime was admissible. The judge's failure to suspect him was irrelevant. The fact that the judge did not initially suspect any particular person did not make it more or less probable that defendant committed the crime.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of failing to reregister as a sex offender after he had moved from his original residence. The appellate court found that the trial court had allowed the State to present evidence of the sheriff's office's standard registration procedures. It did not, however, allow defendant to rebut the evidence.
