State v. Timothy K.

August 6, 2001, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, which convicted him of malicious mischief in the second degree and malicious harassment in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.48.080(1)(a), 9A.36.080(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove by the victim's car while a passenger hit it with pliers. The victim was gay. There was evidence that defendant's car had been used in several prior drive-by incidents, while someone shouted homophobic expletives out of the window. OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court was affirmed.

State v. Lee

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1855

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of unlawful delivery of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school bus route stop in the Superior Court of King County (Washington). The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that: (1) his counsel was ineffective for failing to object to opinion testimony about his guilt; (2) the sentence enhancement did not provide fair notice of proscribed conduct as required by due process; and (3) his sentence did not adequately specify the geographic restrictions during community placement. State v. Rayburn


No. 26688-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1837



August 3, 2001, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a convicted sex offender, appealed an order of the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington) denying his motion to modify its order revoking his suspended sentence.


OVERVIEW: In March 1994, the trial court revoked appellant's special sex offender sentencing alternative (SSOSA) because of his failure to make acceptable progress in his sexual deviancy treatment. The sentence was valid on its face and appellant's action was time-barred under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090. Although appellant contended that the trial court exceeded its statutory authority by improperly delegating the task of treatment to the Department of Corrections, the instant court found that there was no improper delegation of authority.

2133 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Singh


No. 45393-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1734



July 30, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 99-1-00383-1. Date filed: 10/11/1999. Judge signing: Hon. George Bowden.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was walking through a city park. He was aware that the park was an area used by some individuals to consume drugs and alcohol. Through a truck window, the officer observed defendant twice place his hands to his nostrils and snort quickly as if forcing something up his nostrils. The officer also heard defendant say to another person in the truck something to the effect "you can make as much money as you want to." Concluding that narcotics use had occurred, the officer arrested defendant. When the officer asked defendant what narcotic he had snorted, defendant replied "cocaine." On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred when it concluded that the officer had probable cause to arrest him. The instant court held that defendant's snorting action was highly consistent with the illegal consumption of narcotics and was not consistent with innocent activity. This was particularly true given that the area was known for narcotics use. The officer reasonably concluded that defendant committed a crime by inhaling illegal narcotics. Thus, substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding that probable cause existed for the officer to arrest defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2134 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Leibbrand v. Employment Sec. Dep't


No. 47149-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


107 Wn. App. 411; 27 P.3d 1186; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1557; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P9024



July 23, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant employee applied for unemployment benefits after he was terminated from his job. The appellee Washington Employment Security Department denied him benefits based on disqualifying misconduct. The Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) affirmed the denial of benefits and the employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that the last sentence of Wash. Rev. Code. § 50.20.060, which precluded a claimant from arguing as a defense to disqualification that alcoholism caused the alleged misconduct, was unconstitutional because it violated his equal protection rights. The court of appeals held that the statute was not unconstitutional because: (1) the classification did not involve a suspect class nor threaten a fundamental right; (2) the classification applied alike to all members within the designated class of alcoholics; (3) the legislature had a rational basis for the distinction suggested by the statute; and (4) the classification bore a rational relationship to the purpose of the statute. The employee also argued the record lacked substantial evidence to support the finding that he committed misconduct. The court of appeals held that the record supported the finding because it was established that the employee's presence on the job was important to meet deadlines, his repeated absences adversely affected the employer's interest in having a predictable workforce, and therefore, substantial evidence supported the determination that his absences were harmful to his employer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court was affirmed.

Cogswell v. Whatcom County


No. 47518-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1621



July 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 742.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 002002145. Date filed: 10/06/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Michael F. Moynihan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the order of the Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington) dismissing the driver's negligence action against respondent, county auditor.


OVERVIEW: The driver filed a claim for damages with the county auditor, alleging that an automobile accident he was involved in was the result of a negligently designed and maintained county road. It was undisputed that the driver filed his claim with the county auditor rather than with the clerk. The driver asserted that he filed his claim with the "governing body" of the county by filing it with the auditor and therefore complied with Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.020(2). The appellate court held that the trial court properly dismissed the driver's action because: (1) the county code clearly stated that claims against the county were to be filed with the clerk of the county council; (2) the auditor was not an agent of the "governing body" of the county; (3) the driver's reliance on a letter was unreasonable and a claim of equitable estoppel failed; and (4) the driver failed to satisfy his burden of proving impermissible vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Arbeeny


No. 25861-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1558

DISPOSITION: Reversed without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed a judgment of the Pierce County Superior Court (Washington), which convicted him of first degree trafficking in stolen property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the State violated his speedy trial rights. The State conceded that appellant's conviction was void because the statute under which appellant was charged was no longer in effect. The instant court set aside appellant's conviction. Appellant was charged and convicted of trafficking in stolen property under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.050, a section of the Criminal Profiteering Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9A.82. Because the Criminal Profiteering Act was ineffective after July 1995, including the section criminalizing trafficking in stolen property, appellant's trial and conviction were void. The speedy trial issue was moot. The proper remedy was dismissal without prejudice and to recharge and retry appellant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed without prejudice.

State v. Miles


No. 26009-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1514



July 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 8, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 25.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 98-1-04521-5. Date filed: 05/26/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Kitty-Ann Vandoorninck.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1985 defendant pleaded guilty to and was convicted of vehicular homicide in violation of former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.520 (1985). In 2000 the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, convicted him of seven counts of first-degree unlawful possession of a firearm in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The 1985 information stated three means of committing vehicular homicide, but defendant plead guilty based on driving while intoxicated. The affidavit for the search warrant showed that the confidential informant was recently inside defendant's house, saw him with and bought cocaine from him, and the informant had a track record with police. The firearms were found in defendant's house, not on his person. There was testimony that defendant was paying for the house, and the police found two bills and his bank statement addressed to defendant. There was no evidence that any of the firearms were permanently inoperable. The appellate court found that there was sufficient evidence for the jury to convict the defendant because: (1) a jury could have found that defendant exercised dominion and control over the house where the firearms were found; (2) the issuing magistrate did not abuse his discretion when he determined that the affidavit established probable cause; and (3) the defendant had reasonable notice that the causation element of the 1985 predicate offense was based on driving while intoxicated and defendant suffered no unfair prejudice.


OUTCOME: The superior court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Loggins


No. 24644-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1522



July 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 98-1-02369-6. Date filed: 04/09/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Brian M. Tollefson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of second degree murder in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington). He was sentence to life in prison without parole under the state three strikes law. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued: (1) the state could not use his out-of-state conviction as a strike unless it proved that it was constitutionally valid when entered; and (2) that one of his convictions was not a strike within the meaning of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030(31) (2001). The court of appeals held that: (1) the state could use his conviction because the defendant had not shown that the conviction had previously been found unconstitutional, or that it is unconstitutional on its face; and (2) his conviction was a strike under the state three step test because the crime he was convicted of was almost identical to the state's counterpart crime of second degree assault, the conviction had not washed out because the defendant had not remained conviction free for 10 years, and the conviction was for a most serious offense includable in his offender score.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hernandez v. Labor & Indus.


No. 19130-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


107 Wn. App. 190; 26 P.3d 977; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1505



July 12, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applied for labor and industry benefits with respondent employer. The Department of Labor and Industries (Washington) allowed the claim for medical treatment but denied the claims for additional time loss benefits, permanent partial disability, and permanent total disability. The Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals affirmed, and on review the Franklin County Superior Court dismissed the claim. The worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The superior court dismissed because the worker had failed to perfect her appeal within 30 days of the board's adverse decision by serving the board, as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 51.52.110. The court of appeals held that (1) because there was no attempt to serve the board until after the motion to dismiss was made, not only was this not substantial compliance, it was no compliance at all; (2) the worker did not claim she was in fact misled by the statutory language because of her linguistic, socio-economic, or cultural hurdles, as she was represented by counsel before, during, and after the appeal; (3) due process was satisfied, as the statute was not ambiguous about the need to serve notice of the appeal on the board; (4) conditioning judicial review of administrative actions on perfecting the appeal as prescribed did not violate equal protection; and (5) there was no disparate impact because, by providing for attorney fees, the Industrial Insurance Act did not require the average citizen to grasp statutory nuances.


OUTCOME: The superior court judgment was affirmed.

Harrison Mem. Hosp. v. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 25538-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1485



July 10, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 96-2-00955-7. Date filed: 01/07/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Karen B. Conoley.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, upon a jury verdict in favor of the respondent Department of Natural Resources (DNR), arguing that the trial court erred in instructing the jury. DNR cross-appealed following the trial court's award of attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Natural Resources (DNR) identified state trust land on Bucklin Hill in Kitsap County (Washington) as property subject to sale because of changes in the surrounding areas. Appellant hospital appealed from a jury verdict in favor of respondent, arguing that the trial court erred in instructing the jury. Respondent cross-appealed the trial court's award of attorney fees. On review, both parties requested the court to analyze the attorney fees award under the lodestar method. The court of appeals affirmed. Under the lodestar method, the court multiplied the reasonable number of hours by the reasonable rate. The party requesting fees was required to provide the trial court with records showing attorney costs. Here, DNR's records failed to show that DNR exercised billing judgment. Based upon these inadequate records and the trial court's unique ability to observe and judge each parties' work, the appellate court could not say that the trial court abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

2141 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 46669-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1492



July 9, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 5, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 70.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-09881-8. Date filed: 04/25/2000. Judge signing: Hon. William L. Downing.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The King County Superior Court (Washington) convicted defendant for possession of cocaine. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Police officers arrested defendant for obstructing a law enforcement officer and for pedestrian interference. At the scene, the officers performed a pat-down search. Then, the officers took defendant to a police station and searched him again. During this search, the officers found a substance later identified as crack cocaine in a zip-lock baggie in the inside of the bottom of defendant's pants. On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) the officers did not have probable cause to arrest him; and (2) the warrantless search, conducted at the police station, was an unlawful strip search, and the trial court therefore erred by denying his motion to suppress the cocaine found on his person during the search. The instant court held that the officers had probable cause to arrest defendant for obstruction of a law enforcement officer. The evidence supported the conclusion that defendant acted knowingly in taking action that hindered, obstructed, or delayed the officers. Whether the search during which the cocaine was found was a strip search or a search incident to defendant's arrest, it was lawful. Thus, the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress the cocaine.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Glas


No. 19111-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


106 Wn. App. 895; 27 P.3d 216; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1474



July 5, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Glas, 145 Wn.2d 1033, 43 P.3d 21, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 238 (Wash. Apr. 2, 2002).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Yakima County Superior Court (Washington) convicted defendant of violating Washington's voyeurism statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.115. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was caught photographing up women's skirts at a public shopping mall. On appeal, defendant claimed that § 9A.44.115 was constitutionally defective because it was vague as to what constituted a hostile intrusion. Defendant also argued that, looked at facially, the voyeurism statute was overbroad. The instant court concluded that the voyeurism statute passed constitutional muster. It was neither vague nor overbroad as applied or facially. The trial court applied the voyeurism statute correctly, as the photographs defendant took were ultimately destined for a pornographic internet web site. Defendant failed to articulate any First Amendment overbreadth argument. Defendant conceded that security camera surveillance and eye-level, arms-length viewing and photography did not constitute hostile intrusions under the voyeurism statute. Only photographing from certain angles was prohibited. Defendant conceded that hypothetical conduct he described, such as openly photographing or romantically gazing at people, was not outlawed by the voyeurism statute. Thus, defendant failed to suggest any protected conduct that was prohibited by the voyeurism statute.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Deman


No. 46089-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


107 Wn. App. 98; 26 P.3d 296; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1414



July 2, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied January 8, 2002, Reported at: 145 Wn.2d 1016, 41 P.3d 482, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 47.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 99-1-07411-1-KNT. Date filed in Superior Court: 1/19/00. Superior Court Judge Signing: LeRoy McCullough.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pled guilty to vehicular homicide, hit and run, and driving with a suspended license in the third degree. At sentencing, the State sought a sentence enhancement for the defendant's two prior convictions for driving under the influence. The King County Superior Court (Washington) enhanced the sentence by 48 months for the two prior convictions. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant argued that the prior convictions had "washed out" due to the passage of time, and therefore the 48 months attributable to the enhancement had to be stricken from his sentence. Defendant claimed that case law and Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.360(2) prohibited the prior convictions consideration. The court rejected the defendant's contentions. The statute relied upon by the defendant excluded the prior convictions from being used by the trial court to calculate the defendant's offender score. The trial court did not use the convictions for that purpose. Both Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9.94A.310(7), 46.61.520(2) clearly required the enhancement of a sentence for vehicular homicide to occur independently of the calculation of the defendant's standard range sentence and without regard to § 9.94A.360(2). Therefore the trial court did not err in enhancing the defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rabon v. City of Seattle

The supreme court remanded for a hearing, and the animal control manager ordered the dogs be destroyed. That decision was affirmed. In the superior court, the dog owner and the city moved for summary judgment, and the superior court dismissed the claims. The dog owner appealed.

State v. Martin


NO. 45964-3-I, NO. 46579-1-I, NO. 46879-1-I (Linked Cases)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


106 Wn. App. 850; 25 P.3d 488; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1358



June 25, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied: State v. Martin, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1774 (Wash. Ct. App. July 26, 2001).
Review or Rehearing granted: City of Everett v. Schroeder, 145 Wn.2d 1016, 41 P.3d 482, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 13 (Wash. Jan. 8, 2002).
Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Martin, 145 Wn.2d 1014, 41 P.3d 483, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 14 (Wash. Jan. 8, 2002).
Review or Rehearing granted: State v. McKinney, 145 Wn.2d 1014, 41 P.3d 483, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 16 (Wash. Jan. 8, 2002).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant drivers appealed decisions of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which concluded that a driver did not have, pursuant to Wash. Const. art. I, § 7, a reasonable expectation of privacy in his or her Department of Licensing (DOL) records that precluded law enforcement officers from searching those records without an individualized suspicion of the driver's involvement in criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: Each of the drivers argued that a police officer's search of the DOL database absent probable cause or reasonable suspicion of criminal activity violated the expectation of privacy under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7. Based on the information from the DOL database, the officers either stopped one of the drivers for driving with a suspended license or cross-referenced a criminal information database and discovered other information sufficient to justify further investigation. The instant court held that Washington drivers do not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in their DOL records. The practice complained of - i.e., the dissemination of individual licensing information to law enforcement officers - was authorized by statute. There was no evidence that the officers either improperly gained access to the drivers' license records or made improper use of the information after accessing it. The searches of the DOL database were not invasive and the information accessed was not highly personal. There was also no evidence that the officers specifically targeted the drivers for investigation based on their race, gender, physical characteristics, or for any other improper purpose.


OUTCOME: The decisions were affirmed.

State v. McKee


No. 47079-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1416



June 25, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: King. Docket No(s): 99-1-10116-9 SEA Judge Signing: William L. Downing. Date entered: July 10, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed conviction and the school zone sentence enhancement.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant challenged the judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington) which convicted the defendant for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver with a school zone enhancement pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant argued that his conviction had to be reversed due to prosecutorial misconduct in closing arguments. The defendant also argued that the school zone sentence enhancement in Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435 violated his right to due process of law because the location of the school bus stop, which he was found to be within 1,000 feet of at the time he committed the offense, was not readily ascertainable. The court rejected the defendant's contentions and affirmed the conviction and sentence enhancement. The court found that the defendant did not object to the statement he contended was misconduct when the prosecutor made it. Because a curative instruction would have cured any prejudice arising from the prosecutor's remark, even if it were misconduct, the statement did not require reversal. And because the defendant could have readily ascertained the location of the school bus stop through objective means, such as contacting the school district or observing school children waiting for a school bus, imposing the sentence enhancement did not deprive him of due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

2149 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tarvin


No. 24701-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1326



June 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied December 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 815.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 95-1-01258-4. Date filed: 05/12/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Rudolph J. Tollefson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the imposition of the weapon enhancement.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which applied a deadly weapon enhancement to his assault conviction. Appellant claimed that the 1994 amendment to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310 was not in effect when he committed the offense and the phrase "any violent offense" was ambiguous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of assault and robbery and was sentenced. He moved for resentencing, challenging the trial court's authority to impose the weapons enhancement on his assault conviction. The court denied the motion and he appealed, contending that the 1994 amendment to the statute, applying the weapon enhancement to "any violent offense," was not in effect at the time he committed the offenses or when he was sentenced. The appellate court disagreed. The legislative history did not support appellant's argument that the amendment applying the weapon enhancement never became law. The provision of a contingent expiration date clearly indicated that the legislature intended the section to become law before the vote on the tax issue, and the subsequent repeal of the amendment indicated that it was the law when appellant committed the crime. Additionally, the phrase "any violent offense" clearly included first degree assault; thus, the amendment was not ambiguous.


OUTCOME: Imposition of the weapon enhancement was affirmed.

Citizen Advocates v. Utils. & Transp.


No. 46546-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


106 Wn. App. 605; 24 P.3d 471; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1167



June 4, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied February 5, 2002, Reported at: 145 Wn.2d 1021, 41 P.3d 483, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 94. Order Denying Appellant's Motion to Reconsider July 27, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1773.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, Washington Utilities and Transportation Commission, issued a final order determining that appellant, nonprofit corporation, was a telecommunications company providing telecommunications for sale to the general public, and ordered it to cease and desist operations until it registered with the commission. The nonprofit corporation challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, King County (Washington), affirming the commission's order.


OVERVIEW: The nonprofit corporation argued that the commission did not have jurisdiction to determine whether it was a telecommunications company. The appellate court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 80.04.015 granted the commission jurisdiction. The court found that substantial evidence supported the commission's determination because it: (1) owned computers equipped with voice cards which were "facilities" as defined in Wash. Rev. Code § 80.04.010; (2) managed the use of its network features which were "telecommunications" as defined in § 80.04.010; and (3) did not operate a private telecommunications system used exclusively by it, but instead offered services essentially identical to the operations of regulated toll providers. The nonprofit corporation claimed that by classifying it as a telecommunications company, the commission violated its constitutional rights. The court found that the question of the character of the corporation was one to be determined by the evidence disclosed in the record, and contrary to its "constitutional claim," the nonprofit corporation was not being deprived of its ability to conduct business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2152 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barbee


No. 46604-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1115



May 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 740.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-08640-2. Date filed: 04/27/2000. Judge signing: Hon. William L. Downing.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed. Case remanded solely for resentencing on possession count.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) convicting him of and sentencing him for delivery and possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions of and sentences for delivery and possession of cocaine, alleging that the trial court violated his constitutional right to counsel of his choice when it failed to continue the pretrial proceedings and that certain conditions of his sentence were unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The appellate court affirmed the convictions and remanded solely for resentencing on the possession count. The trial court's decision not to continue the pretrial proceedings was not an unreasoning and arbitrary insistence upon expeditiousness, such that defendant's right to counsel of his choice was not violated. The sentencing condition prohibiting defendant from loitering in areas of known drug activity or with persons involved in such activity was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. However, the trial court had incorrectly calculated defendant's offender score for the possession conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed and the case was remanded solely for resentencing on the possession count. The trial court did not violate defendant's constitutional right to counsel of his choice when it refused to continue the pretrial proceedings, since that decision was not an unreasoning and arbitrary insistence upon expeditiousness.

Miller v. Bd. of Denture Tech., 106 Wn. App. 1002, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1852 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state board of denture technology sought review of the order of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, reversing the order denying respondent's application for a license to practice as a denturist.


OVERVIEW: Washington voters approved Initiative 607 which allowed denturists to practice without the supervision of dentists and created appellant Washington State Board of Denture Technology to oversee and regulate denturists. Under the measure, licenses were issued by the secretary of the Department of Health. Respondent applied for a license to practice as a denturist in Washington. On remand, the department was directed to determine whether the Nooksack Reservation practice requirements were substantially similar to those of Initiative 607.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

Inland Foundry v. Labor & Indus.


No. 19759-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


106 Wn. App. 333; 24 P.3d 424; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 842; 2001 OSHD (CCH) P32,356



April 24, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported in Table Case Format at: 106 Wn. App. 1002, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1852. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published May 29, 2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Department of Labor and Industries cited appellant for failing to comply with several provisions of the Washington Industrial Safety and Health Act (WISHA). The Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals upheld the citations and penalties, and the Superior Court for Spokane County (Washington) affirmed. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Respondent conducted a fatality investigation as required by WISHA. The investigation revealed that appellant violated numerous safety regulations. Each citation listed the relevant inspection dates, cited the regulation involved, and specifically stated what appellant had failed to do. The citations provided appellant with adequate information to prepare and present a defense. The citations complied with Wash. Rev. Code § 49.17.120(1). The citations were timely issued within six months of the start of the investigation. Appellant failed to make a substantive argument explaining why the regulations were vague. The findings of fact and conclusions of law made by the Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals (Board) were supported by the evidence. The fact that respondent did not stipulate to jurisdiction had no bearing on whether the Board did in fact have jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The citations were sufficiently specific to satisfy due process requirements, and the WISHA regulations were not unconstitutionally vague. The Board's findings of fact and conclusions of law were supported by substantial evidence.

Peterson v. City of Mercer Island


No. 46298-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 847



April 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1594. Petition for Review Denied December 4, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 789.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-2-01393-0. Date filed: 03/17/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Larry Jordan.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners filed suit against respondent city and respondent tavern owner, arguing that the tavern was an illegal, nonconforming use and a public nuisance. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, and the appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Appellants owned a home adjacent to a tavern. They complained to respondent city's attorney and requested abatement of the tavern, but to no avail. Appellants had no standing to enforce the repealed zoning code. The zoning code in effect at the time of suit provided a procedure for establishment of an abatement date. However, appellants never attempted to bring the matter before respondent city's planning commission. This was the sole administrative avenue of relief for a perceived violation of the zoning code. Appellants' claim against respondent city was barred by the public duty doctrine. The trial court did not err in granting summary judgment on the nuisance claim, because appellants failed to establish that claim as a matter of law. They did not show that the tavern was specially injurious to them as a result of wrongdoing.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Appellants' claims were properly dismissed. Appellants' legal theories were either unavailable to them or unsupported by admissible evidence.

2159 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Haberman


No. 23843-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


105 Wn. App. 926; 22 P.3d 264; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 822



April 20, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Thurston County Superior Court (Washington) convicted defendant for malicious harassment, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.080. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based on angry racial comments and threats he made to a grocery clerk who had refused to sell him beer the previous night when defendant appeared intoxicated. Defendant argued that: (1) the State charged him under an invalid, old law, which the legislature had amended before the incident, and (2) the trial court gave erroneous jury instructions based upon outdated statutory language. The instant court agreed with defendant. The necessary elements for the crime of malicious harassment did not appear in any form in the information charging defendant, nor could the instant court find these elements by fair construction. The information clearly charged defendant under a version of the malicious harassment law that had been significantly amended five years before the alleged offense. Charging defendant with violating an invalid law was a fundamental due process violation. The jury instructions at issue were outdated and did not provide a correct statement of the law regarding malicious harassment. The "to-convict" instruction not only stated the wrong crime, but it also allowed the jury to convict defendant for conduct that was no longer a crime.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed.

State v. Schmitz


No. 45508-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 799



April 16, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1399.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 99-1-00446-3. Date filed: 11/01/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Joseph Thibodeau.



DISPOSITION: Schmitz's convictions affirmed, his community placement sentence reversed, and remanded for correction of the judgment and sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) of first degree burglary with a firearm enhancement. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for first degree burglary and an accompanying firearm enhancement, alleging error in the jury instructions, and challenging the finding that he was armed during the burglary. The court of appeals affirmed the convictions, holding that the challenged instruction clearly informed jurors that they could find appellant was armed with a deadly weapon only if they also found that he stole a firearm during the burglary and the firearm was easily accessible and readily available for use. The jury was free to make that finding based on the evidence presented, and the instruction contained no unconstitutional permissive inference. Second, there was no ineffective assistance by appellant's counsel, who properly declined to pursue the theory that appellant did not know there were guns among the property appellant was caught stealing. The court reversed appellant's community placement sentence under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(9)(a) (1999), because there was no evidence that he committed a crime against a person by during the burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions but reversed his community placement sentence, and remanded for correction of the judgment and sentence.

United Development v. Mill Creek


No. 45882-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


106 Wn. App. 681; 26 P.3d 943; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 802



April 16, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals June 5, 2001.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported in Table Case Format at: 105 Wn. App. 1053, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1401. Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 145 Wn.2d 1002, 35 P.3d 380, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 700. Order Granting Award of Attorney Fees June 5, 2001, Reported at: 106 Wn. App. 681, 26 P.3d 943, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1317. Order Changing Opinion June 5, 2001. Order Granting Motion to Publish June 5, 2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subdivision developer challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) which affirmed respondent's imposition of mitigation fees for the impacts of the subdivision on traffic and parks. Respondent cross-appealed from the decision that certain drainage improvements sought to be imposed by respondent were not justified.


OVERVIEW: Appellant subdivision developer contested a decision of the trial court affirming respondent city's imposition of mitigation fees for impacts on traffic and public parks. Respondent city cross-appealed from the decision that certain drainage improvements sought to be imposed by respondent were not justified. Properly asserting that a developer could not be required to mitigate the same impact twice, appellant alleged that all traffic and park impacts for the subdivision were mitigated in earlier stages of the development process. Appellant also alleged that the assessments did not accurately reflect the impact of the development. The appellate court affirmed the trial court in all respects. Traffic and park impacts for appellant's subdivision were not mitigated in earlier stages of the development process. Respondent was not required to have considered the effect of certain private recreational facilities to which subdivision residents had access when it measured the impact of the subdivision on public parks. However, the subdivision had no effect upon drainage at the relevant location.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision was affirmed in all respects. In assessing mitigation fees for a subdivision's impact on public parks, respondent city did not have to consider the effect of certain private recreational facilities to which subdivision residents had access.

Citizens v. Chelan County


No. 17795-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


105 Wn. App. 753; 21 P.3d 304; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 586



April 10, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Chelan County (Washington) which affirmed the decision of the Chelan County Board of Commissioners approving the respondent landowners' revised plan.


OVERVIEW: The association contended that the landowners' proposed subdivision was "urban growth" and was therefore prohibited under both the Growth Management Act (GMA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.70A (1994), and Chelan County, Wash., Res. 93-122. The appellate court found that because the landowners' subdivision was located outside of Chelan County's interim urban growth area, the subdivision could not be "urban." The court determined that the question was whether the findings of fact were supported by substantial evidence, and if they were, whether the factual findings, in turn, supported the legal conclusions. Because the board approved the landowners' plan based on the fact that it was consistent with other previously approved subdivisions, the court remanded to the board to independently evaluate the subdivision, and determine whether it was urban according to the laws in force when the landowners filed their application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded to the board for entry of findings of fact and conclusions of law on whether the subdivision was urban.

In re Det. of C.W.


No. 44635-5-I Consolidated with No. 44938-9-I, No. 45506-1-I, No. 45181-2-I, No. 44939-7-I, No. 45719-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


105 Wn. App. 718; 20 P.3d 1052; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 582



April 9, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted: In re Det. of C.W., 145 Wn.2d 1007, 37 P.3d 290, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 763 (Wash. Dec. 4, 2001).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, respondents were hospitalized after notice by emergency room (ER) staff that each respondent needed to be evaluated for mental illness. Prior to the 72-hour period prescribed by Wash. Rev. Code § 71.05.150, a county designated mental health professional (CDMHP) petitioned for 14-day involuntary treatment. The King County Superior Court (Washington) granted respondents' motions to dismiss the petitions. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: At issue was the timeliness of detention of each respondent by the CDMHP after notice by hospitals' ER staff, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.05.050, that each respondent needed to be further evaluated for mental illness. Respondents also challenged, on due process grounds, the constitutionality of the statute. The instant court held that the six-hour period specified in the statute began to run from the time the ER staff determined that an evaluation by the CDMHP was necessary. The instant court concluded that the statute satisfied the due process challenge made, provided that the State met its burden to justify, by a preponderance of the evidence, any delay between a person's arrival at an ER and the determination by professional staff that it was necessary to notify the CDMHP to take action. The instant court rejected respondents' contention that the six-hour period began as soon as one was either restrained in the ER or no longer required medical treatment. The instant court found no due process violation for four of the cases, and reversed the orders of dismissal as to them, but it found insufficient evidence to justify the detentions in two of the cases.


OUTCOME: The instant court reversed the orders of dismissal as to four of the respondents, but it vacated the orders of dismissal as to the two respondents in which it found insufficient evidence to justify their detentions.

Knight v. Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs., Div. of Child Support


No. 46753-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 531



April 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 734. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1263.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-2-22195-8. Date filed: 05/12/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Harriett M. Cody.
Knight v. Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs., 105 Wn. App. 1040, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1263 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father filed an appeal of the order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) granting the motion for summary judgment by respondent Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS).


OVERVIEW: The father accrued a debt for past due child support since 1995. The father filed suit in 1997 after receiving a license suspension warning letter from DSHS. The superior court granted the summary judgment motion by DSHS. Ultimately the appeal was dismissed, and the court of appeals issued a mandate to the superior court. In 1999, DSHS sent the father another warning letter, and the father filed the instant action. The appellate court held that res judicata barred the suit because: (1) the state's interest in enforcing child support orders would be impaired by varying results across successive suits; (2) the evidence in each suit was virtually the same; (3) the father sought to protect his interest in his driver's license in each suit; and (4) the father challenged the same statute in both suits on identical grounds so the same transactional nucleus of facts gave rise to his claim. The court determined that even if it regarded each warning letter as providing a separate cause of action to make res judicata claim preclusion inappropriate, collateral estoppel barred the father's claim because there was no significant change in the legal climate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Morgan v. City of Edmonds


No. 47414-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 536



April 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 830. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1266.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 98-2-05743-1. Date filed: 04/04/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth Cowsert.
Morgan v. City of Edmonds, 105 Wn. App. 1041, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1266 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sued respondent for damages for personal injuries. The Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) dismissed the claim on summary judgment, based on appellant's failure to comply with Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.020. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was hit by a car immediately after she exited a bus operated by respondent, an independent municipal corporation. She sued respondent and defendant city for damages. The trial court dismissed the claim against respondent, because appellant did not file a notice of claim before initiating her tort action, as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.020. On appeal, the appellant argued that she substantially complied with the statute by making a good faith effort to file her notice. The court of appeals affirmed, holding that respondent did not mislead appellant by informing her there was no preprinted form to be used in filing a notice of claim, and strict compliance with claim filing procedures was required. Second, respondent was not estopped from raising the defense of failure to file a claim, as it raised the defense in its answer three months after appellant filed her complaint and five weeks before the statute of limitations extinguished her claim. Finally, appellant was not denied due process; when respondent filed its answer raising the claim filing defense, appellant was on notice that further investigation was required.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of respondent was affirmed.

2167 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Silverdale Water Dist. v. Bucklin Hill, Inc.


No. 25320-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 499



March 30, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 93-2-02735-6. Date filed: 11/05/1999.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) entered a declaratory judgment in favor of appellee water district, after concluding that Wash. Rev. Code § 35.51.040 did not apply to utility local improvement districts (ULIDs) and revenue bonds. Appellant property owners claimed appellee was not entitled to retain the reserve funds.


OVERVIEW: Appellee formed a ULID to finance construction of a water supply system to benefit appellant property owners. A special assessment was levied on appellants. The lower court erroneously determined that appellee was entitled to retain the reserve fund, even though the construction was completed and the bonds retired. Appellee created the reserve fund in order to secure payment of the principal and interest on an issue of local improvement bonds. The 1987 amendment to Wash. Rev. Code § 35.51.040 required that appellee return the reserve fund to appellants, whose assessments created this fund. Because § 35.51.040 directed that appellee refund the reserve fund after retirement of the bonds, appellee was required to follow this mandate. Return of the funds did not constitute a gift of those funds, but rather a return of appellants' money after it was no longer needed to fund the special benefit.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed. Local improvement bonds encompassed bonds payable from ULID assessments because it was a type of local improvement district. It was not a gift of public funds to return the reserve to appellants.

 

2168 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Locklear


No. 24529-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


105 Wn. App. 555; 20 P.3d 993; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 509



March 30, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, which convicted him of a drive-by shooting in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.04.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a passenger in a car. When it stopped, he got out, walked two blocks, and fired a gun at an occupied house. He was convicted of a drive-by shooting, which required that he fire the gun either from a motor vehicle or from the immediate area of a motor vehicle that was used to transport him or the firearm, or both, to the scene of the discharge. Appellant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to these facts. The appellate court found that a person of common intelligence had no way of knowing, without guessing, whether a citizen who discharged a gun two blocks away from a motor vehicle was discharging the gun "from the immediate area" of the motor vehicle. Further, the appellate court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.045 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of this case.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was reversed.

 

2169 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Silverdale Water Dist. v. Bucklin Hill, Inc.


No. 25320-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 499



March 30, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 93-2-02735-6. Date filed: 11/05/1999.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, entered a declaratory judgment in favor of appellee water district, after concluding that Wash. Rev. Code § 35.51.040 did not apply to utility local improvement districts (ULIDs) and revenue bonds. Appellant property owners claimed appellee was not entitled to retain the reserve funds.


OVERVIEW: Appellee formed a ULID to finance construction of a water supply system to benefit appellant property owners. A special assessment was levied on appellants. The lower court erroneously determined that appellee was entitled to retain the reserve fund, even though the construction was completed and the bonds retired. Appellee created the reserve fund in order to secure payment of the principal and interest on an issue of local improvement bonds. The 1987 amendment to Wash. Rev. Code § 35.51.040 required that appellee return the reserve fund to appellants, whose assessments created this fund. Because § 35.51.040 directed that appellee refund the reserve fund after retirement of the bonds, appellee was required to follow this mandate. Return of the funds did not constitute a gift of those funds, but rather a return of appellants' money after it was no longer needed to fund the special benefit.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed. Local improvement bonds encompassed bonds payable from ULID assessments because it was a type of local improvement district. It was not a gift of public funds to return the reserve to appellants.

 

2170 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Dependency of Q.L.M.


No. 48026-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


105 Wn. App. 532; 20 P.3d 465; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 497



March 28, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Department of Social and Health Services, sought to release respondent's juvenile court psychological and treatment records to the state prosecutor, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.025. The King County (Washington) Superior Court entered a protective order and limited dissemination of the information to the Division of Children and Family Services. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, a juvenile offender living in a group home under the supervision of appellant department of social services, pleaded guilty to two counts of fourth degree sexual assault, and was committed to a sex offender rehabilitation program. In anticipation of his release, a sentence review board referred the case to the prosecutor's office to consider filing a sexually violent predator petition under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.025. Respondent sought injunctive relief, arguing that the release of his records conflicted with the policy of confidentiality in the dependency and child welfare statutes. The trial court granted a permanent injunction, forbidding the prosecutor from using or disseminating any documents from respondent's dependency proceedings. The court of appeals reversed, holding there was no conflict between the dependency statute, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 13.50, allowing the prosecutor access to dependency files, and § 71.09.025. Appellant failed to demonstrate any right to confidentiality that could contravene the clear mandate of § 71.09.025.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was reversed.

 

2171 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


McLane Co. v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 25661-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


105 Wn. App. 409; 19 P.3d 1119; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 467



March 23, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 145 Wn.2d 1005, 35 P.3d 381, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 732.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants (distributors of tobacco products) appealed from a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) granting summary judgment to respondent, the Washington State Department of Revenue, in a case challenging respondent's interpretation of Washington's Other Tobacco Products tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellants petitioned for a tax refund. The tax was imposed upon the sale, use, consumption, handling, or distribution of tobacco products in Washington. Wash. Rev. Code § 82.26.020(1). The tax was imposed only on distributors, and one of the statutory definitions of distributor was a person who brought, or caused to be brought, tobacco products into Washington for sale. Wash. Rev. Code § 82.26.010(3). Respondent reasoned that appellants caused the tobacco products to be brought into the state when they placed an order with an out-of-state supplier, and because they handled or distributed the products in Washington, they were liable for the tax. The trial court agreed, and granted summary judgment to respondent. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the tax was not an unconstitutional tax against interstate commerce. Under the plain language of the statutes, an in-state distributor was a person engaged in the business of selling tobacco products in Washington whose tobacco products were to be brought into the state for sale. Appellants were responsible for paying the tax, and the trial court did not err by granting summary judgment in respondent's favor.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting summary judgment in favor of respondent was affirmed.

 

2172 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Cherry v. State (In re Cherry)


No. 25280-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 472



March 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 2, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 666. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1208.
Related proceeding at In re Det. of Cherry, 2011 Wash. App. LEXIS 2564 (Wash. Ct. App., Sept. 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Mason County. Docket No: 99-2-00218-4. Date filed: 10/20/1999. Judge signing: Hon. James B. Sawyer II.
In re Det. of Cherry, 105 Wn. App. 1026, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1208 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant received a sentence of 120 months for second degree rape. One day before the expiration of his sentence, respondent filed a petition under the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09, in the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington), seeking appellant's involuntary civil commitment. Respondent's petition was granted, and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Respondent sought appellant's civil commitment as a sexually violent predator, based on diagnoses of sexual sadism and paraphilia NOS (rape). Commitment of a sexually violent predator, under Wash. Rev. Code, ch. 71.09, was not criminal incarceration, so appellant could not raise double jeopardy or ex post facto claims. The legislature could accord fewer due process protections to persons committed as sexually violent predators than to those otherwise involuntarily committed for treatment. To be entitled to the appointment of a second expert witness, at public expense, appellant had to demonstrate good cause under Wash. Admin. Code § 275-156-010(3), and appellant failed to establish such cause. Appellant was entitled to appointed counsel, but, applying the Strickland standards to counsel's effectiveness, appellant failed to show he suffered any prejudice from his counsel's performance due to counsel's failure to raise invalid evidentiary objections or to discover, pre-trial, that his expert agreed with the diagnosis of paraphilia NOS (rape). Counsel's failure to move for reconsideration of the trial court's denial of his request for a second expert was also not prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The trial court's commitment of appellant as a sexually violent predator was affirmed because such commitment was not criminal incarceration, appellant did not have to be afforded all the due process protections provided others involuntarily committed for treatment, he did not show cause for a second expert witness, and his counsel's representation was effective.

Medina v. Public Util. Dist. No. 1


No. 19435-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 431



March 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 1036.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 98-2-00367-4. Judge signing: CRAIG MATHESON. Date filed: June 8, 1999.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Benton County (Washington) dismissing appellants' lawsuit on summary judgment for failure to wait 60 days before filing their suit, as required under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.020.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband was injured by a truck that was owned by appellee, a public utility district, and was driven by appellee's employee. Appellant husband and wife filed a claim with appellee, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.020. Appellee denied the claim. Appellants filed a complaint 57 days later. Appellee answered, and nine days later, filed an amended answer. The amended answer raised the defense that appellants failed to wait the 60 days required by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.020(4). Appellee moved for summary judgment, which the court granted, dismissing the claim. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal. Strict compliance with the filing procedures was required. Appellee's rejection of the claim prior to the end of the 60-day waiting period did not amount to a waiver. Although appellants asserted that appellee should have been precluded from asserting the 60-day violation as a defense based on laches and equitable estoppel, they failed to show prejudice, damage, or manifest injustice. The statute did not violate appellant's equal protection or due process rights, and thus was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of appellants' lawsuit was affirmed.

 

2174 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nemitz


No. 18680-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


105 Wn. App. 205; 19 P.3d 480; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 413



March 13, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: District Court Name and County: SPOKANE COUNTY. District Court: Docket No. CB009367. Date filed in District Court: October 15, 2000. District Court Judge signing: DONNA WILSON


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the district court of driving under the influence. The Spokane County Superior Court (Washington) affirmed the conviction. Appellant claimed his due process rights were violated when a juror who could not understand English was excluded. He also claimed a motion in limine should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: At appellant's trial, the judge refused to provide an interpreter and excluded a prospective juror who had trouble understanding spoken English. The jury selection complied with the English-only restriction for jurors in Wash. Rev. Code § 2.36.070(4). Appellant's motion in limine to exclude all reference to a card he had been given by his attorney outlining what to do in the event of an arrest was denied. Appellant's due process rights were circumvented when the prosecutor asked him what was written on the card. There was no probative value to the information contained on the lawyer's card. The only value of the card was its inference that only a person disposed to drink and drive would take anticipatory steps to avoid self-incrimination. To invite the inference of guilt from the exercise of constitutional rights was impermissible.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirming the conviction was reversed. Appellant had no constitutional right to a non-English-speaking juror, but his due process rights were violated when the prosecutor questioned him about the contents of the card he was given by his attorney. Motion in limine should have been granted.

State v. Knox


No. 19082-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 386



March 6, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 99-1-00511-3. Judge signing: TARI EITZEN. Date filed: January 26, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of the County of Spokane (Washington) that convicted him of first degree rape of a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for first degree rape of a child. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by concluding that the child was competent to testify, as she had the ability to perceive the events at the time they occurred and could relate them truly. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the child's out-of-court statements regarding the sexual assault, as such statements, made by a child younger than 10 years old, was admissible in a criminal proceeding, as the court found that the time, content, and circumstances of the statement provided sufficient indicia of reliability. The trial court did not err in declining to give defendant's proposed jury instruction on alternative means of committing the crime, as defendant failed to demonstrate how his proposed instruction added anything beyond what was contained in the trial court's Petrich instruction. Finally, in the absence of an argument by defendant specifically addressing the four Fain factors, the court declined to hold the sentence was unconstitutionally cruel or unusual by labeling defendant a persistent offender.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Wells v. Whatcom County Water Dist.


No. 47262-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


105 Wn. App. 143; 19 P.3d 453; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 370



March 5, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a county hearing examiner approved a conditional use permit, respondents, opponents of the project, filed a land use petition in the Skagit County Superior Court (Washington). The trial court agreed that the examiner erred by refusing to require a supplemental environmental impact statement (SEIS). Appellant water district sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought a conditional use permit (CUP) for a sewer interceptor. Respondents challenged the permit decision under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C of the Land Use Petition Act (LUPA). The trial court remanded for completion of an SEIS and reconsideration of the CUP. The court on appeal affirmed the hearing examiner's ruling rejecting respondents' Wash. Rev. Code § 43.21C.080 of State Environmental Policy Act (SEPA), request for two reasons. First, the information respondents relied on did not qualify as new information under the SEPA regulations. Second, respondents' challenge was untimely because they failed to file a LUPA petition within the time allowed by Wash. Rev. Code § 43.21C.080. Respondents did not show a substantial change in the proposal, or an impact previously identified as needing further evaluation. The CUP decision was not based on considerations beyond the hearing examiner's authority.


OUTCOME: The hearing examiner's decision approving the CUP was reinstated. Even if the interim agreement qualified as new information, neither the examiner nor the trial court could properly order an SEIS because the issue was time-barred. Hearing examiner's mention of landowners' property rights did not merit relief under LUPA's standards.

State v. Beagles


No. 44135-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 377



March 5, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 2, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 670.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 98-1-00738-5. Date filed: 02/08/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Linda Lau.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the conviction entered in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) for second degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with second degree assault after he shot the victim during an altercation. After unequivocally asserting his intent to proceed pro se at trial, defendant realized he made a mistake, and near the end of trial, requested a continuance so that his new counsel could prepare his case. The trial judge denied the motion, and the defendant was found guilty. The appellate court affirmed. The trial court did not err by giving a self-defense jury instruction or by denying defendant's motion for a new trial on that issue. The "no duty to retreat" instruction was not supported by the evidence; thus the trial court could properly refuse to give it, and defendant's constitutional rights were not violated, or did the trial court err by giving an aggressor instruction. Also, the trial court did not err in refusing defendant's severance request. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding defendant's expert's testimony, or did the trial court err by applying a firearm enhancement to defendant's second degree assault conviction, because it did not result in double punishment.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, because the lower court did not err in the instruction of the jury, in denying defendant's request for severance, by excluding defendant's expert's testimony, and in sentencing defendant.

State v. Lusby


No. 18869-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


105 Wn. App. 257; 18 P.3d 625; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 346



March 1, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 10, 2001, Reported at: 144 Wn.2d 1005, 29 P.3d 718, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 477.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Asotin County (Washington), convicting her of possession of marijuana with intent to deliver and sentencing her for that offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction of and sentence for possession of marijuana with intent to deliver. Defendant alleged that the trial court abused its discretion when it denied her motion to compel the State to reveal the identity of a confidential informant, that the trial court erred by applying a Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(a)(6) "drug-free zone" sentencing enhancement because the statutory provision was violative of equal protection, and that the trial court failed to recognize it had discretion to order work ethic camp (WEC). The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded for resentencing in order to allow the trial court to exercise its discretion as to whether to sentence defendant to work ethic camp. Disclosure of the identity of the confidential informant was not necessary because defendant had admitted that she sold drugs of the type found in her home. Section 69.50.435(a)(6) applied equally to any offender and did not violate equal protection. The trial court was mistaken in its belief that WEC was unavailable to defendant due to the 1999 amendment to the applicable statute.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed and case was remanded for resentencing in order to allow trial court to exercise its discretion as to whether to sentence defendant to work ethic camp. Statutory provision providing for "drug-free zone" sentencing enhancement applied equally to any offender and did not violate equal protection.

 

2179 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duncan


No. 46174-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 354



February 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted October 2, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 633.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 99-1-08665-8. Date filed: 02/22/2000. Judge signing: Hon. Patricia Hall Clark.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent was charged with unlawful possession of a firearm, possession of a stolen firearm, and possession of stolen property. Respondent moved to suppress the evidence in his possession. The Superior Court, King County (Washington), suppressed the evidence on the ground that the police lacked authority to make the arrest which led to the discovery of the evidence, and dismissed the case.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the initial detention of the respondent for possession of an open beer container was not legitimate. On appeal, Appellant State argued that the trial court erred by applying a proof by a preponderance of the evidence standard to the officer's initial detention when the appropriate standard is whether there was a reasonable articulable suspicion. The court held that the trial court erred in granting the motion to suppress. The evidence that the a beer was within the reach of the respondent, was cold to the touch, and that an officer detected the odor of alcohol on the respondent's breath was sufficient to warrant a person of reasonable caution to believe the respondent had committed the civil infraction of possession of the open beer container in public. As a result, the initial stop of the respondent was proper, and therefore police had authority to search the respondent. The officers did not have to have evidence sufficient to prove every element of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt to possess probable cause for arrest.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. The court held that because the trial court erred in finding the initial detention invalid, it erred in granting the motion to suppress. The evidence that respondent had possession of the beer was sufficient to allow police to believe the respondent had committed an infraction, and therefore the initial detention was valid. The suppression order was reversed and the case was remanded for trial.
