State v. Peck


No. 19324-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 279



February 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 601.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 99-1-01761-8. Judge signing: RICHARD SCHROEDER. Date filed: May 9, 2000. Reported in table case format at 104 Wn. App. 1050, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 886.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which convicted her of felony hit and run in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.52.020 (1990).


OVERVIEW: On a dark, rainy night, appellant struck a pedestrian dressed in dark clothing, who she did not see crossing the street in the middle of the block. Appellant did not stop her vehicle, even though it sustained significant damage to its windshield, because she assumed she had hit something that had fallen from a truck that was traveling in the lane ahead of her. Appellant contended on appeal that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because a person of ordinary understanding would have to guess at the meaning of the term "accident," and the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction. The appellate court found that the term "accident" was unambiguous as applied to the facts of the case. The appellate court further found that the circumstances were sufficient for a rational jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that a reasonable person in appellant's situation would have known that she had been involved in an accident; therefore the verdict was supported by sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Taylor


No. 24646-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 296



February 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 695.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 98-1-00061-1. Date filed: 06/22/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Grant L. Anderson. Reported in table case format at 104 Wn. App. 1052, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 296.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Taylor's convictions and sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) convicted appellant of attempted rape, assault, and unlawful imprisonment. On appeal, she claimed, inter alia, that the trial court erred in (1) requiring her to wear shackles during trial, (2) sustaining objections to the defense's questioning of her expert, (3) commenting on the evidence, (4) instructing the jury, and (5) calculating her offender score.


OVERVIEW: Although appellant raised several claims of error, the appellate court found no prejudice requiring reversal. The trial court did err in deferring to correctional officers regarding the use of shackles, and therefore failed to properly exercise its discretion on the record with an appropriate factual basis. Although appellant was restrained during her trial, there was no indication that the jury saw her in shackles. Due to the overwhelming evidence that supported the convictions, any error in regard to the shackling was harmless. Appellant also failed to show: (1) the trial court erred in sustaining objections to defense questions to her expert witness; (2) error due to impeachment of the expert witness with matters from another case to show bias; (3) a statement by the judge was improper comment on the evidence; (4) manifest constitutional error regarding two jury instructions, to which she failed to object; (5) the jury considered an uncharged offense due to a typographical error on the verdict form; (6) abuse of discretion in how appellant's offenses were counted in calculating her offender score; (7) counsel was deficient; or (8) cumulative error.


OUTCOME: The appellant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Rafn Co. v. Labor & Indus.


No. 25575-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


104 Wn. App. 947; 17 P.3d 711; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 289



February 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

As corrected by 173 Wn. App. errata.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 10, 2001, Reported at: 144 Wn.2d 1006, 29 P.3d 719, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 509.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent department of labor attempted to collect industrial insurance premiums from appellant for temporary workers employed by the appellant pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 51.16.060. Appellant filed suit alleging the statute unconstitutionally violated procedural and substantive due process. Both parties moved for summary judgment. The Superior Court, Thurston County (Washington) granted the respondent's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the statute was unconstitutional because it arbitrarily imposed liability on employers for the debts of others. The statute made the appellant statutorily liable for the industrial insurance premiums of temporary workers. The appellant's liability was secondary to that of the temporary help company. Therefore, the court found that the statute was not arbitrary. Appellant also challenged the statute on economic substantive due process grounds, arguing that although the ends the respondent sought to effect were permissible, the means used were unduly oppressive and not reasonably necessary. The court rejected this argument, because the appellant's assertions addressed the wisdom of the statute, not its constitutionality. Because the appellant failed to analyze the Gunwall criteria or to present argument or analysis on the subject, the court declined to consider appellant's due process claims under the state constitution.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The court found that the statute, which required the appellant to pay the industrial insurance premiums of temporary workers when the temporary help company failed to pay, violated neither procedural nor substantive due process. The statute did not impose an arbitrary liability on the appellant, and appellant's economic due process arguments only addressed the wisdom of the statute.

 

2183 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neill


No. 45163-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


104 Wn. App. 850; 17 P.3d 682; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 250



February 12, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted September 5, 2001, Reported at: 144 Wn.2d 1008, 31 P.3d 1185, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 565.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Whatcom County (Washington) Superior Court held that evidence of cocaine found in respondent's car was the result of an illegal seizure. Appellant, the State of Washington, sought review.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was charged with possession of cocaine after an officer asked respondent to step out of his car for a pat-down search. The officer immediately saw a "cook spoon" in the car and, investigating further, found the cocaine. The trial court suppressed the cocaine because the officer's request for identification was made absent any articulable suspicion of criminal activity. The court of appeals reversed, holding a seizure occurred when the officer asked respondent to step out of the car for a pat-down search for identification, and this seizure was reasonable because of the nexus with respondent's admitted criminal activity of driving on a suspended license and the need to properly identify respondent. The officer then saw the cook spoon in plain view. The officer had probable cause to arrest respondent at that point for possession of a controlled substance (the residue on the spoon). Although the officer did not arrest respondent until after the search of the vehicle, the arrest and search were reasonably contemporaneous. Thus, the search did not violate Wash. Const. art. 1, § 7, because it was incident to arrest.


OUTCOME: Trial court's suppression of the evidence was reversed. The pat-down search of respondent was reasonable in light of his suspended license and lack of identification; the officer then saw drug residue and was justified in searching the vehicle, and the subsequent arrest was reasonably contemporaneous to the search.

In re Visitation Rights of Clay


No. 45867-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 270



February 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 791.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 93-3-03261-9. Date filed: 12/13/1999. Judge signing: Hon. George Bowden.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded to trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for visitation with respondent's child. The petition was dismissed and respondent was awarded attorney's fees. The case was remanded after an appeal for a determination of whether attorney's fees were warranted on appeal. The Superior Court, Snohomish County (Washington) awarded respondent fees for the appeal, but did not enter any written findings of fact or conclusions of law in support of its decision.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant argued that the trial court committed reversible error by failing to articulate specific reasons for the amount of the award or to enter written findings of fact or conclusions of law to support the award of attorney's fees. Because the trial court failed to develop an adequate record upon which to review the fee award, the court remanded for entry of proper findings of fact and conclusions of law as to the reasonableness of the claimed fees. Based on the extremely limited record, the court could not determine how the trial court concluded that the respondent was entitled to fees, or that the appellant had the ability to pay. The court was unable to determine whether the trial court considered whether any of the fees charged by respondent's counsel were unnecessary or duplicative, or whether the fees were reasonable. Additionally, the court could not determine how the trial court arrived at the amount of fees, particularly in light of the fact that the billing records reflected fees of less than half that amount.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court reversed the portion of the fee award awarding respondent fees for the appeal and remanded to the trial court for the entry of proper findings of fact and conclusions of law. The trial court was directed to make specific findings of fact and conclusions of law regarding the respondent's financial need for reimbursement of attorney's fees, and appellant's ability to pay.

State v. Grant


No. 19032-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


104 Wn. App. 715; 17 P.3d 674; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 231



February 8, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State submitted a citation as appellant's charging document for driving while intoxicated. The Spokane County Superior Court (Washington) reversed his conviction after ruling the citation failed to charge all the elements of the alternatives of the crime. The State sought discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by citation with driving while intoxicated. The citation contained the blood-alcohol content readings, and listed Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502, Driving While Intoxicated. Appellant objected to an instruction that included two alternatives. The lower court found the complaint was deficient for failing to include the necessary elements of the alternate means that were included in the jury instructions. However, the citation contained all the necessary elements for charging any of the alternatives for committing the offense of driving while intoxicated. Appellant was clearly put on notice that he could have faced any one or more of the three alternate means of committing the crime.


OUTCOME: Lower court's judgment was reversed and the district court's judgment and sentence were reinstated. Liberal standard of review was appropriate, and the statutory citation and the statement "Driving While Intoxicated" contained the necessary facts of the offense.

State v. Land


No. 23822-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 204



February 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 10, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 508.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 98-1-01190-8. Date filed: 10/01/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Christine A. Pomeroy. Reported in table case format at 104 Wn. App. 1035, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 736.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction in the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) for two counts of assault in the second degree while armed with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with assault in the second degree while armed with a deadly weapon. The jury rejected his theory of self-defense and found him guilty. Defendant appealed, arguing that there was insufficient evidence to support the jury's finding of no self-defense. He also alleged that the trial court erred by excluding evidence about the victims' possible gang affiliation, by refusing to allow him to recall a witness, and in instructing the jury. The appellate court affirmed. The trial court did not violate defendant's constitutional right to confront witnesses when it refused to permit him to: (1) introduce the portion of a report that referred to "suspected gang members," and (2) inquire into the victims' possible gang affiliations. Nor did the trial court violate defendant's right of compulsory process and right to a full and fair hearing, including the right to cross-examine witnesses, when the court ruled that comments made to another inmate were inadmissible hearsay. Further, the jury was properly instructed, and the evidence was sufficient to prove the absence of self-defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, since the lower court did not violate defendant's constitutional right to confront witnesses, right to a fair trial, and right to cross-examine witnesses.

State v. Robinson


No. 46141-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


104 Wn. App. 657; 17 P.3d 653; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 120



January 29, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 30, 2001, Reported at: 145 Wn.2d 1002, 35 P.3d 380, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 690.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contested a decision of the Superior Court of Skagit County (Washington) denying her motion to withdraw her guilty plea because it was untimely pursuant to the Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1) one-year time limitation for collateral attacks.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a motion to withdraw her guilty plea to charges of robbery in the first degree with a deadly weapon enhancement, burglary in the first degree, and kidnapping in the first degree. The trial court denied the motion on the basis that it was untimely pursuant to the Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1) one-year time limitation for collateral attacks. Appellant challenged that determination, contending that her motion should have been considered as timely filed because it was mailed in sufficient time to ordinarily reach the trial court within the time frame established by § 10.73.090(1), that the trial court should have considered the merits of her motion under the doctrine of substantial compliance, and that equitable tolling should have applied. The appellate court affirmed. As to appellant's mailing related argument, courts did not have the authority to waive statutory limitation periods. Also, filing after a statutory time limit could not be considered to have been actual filing within the time limit. Finally, appellant's situation did not support application of equitable tolling.


OUTCOME: Trial court's denial of appellant's motion to withdraw her guilty plea was affirmed. Doctrine of substantial compliance was inapplicable to appellant's filing of motion to withdraw guilty plea, as filing after a statutory time limit could not be considered to have been actual filing within the time limit.

Chinatown-Int'l Dist./Save Lane St. v. City of Seattle


No. 46138-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 137



January 29, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 677.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 98-2-26459-4. Date filed: 07/14/1999. Judge signing: Hon. Kathleen J. Learned.



DISPOSITION: The hearing examiner's decision is affirmed, and attorney fees awarded to the City of Seattle and Uwajimaya.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seattle, Washington City Council voted to vacate a portion of a street as part of a development project by respondents. An administrative hearing examiner affirmed, and plaintiff sought review under the Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.70C. The Superior Court of King County upheld the approvals. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondents obtained approval from a city's land use and neighborhoods departments for vacation of a portion of a street. Appellants, member of a non-profit corporation, opposed the action. A hearing examiner and the trial court affirmed the decision. The court of appeals also affirmed, holding that (1) the issue was ripe for review of a final agency action; (2) respondent was free to proceed with the categorically-exempt street vacation before obtaining environmental review of its larger development proposal; (3) there was substantial evidence supporting the finding that vacating a portion of the street would have no probable significant adverse impact on traffic circulation; (4) the project was not the introduction of a completely new type of use into the area that would significantly change the utilization of the two contiguous blocks, so the special review board had no duty to consider alternatives to vacating the street; and (5) respondents prevailed in all major respects, and were therefore entitled to attorney fees on appeal.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment and administrative ruling affirmed, because (1) the issue was ripe for review; (2) respondent was not required to first obtain environmental review of its larger development proposal; (3) evidence indicated no significant adverse impact on traffic; (4) the review board had no duty to consider alternatives; and (5) respondents were entitled to attorney fees on appeal.

Skamania County v. Woodall


No. 25204-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


104 Wn. App. 525; 16 P.3d 701; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 113



January 26, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 2, 2001, Reported at: 144 Wn.2d 1021, 34 P.3d 1232, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 651. Certiorari Denied April 1, 2002, Reported at: 535 U.S. 967, 122 S. Ct. 1459, 152 L. Ed. 2d 378, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2316.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Columbia River Gorge Commission held that prior owners of a mobile home park had forfeited their nonconforming use because they had discontinued using the site for over one year. The Superior Court of Skamania County (Washington) affirmed respondent commission's ruling. Appellant county sought review.


OVERVIEW: The Skamania County, Washington, Department of Planning and Community Development approved an application to run a mobile home park in a Special Management Area of the Columbia River Gorge, finding that it had been a mobile home park prior to the new zoning rules, and thus was a valid nonconforming use. Respondent neighboring landowner appealed. The Skamania County Board of Adjustment ruled that Washington law required a person seeking to prove that a land occupier had discontinued a nonconforming use to prove that the land occupier intended to discontinue that use. Respondent Columbia River Gorge Commission ruled that the term "discontinued" did not contain an intent element. The superior court affirmed respondent commission, and appellant county sought review. The instant court reversed and remanded to respondent commission. Under the Columbia River Gorge National Scenic Area Act of 1986, 16 U.S.C.S. § 544-544p, and the Columbia River Gorge Compact, respondent commission was required to apply Washington law to resolve the issue. Washington law required an intention to abandon in order to discontinue a nonconforming use.


OUTCOME: Decision of the superior court was reversed and the case was remanded to respondent commission for consideration of whether the evidence supported the finding that the land occupiers did not intend to abandon the nonconforming use of the mobile home park site.

State v. Hamilton


No. 23890-0-II, Consolidated with No. 24011-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 50



January 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied April 2, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Wash. LEXIS 229. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 717.
Habeas corpus proceeding at Hamilton v. Pacholke, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 9999 (W.D. Wash., Jan. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 97-1-02412-1. Date filed: 10/08/1998. Judge signing: Hon. Rosanne N. Buckner.
State v. Hamilton, 104 Wn. App. 1008, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 717 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) that convicted them of first degree murder, robbery, and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were convicted of first degree murder, kidnapping, and robbery; they appealed, and the court affirmed. Use of appellant two's confession did not violate appellant one's confrontation clause rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI, because his name was redacted. The prosecutor's reference to this confession in closing was intended to buttress a witness's credibility, not to implicate appellant one, and was harmless because other evidence was more probative of his guilt. That appellant one was shackled during the trial was not error, and did not prejudice him, as the jury was prevented from seeing this. The state had no duty to preserve the car in which the victim was killed, as it had no reason to believe it contained exculpatory evidence and appellants' claim that it did was speculative. The state's failure to timely make a witness's identity available was not caused by bad faith, and the trial court cured any prejudice by allowing appellants a continuance and requiring the state to make the witness available for interview. Appellant one failed to objection to the trial court's determination of his sentence, so he waived his right to contest the sentence on appeal.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Redacting reference to appellant one in appellant two's confession cured any confrontation clause violation as to the former; shackling appellant one during trial did not prejudice him, as the jury did not see this; the state's untimely disclosure of identity and location of its witness did not prejudice appellants; the state did not have a duty to preserve the vehicle in which the murder victim was killed.

State v. Imbiorski


No. 24670-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 61



January 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 721.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Jefferson County. Docket No: 98-1-00154-8. Date filed: 05/06/1999. Judge signing: Hon. William E. Howard.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for second degree unlawful possession of a firearm from the Superior Court of Jefferson County (Washington).


OVERVIEW: At the end of the evidence, the trial court instructed the jury. It did not include "knowing possession of a firearm" as an element in the "to convict" instruction. The jury returned a verdict of guilty. On appeal the court ordered a new trial rather than dismiss with prejudice. Defendant owned the house in which the guns were found. He had lived in the house for more than two years. The guns were kept in plain sight in the gun cabinet. Neither the guns nor the cabinet were locked. Defendant was in the home at the time of the charged possession. Based on these facts, a jury could reasonably have inferred he was in possession of the guns at that time. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts. Defendant's proposed instruction, implying that when two people lived together, only one of them could own and possess firearms found in the house was a misstatement of the law. The occupants of a house could jointly own or possess its contents. Defining "constructive possession" as no actual physical possession, but dominion and control of an item which could be immediately exercised, was an accurate statement of the law.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed and remanded for new trial because an essential element, "knowing possession of a firearm," was missing from the "to convict" jury instruction. It could have been reasonably inferred that defendant was in possession of the firearms, because, in addition to having access to them and being in close proximity to them, he was an owner and possessor of the premises on which the firearms were found.

State v. Fisher


No. 18379-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


104 Wn. App. 772; 17 P.3d 1200; 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 37



January 9, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted July 10, 2001, Reported at: 144 Wn.2d 1002, 29 P.3d 718, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 497. Reported in Table Case Format at: 104 Wn. App. 1006, 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 708. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published February 1, 2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her conviction for possession of methamphetamine, marijuana, and drug paraphernalia by the Superior Court Walla Walla County (Washington) after her motion to suppress evidence found in her purse pursuant to a bench warrant issued while she was free awaiting sentencing was denied.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to possession and delivery of methamphetamine and was released on bail. While awaiting sentencing, the trial court issued a bench warrant for appellant's arrest based on the prosecutor's affidavit that she had been spending a lot of time with a known drug user. While executing the bench warrant, police searched appellant's purse and found controlled substances and paraphernalia. Appellant's motion to suppress was denied and she was convicted for possession of methamphetamine, marijuana, and drug paraphernalia. The court affirmed. Because appellant had been adjudicated guilty of a felony and had been released pending sentencing, the trial court could authorize the bench warrant based upon a well-founded suspicion, rather than probable cause, that a probation violation had occurred. Information from appellant's child's grandmother and officers, one of which reported another probationer's information, taken together provided the well-founded suspicion. An alleged statement that someone "had a surprise for" appellant in regard to the contents of her purse, was hearsay, in that appellant sought to prove by it that the speaker had placed the drugs there.


OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed. As appellant had been found guilty of a felony and been released pending sentencing, she had a diminished right to privacy and the trial court could issue a bench warrant based on well-founded suspicion, taken from information provided by three individuals, rather than on probable cause.

State v. Thomas


No. 24962-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


103 Wn. App. 800; 14 P.3d 854; 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2544



December 21, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Answer Denied June 5, 2001, Reported at: 143 Wn.2d 1022, 29 P.3d 719, 2001 Wash. LEXIS 415.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of leading organized crime and conspiracy to deliver marijuana, entered by the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington).


OVERVIEW: Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.903 repealed certain portions of the Criminal Profiteering Act so that they were not in effect when defendant committed the acts leading to the charge of leading organized crime under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.010(14)(p) (1995), former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.010(15) (1995), and Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.060. The attempt by the legislature to continue the Criminal Profiteering Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9A.82, by repealing Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.903 was unconstitutional because it violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 19 by not expressing the subject in the title, and embracing more than one subject. It was determinative that the title of the repealing legislation did not inform even the most intelligent, astute reader that the effect of the bill was to continue the life of the Criminal Profiteering Act and to continue to criminalize leading organized crime. Thus, the title did not fairly apprise the legislature and public of the substantive consequences of the legislation, and it violated the subject-in-title mandate of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part, affirmed in part. Legislation meant to retain previously repealed portions of Criminal Profiteering Act was unconstitutional. Conspiracy jury instructions were proper. There was sufficient evidence for conspiracy conviction. Defendant's counsel was competent. Because State dropped delivery of controlled substance charge before trial, related sentencing enhancement should not have been submitted to jury.

Phelps v. Franklin County


No. 18326-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2499



December 19, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 10, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. LEXIS 499. Motion for Reconsideration Denied January 12, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 76.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: FRANKLIN. Docket No(s): 95-2-50421-6. Judge signing: PHILIP RAEKES. Date filed: March 23, 1999.
Phelps v. Franklin County, 103 Wn. App. 1050, 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 3165 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Franklin County (Washington) which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent county based on res judicata, release, and statute of limitations. Appellants' claim related to the state's decision to upgrade a highway which appellants claimed was inverse condemnation. A settlement was reached with the state on the issue several years previously.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, husband and wife, bought a mini-mart on a section of road which became affected when the state department of transportation upgraded the highway and limited access points to selected intersections. The state filed an eminent domain action. Pursuant to a settlement agreement, the state paid appellants who dismissed their appeal, and stipulated that they had no right to compensation. Two years later, appellant filed an action against respondent county for constructive reverse condemnation. The appellate court affirmed the granting of summary judgment to respondent. Due to the earlier action, issue preclusion, not res judicata, applied. There was a final judgment on the merits, that there was no taking and no right to compensation. The facts and issues constituting appellants' claims against respondent county were identical, except that the term inverse condemnation was not used in the prior complaint. Thus, appellants' claim was precluded. The three-year statute of limitations under the Administrative Procedure Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 47.52.195, did not apply as appellants had no administrative cause of action against respondent county.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was affirmed because issue preclusion applied as appellants fully litigated the issue of whether the placement of highway access constituted a taking of his property rights or value and whether he was entitled to compensation. Appellants did not have an administrative cause of action, thus, the three-year statute of limitations did not apply. Appellants' remaining issues were not preserved for appeal.

State v. Labor Ready


No. 18824-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


103 Wn. App. 775; 14 P.3d 828; 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2504; 169 L.R.R.M. 2052



December 19, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals January 11, 2001.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Amending Court's Opinion January 11, 2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington), which granted respondent corporation's motion for dismissal on charge of violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 49.44.100, for hiring outside of the state during a lockout. The trial court declared the law unconstitutional as it violated the supremacy clause's preemption principles.


OVERVIEW: Respondent corporation was charged with violating Wash. Rev. Code § 49.44.100, for allegedly recruiting or securing employment of out-of-state workers to work at its plant during a lockout. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the complaint. Section 49.44.100 was unconstitutional as it violated the supremacy clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2, because it was federally preempted by the National Labor Relations Act (NLRA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 151 et seq. By curtailing an employer's right to hire replacement workers, § 49.44.100 attempted to regulate conduct that was intended to be left unregulated. Such restrictions were prohibited under the Machinist doctrine. Further, neither preserving industrial jobs for state residents nor preventing violence were express policy considerations of § 49.44.100. Although appellant State had an interest in preventing violence and maintaining employment for its residents, §49.44.100 by its plain language did not expressly provide for these interests. Moreover, even with this statute in place, employers could still hire out-of-state replacement workers themselves. Thus, the State interest exception did not apply.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the trial court did not err when deciding that the strikebreaker law was unenforceable as barred by federal preemption, as it involved an impermissible extension of state regulation into areas that had been left under the control of free play of economic forces. Further, it did not meet any of the exceptions to forestall preemption.

In re Custody of Nunn


No. 46015-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


103 Wn. App. 871; 14 P.3d 175; 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2496



December 18, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Denying Motions January 26, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Wash. App. LEXIS 162.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed an appeal of an order by the Superior Court of King County, Washington, that granted custody of her son to his paternal aunt, after the child's father, with whom appellant had shared joint custody, died.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother shared joint legal custody of her son with her ex-husband. When the child's father died, respondent, the decedent's sister and the child's paternal aunt, filed for and was awarded nonparental custody of the child. Appellant filed an appeal. The appellate court found that the trial court improperly addressed the issue of parental unfitness. Under the Wash. Rev. Stat. § 26.10.030, the allegation of parental unfitness should have been addressed as a threshold jurisdictional issue as early in the nonparental custody proceeding as practicable. The appellate court found that not only did the court delay to the detriment of both the mother and son, but that the proof of unfitness was insufficient to support the court's order, whether the standard was clear, cogent, convincing or compelling or by a preponderance of the evidence. There court concluded from the evidence in this record that appellant lost custody of her child because she tried to defend the integrity of her family unit against state intervention that was unfounded in the first place because it was based on a petition containing allegations of parental unfitness that ultimately proved to be false.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the custody order and remanded for dismissal of respondent's custody petition, for prompt return of the child to appellant's care, and for determination and award of attorney fees to appellant, finding that an otherwise fit parent could not be found unfit because she chose to fight a nonparental custody petition, and openly expressed her dislike and distrust of those who brought and supported it.

State v. Hendricks


No. 25159-1-II (linked), No. 24283-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


103 Wn. App. 728; 14 P.3d 811; 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2486



December 15, 2000, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants claimed the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) erred in calculating their sentences. They argued that their adult offender scores should not have included points for their prior juvenile convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants claimed their adult offender scores should not have included points for juvenile convictions. In 1997, the legislature amended Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030 to include all prior juvenile adjudications. Prior to 1997, appellants' juvenile convictions automatically washed out when calculating an adult offender score. The legislature specifically provided for retroactivity of a 2000 amendment to clarify an ambiguity present in the earlier revisions to the Sentencing Reform Act (SRA). The relevant version of the SRA to be applied in imposing a sentence was the law in effect when the current offense was committed. Sentencing court properly counted juvenile convictions when calculating adult offender scores. Appellants did not have a vested right to exclusion of juvenile convictions from adult criminal history. Use of juvenile convictions did not violate due process or ex post facto principles. Juvenile convictions did not have to be excluded based on bargains reached in juvenile pleas.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Use of juvenile convictions for calculating adult offender scores did not violate ex post facto principles or due process. Decision as to whether a prior conviction was to be included in an offender score was determined by law in effect when the current offense was committed.
